Report on the results of the parallel controls carried out in 2005 on the administration of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Opening Word
The submitted material informs about the progress and results of parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of value added tax administration and the use of the VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so the revenue from value added tax affects not only the national budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were aimed in particular at checking the tax authorities' procedures for verifying the amount of value added tax paid on commercial transactions between Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system has enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of VAT payers in the Member States of the European Union and on the commercial transactions carried out by them.
The mismatch between the VIES data and the data in the VAT return submitted by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and allow the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefits of the parallel controls were not only in the exchange of information on the procedure of the tax or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular in the examination of the use of the VIES system in the control of the application of the right to exemption from value added tax in intra-community transactions.
The lessons learned from the implementation of parallel controls contribute to the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of further parallel controls in cooperation with the control institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the administration of value added tax for the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic) concluded on 12 September 2005 the Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activities.
The object of the contract was cooperation in parallel audits “Value Added Tax Administration”, included in the audit plan of the SAO CR for 2005 under No. 05/19 and “Control of the tax authorities’ procedure for the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU member countries”, included in the audit plan of the SAO SR under No. 22/2005.
The control actions carried out in parallel had the character of a coordinated control.
The result of the joint coordinated inspection was processed within the meaning of the European Implementing Regulation No 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the contract concluded and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated inspection was to verify selected cases of supply and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Slovak Republic).
Both parties contractually undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the electronic system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on received and sent requests to verify commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the audit was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited bodies were the Ministry of Finance and 12 financial offices: the Financial Office in Mladá Boleslav, the Financial Office in Kolín, the Financial Office in Teplice, the Financial Office in Karlovy Vary, the Financial Office in Tábor, the Financial Office in Brno III, the Financial Office in Znojmo, the Financial Office in Zlín, the Financial Office in Šumperk, the Financial Office in Ostrava I, the Financial Office for Prague 7 and the Financial Office for Prague 9.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the Expoziturami SAO of the Slovak Republic Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: Tax Office of Bratislava I, Tax Office of Komárno, Tax Office of Trenčín, Tax Office of Prievidza, Tax Office of Zvolen, Tax Office of Dolný Kubín, Tax Office of Košice II, Tax Office of Košice V and Tax Office of Michalovce.
Objective of controls:
The aim of the parallel audits was to examine the procedure of the financial and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and Slovakia into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter "EU") and to examine the use of the electronic information system VIES, in particular when checking the application of the VAT exemption.
The audited coordinated inspection period covered the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions An electronic VIES system is in place in EU Member States to allow tax authorities to check whether the supplier has been authorised to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and to check in the country of destination whether the purchaser has duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES system is not centralised within the EU, with each Member State developing its own system.
The audit found differences in national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the following areas:
The recapitulative statements indicate the values of deliveries to other EU Member States, the values of services provided are not included in the recapitulative statements.
Data from recapitulative statements submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States listed in VAT returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In SR, data from recapitulative statements filed by Slovak payers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of SR (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and services to other EU Member States on separate rows of VAT returns, which makes it possible to compare the values stated in the recapitulative statements with the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and to identify their possible differences.
In the SR, the values of goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are shown in aggregate on the common line of the VAT return.
Consequently, in the SR, the system does not allow the automatic identification of differences between the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of the value of supplies of goods in VAT returns makes it possible to use the results of data comparisons when checking the VAT exemption of supplies of goods to the EU.
The delivered data from recapitulative statements submitted by payers in other EU Member States are processed into Customs and compared with the value of acquisition of goods stated by payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia in their VAT returns.
In the Slovak Republic, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities themselves decide which cases of differences to check.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of supplies and acquisitions of goods must be verified by the tax administrators and sends a list of these cases to the local tax authorities.
This ensures that, for the most important derogations, it will be verified whether the VAT on the acquisition of goods was correctly declared.
The audit also highlighted some problems in the VAT administration system, complications caused by different reporting of intra-Community transactions (i.e. supplies and acquisitions of goods made by payers from different EU Member States):
Aggregate reports are submitted in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum period for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
The reduction of the period for which recapitulative statements are submitted to one month, together with the shortening of the processing time, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
Tax authorities would thus be able to check more effectively whether the VAT on intra-community acquisitions was correctly declared.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax period (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer has declared identical values for the supply of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return.
Differences between the values of deliveries of goods declared by EU payers and the values of acquisitions of goods declared by Czech and Slovak payers were due, among other things, to different reporting of data on intra-Community delivery and acquisitions in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in the recapitulative statements, or the reporting of intra-community supplies in the supplier's recapitulative statement in a quarter other than the intra-community acquisitions in the acquirer's VAT return.
Unifying the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the tax administrations of the Member States more effective.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also focused on the examination of selected intra-community transactions carried out between the two countries.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined where there were doubts about their completion or suspicion of VAT evasion.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic found the following facts:
tax subjects have declared in their VAT returns, for the purpose of unduly obtaining excess VAT, the execution of intra-Community transactions which were not actually carried out;
tax subjects reported intra-community supplies in the context of carousel shops where there was a deliberate multiple decrease in the value of supplies in order to draw excess VAT deductions;
suppliers declared in their VAT returns and recapitulative statements the intra-Community supply of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the goods acquired;
Suppliers made intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to taxable persons not registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
Suppliers declared intra-community supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than the intra-community acquisitions declared by the acquirers, and in some cases VAT was declared incorrectly.
The findings of the audit operation showed that the VIES system provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-community transactions.
In particular, tax administrations should pay particular attention to the rigorous verification of differences between data reported by VAT payers and VIES data and the use of all information in tax procedures.
The issue of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic and Slovakia to the EU
Value added tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and Slovakia became members of the EU.
Internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU have been abolished since EU accession.
Until 30.4.2004, the VAT administrator was the competent tax or tax office, with the exception of the import of goods and occasional bus transport in the Czech Republic, where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 235/2004 Coll."), or Act No. 222/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 222/2004 Coll."), the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU member countries was transferred from the customs authorities to the tax or tax authorities.
The supply of goods in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of § 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
A supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is a supply of goods that have actually been shipped or transported to another EU Member State.
According to the provisions of § 64 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., this is an exempt taxable transaction with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are supplied to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
In the Slovak Republic, according to the provisions of § 8 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z., a supply of tangible property is considered to be a supply of goods where there is a change in the right of ownership.
A transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the territory of the country to another Member State shall be regarded as a supply of goods if those goods are dispatched or transported by that person, or on his behalf, to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Under Paragraph 43 of Law No 222/2004, the supply of goods from the national territory to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the person acquiring the goods is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
Purchase of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of § 16 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods that are dispatched or transported to the acquirer by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer purchases goods at the price without VAT and is obliged to declare VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of § 25 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., if he fulfils the conditions specified in § 73 of this Act, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
Purchase of goods in the territory of the country from another EU Member State in the Slovak Republic pursuant to the provisions of § 11 of Act No 222/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property dispatched or transported to the person acquiring the goods by or on behalf of the supplier or the person acquiring the goods to the territory of the country from another Member State.
Tax liability in the Slovak Republic is incurred by the payer when acquiring goods in the Czech Republic from another Member State in accordance with the provisions of § 20 of Act No 222/2004 Z.z.
The taxpayer may deduct VAT in accordance with the provisions of § 49 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. if the tax is applied by him on the acquisition of goods in the territory of another Member State in accordance with the provisions of §§ 11 and 11a of this Act.
In accordance with the provisions of § 17 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., or § 45 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., a trilateral transaction is a transaction concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States where the object of the transaction is the supply of the same goods between these three persons.
Intracommunal transactions are supplies and acquisitions of goods made between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are shown in the following table.
VIES
In order to control the exercise of the right to VAT exemption in intra-Community supplies of goods, a VAT information exchange system has been set up within the EU.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows the tax authorities of the EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and vice versa, whether the purchaser duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State is developing its own VIES system.
National systems operate on a common principle and are interconnected through a common EU communication network, the so-called CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected to an automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "ADIS"), in the Slovak Republic to the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems are used by the financial and tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and duties.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU country obtains information about tax entities that it would not be able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is the fight against tax evasion and tax losses.
Under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State establishes, within an internal organisational structure, a central unit for administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the management of VAT, the so-called CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance – the Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (hereinafter referred to as “MF CLO”) has been established, performs tasks arising from international cooperation.
The function of the Customs Office in the Slovak Republic is fulfilled by the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as ‘DG CLO’).
These units inter alia communicate with EU foreign administrations in particular in the areas of information exchange within the VIES system, spontaneous information and information exchange at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax inspections, verification of VAT identification numbers of persons registered in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to verify a particular intra-community transaction or to obtain additional information related to a particular tax entity, the tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via the Ministry of Customs or the Directorate of Customs.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use to determine VAT correctly.
Requests for information are mostly sent electronically between the CLOs of the EU Member States, using a standardised SCAC form.
Selected audit findings when verifying commercial transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was focused mainly on the examination of selected intra-community transactions carried out between the two states and on the level of use of information obtained through international cooperation by financial and tax authorities.
The SAO of the Czech Republic required the SAO of the Slovak Republic to examine in 30 cases commercial transactions between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The SAO of Slovakia requested the SAO of the Czech Republic to examine in 10 cases commercial transactions between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
Examination of intra-community transactions revealed, among other things:
o
The SAO of the Czech Republic asked the SAO of the Slovak Republic to verify the procedure of the tax administrator, who was sent a reply to the request for information.
The Slovak Tax Office, using the SCAC form, requested verification of the supply of goods (footwear) in the 3rd quarter of 2004 from a Slovak payer in the value of SKK 2,847,000.
The tax office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer stated the acquisition of goods of this value only in the additional VAT declaration and the same goods were delivered back to Slovak tax entities in the value of CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004.
On the basis of the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the locally competent tax office granted the Slovak supplier a full right to excess VAT deduction arising, inter alia, from this supply.
This tax office did not provide information about the suspicion of re-export to the tax authorities of the locally competent buyers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
This will trigger further investigation of commercial activities in relation to possible carousel fraud.
o
The Czech tax administrator asked through the SCAC form to verify the delivery of a technology line to Slovakia worth CZK 4,850,000 in the second quarter of 2004.
The tax proceedings carried out in Slovakia revealed that only part of the technology line was delivered, components worth CZK 3,395,000 were not delivered.
The SAO of Slovakia, when examining this case, found that the VAT on the taxable transaction was declared by a Slovak tax entity for the amount of CZK 4,850,000 in the VAT return (hereinafter "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO of the Czech Republic also found that the Czech payer reported an excess VAT deduction in the amount of CZK 655,000 in its VAT receipt for that quarter, which was created by the application of a VAT deduction from the purchase of this technology line from another domestic payer.
Based on the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak taxpayer had created a business relationship for the purpose of unduly obtaining an excess VAT deduction, disputed the realisation of the taxable transaction and did not recognise part of the right to deduct the tax amounting to CZK 647,000.
o
In 2004, the Slovak tax administrator, using the SCAC form, requested verification of the supply of goods (copying machines) to the Czech payer in the amount of SKK 24 246 thousand made in December 2002.
These goods were purchased by a Slovak payer in November 2002 in Slovakia from another tax entity in the value of SKK 29 667 thousand and subsequently sold to a Czech payer.
The Slovak taxpayer applied an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
In a tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not file a DAP for the 4th quarter of 2002 or for the following period.
The SAO of Slovakia found that the Slovak tax administrator did not recognise the right to an excess deduction of CZK 5,541,000 based on the results of the tax audit. Sk invoked in the DAP for the month of 11/2002 and established a tax liability of SKK 1 750 000.
At the same time, that taxpayer was not granted an exemption from VAT in respect of the export of goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from MF Customs to verify the value of the purchased goods for the 3rd quarter of 2004.
According to the VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods (paint thinner) from SR in the value of 3 767 thousand SKK.
This taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, did not file a DAP and was charged VAT in the amount of CZK 0 ex officio for the months 7 to 12/2004.
The Czech tax administrator asked through the SCAC form to verify whether deliveries of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic took place, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In reply, the Slovak Tax Office sent a copy of the invoice, the bill of lading and a request for payment of the invoice.
The SAO of Slovakia found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with the right to deduct VAT on this supply.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that the Czech tax administrator assessed the response to the request for information received from the Slovak Republic as evidence that the company had purchased goods from another EU Member State.
On the basis of further investigation, the tax office in the Czech Republic will ask the superior authority to review the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (particle board products) to, among others, an American company which deposited these goods in the Czech Republic in a free customs zone.
The operator of that free zone was named on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, a US company purchased from a Slovak payer particle board tiles worth USD 57 600 (at a unit price of USD 100 per piece), which it placed in a free customs zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company, amounting to USD 14 400 (unit price of USD 25 each) and the goods were re-exported to the Slovak Republic.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the area of the free customs zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax inspections of individual tax periods of 2004 and 2005 at the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
The verification of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech locally competent tax authorities using several SCAC forms.
Individual responses gradually created an image of the shops and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the carousel shops.
The SAO of the Czech Republic in cooperation with the SAO of the Slovak Republic found that in these business relations there was a deliberate multiple decrease in the value of goods.
On the basis of the information received, the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic concluded that the carousel trade in question is free price formation (i.e. the import of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies in the chain between the importer and the exporter) which is not in breach of the VAT Act.
Under the current legislation, the payment of excess VAT to export companies cannot be prevented as they fulfil all the conditions of the law to exempt supplies from VAT.
o
The Czech payer's VAT registration was cancelled on 12 July 2005.
On 27 October 2005, this entity became a taxpayer again on the basis of a voluntarily submitted application for VAT registration.
The Czech taxpayer entered into the DAP for the month of 8/2005 (i.e. the period when he was not a VAT payer) the value of the acquisition of goods (printing press) from the Slovak Republic in the amount of CZK 1,174,000 and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to a supply of goods from a Slovak payer in the amount of SKK 1,530,000, which the Slovak payer listed in the DAP as a supply of goods to another EU Member State with the right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify this supply using the SCAC form, because the Slovak supplier did not prove how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that the Czech payer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and does not reside at the address specified in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the local tax administrator in order to verify the data.
o
The Slovak payer included in the recapitulative statement for the 3rd quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods in the value of CZK 956,000. To a tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was marked as incorrect by the VIES system.
A verification in the database of payers revealed that such a TIN was never assigned in the Czech Republic.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic, it was not the delivery of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it is registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax authority requested to verify these facts using the SCAC form.
The SAO of the Czech Republic inquired at the local tax authority in the Czech Republic and found that the tax entity listed on the invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not declare the tax on received services from the Slovak entity and did not declare the tax on the acquisition of goods.
Neither a local investigation nor a tax inspection was carried out on the Czech entity, its current whereabouts are unknown.
On the basis of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity became a VAT payer by law by accepting the service.
The Slovak tax entity will be audited for the first to fourth quarters of 2004.
o
The Slovak payer included in the recapitulative statement for the 3rd quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods in the value of CZK 1,055,000. To the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not a matter of delivering goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but of providing services.
The Slovak tax authority requested to verify these facts using the SCAC form.
The SAO of the Czech Republic inquired with the local tax authority in the Czech Republic that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the delivery and a local investigation was carried out to verify the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
On the basis of this on-the-spot investigation, it was found that this case was not really a purchase of goods, but a purchase of services, which was also declared by the Czech entity in the regular DAP.
The tax office also found that the Czech entity did not pay the correct amount of VAT for the tax period of the 3rd quarter of 2004 as a result of a bad procedure in the calculation of VAT.
The taxpayer shall submit an additional DAP.
The SAO, when questioned by the local tax office, found that the Slovak payer had misstated the provision of the service in the recapitulative statement and would be subject to a tax audit for the first to fourth quarters of 2004.
o
The Czech tax entity has voluntarily registered as a VAT payer since 10 March 2004.
For the first quarter of 2004, it filed a DAP with a high turnover in both input and output.
The local tax administrator initiated tax proceedings, the entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, therefore due to the suspicion of involvement in the carousel business he was assessed VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
No further DAP has been filed by this payer.
As a result of his failure to comply with his legal obligations, his VAT registration was cancelled on 4.1.2005.
According to data from the VIES system, this entity should have purchased goods in the value of SKK 7,846,000 from the Slovak payer in the 3rd and 4th quarter of 2004.
In order to verify the execution of these transactions, the Czech tax administrator sent two requests for information to SR.
The SAO inquired at the local tax office and found that the managing director of the Czech company denied the execution of the audited transactions and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
The intra-community supply to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was questioned on the basis of the tax procedure carried out in Slovakia.
The payer will not be entitled to VAT exemption and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
o
According to the VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods (working clothes) from the Slovak Republic in the first quarter of 2005 with a total value of SKK 39,970,000.
This quarter, the Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only in the DAP for the month of 3/2005, in the value of CZK 11,292,000.
The locally competent tax authority carried out a local investigation of the entity in order to verify the data in this DAP.
As the company did not submit any documents or otherwise substantiate the implementation of taxable transactions, the tax administrator charged it VAT of CZK 0 on 9 June 2005.
In view of the doubts about the acquisition of the goods, the tax authority sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic in May 2005.
According to the reply to the requests for information, the tax administrator in the Slovak Republic had doubts about the realisation of the business cases as well as about the realisation of the payment.
The SAO of Slovakia was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent a suggestion to the Czech Customs Agency to conduct simultaneous audits with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated inspection in the Czech Republic, the locally competent tax administrator carried out further investigations concerning the Czech subject and at the same time an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was being carried out.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of being involved in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (work clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered them back to SR payer No. 4 (see diagram No. 2).
(a)
Czech payer No. 2 should have purchased goods (work clothes) worth CZK 4,847,000 from Slovak payer No. 1 in the 4th quarter of 2004 and goods worth CZK 17,050,000 in the 1st quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the locally competent tax administrator sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic on 25 May 2005.
In reply, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the realisation of the business cases as well as the realisation of the payment.
On June 8, 2005, a request for information was received at the Ministry of Customs of the Slovak Republic concerning goods worth SKK 16,575,000, which were to be delivered in December 2004 by the Slovak payer No. 1 to the Czech payer No. 2.
The Slovak side requested to verify whether the Czech payer 2 actually received the goods, declared them in the DAP and paid the VAT.
The official record drawn up by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech payer no. 2 has not been residing at an address registered in the Commercial Register for some time.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax period, he filed a DAP for a quarterly tax period.
In view of this, the Czech tax authority was unable to assess the VAT.
Taxable transaction between Slovak payer No. 1 and Czech payer No. 2 mentioned in the application in the amount of CZK 16,575,000. This could not be verified in the light of the above.
The Czech tax authority suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel trade in order to draw an excess VAT deduction.
(B)
Czech payer No. 3, dealing with the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed a DAP for the tax period of months 1 and 2/2005, in which he declared the delivery of goods (work clothes) to Slovak payer No. 4 in a total value of CZK 21,935 thousand.
These work clothes should have been purchased by the Czech payer No 3 from the Czech payer No 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, the main purpose of which was to verify whether the Slovak payer No. 4 purchased goods worth CZK 1,025,000 from the Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 and CZK 21,935,000 in the first quarter of 2005.
The reply to this request for information received from SR showed that in the DAP for the month of 12/2004, the Slovak payer No 4 indicated a zero value for the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for the months 1 and 2/2005 indicated a value for the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State of only SKK 1 193.
The Slovak payer No 4 did not respond to the invitation to submit tax documents for the tax period of 10/2004 to 3/2005.
A local investigation carried out in SR revealed that the company was not at the address indicated in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer fulfils all the characteristics of a so-called "lost company" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO of Slovakia was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent a suggestion to the Czech Tax Office to conduct simultaneous audits with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or refute the existence of the goods.
VAT will be calculated according to the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also being handled by the Czech Police.
Progress of control action
As part of the preparation of parallel audits, a coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO of the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO of the Slovak Republic took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants of this meeting took note of the VAT legislation in both countries and the integration of the VIES electronic system into the national databases.
The outcome of the meeting was to specify the scope of cooperation and to establish the conditions for the selection of control samples.
The two parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: (b) verification of data on intra-community acquisitions listed in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from the summary reports (hereinafter referred to as “SH”) of payers from the Slovak Republic contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; (c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic on executed business transactions.
Furthermore, it was agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out in relation to the volume of intra-community deliveries between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and Slovakia using the SCAC form.
5.1 Intracommunitary transactions
The procedure of information processing by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia for intra-Community delivery and acquisition of goods is illustrated in the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intracommunitary delivery
If the VAT payer makes an intra-community delivery, he is obliged to submit SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides in the SH summary information on his/her deliveries of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to enter in the SH the value of goods that were tax exempt and delivered from the territory of the country to other EU Member States for the period of the calendar quarter.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always given in the SH in Czech or Slovak currency, broken down by individual tax entities with an indication of their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Data on services shall not be included in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds out that he has given incorrect data in the SH, he is obliged to file a subsequent SH.
If the payer in SR finds that the data given in the SH were incomplete or incorrect, he shall file a corrective SH before the deadline for filing the SH, after the expiry of this deadline he shall file an additional SH.
The VIES system allows the exchange of information on VAT registered payers' registration data in EU Member States.
Tax payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia can verify whether the VAT number of the relevant acquirer is registered in the EU Member State.
The data from the submitted SH are grouped into MF CLO or DR CLO by the VIES system according to the individual VAT number of the acquirer.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each VAT number of the acquirer and the code of the method of filling from all its Czech and Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files, are created.
Data from files L1QDs shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia (from the L1QD files) is given in the following table.
If the VIES in another Member State detects erroneous acquirer's TIN in the L1QD files sent, it generates an O_MCTL message containing all the erroneous TIN numbers indicating the type of error.
This report is then sent to the MF CLO, or to the CDC CLO.
The O_MCTL message can contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect VAT number, the VAT number is not registered in the country or has never been allocated, the acquirer with a specific VAT number was not a VAT payer in the given quarter, the registration for the VAT of the acquirer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, MF CLO transmits data from received O_MCTL reports to financial authorities.
If the incorrect VAT number of an EU payer is used in any of the sent lines of the SH or subsequent SH, the so-called "VAT ID Doubt Notice" is generated at the relevant tax office by the ADIS system.
The tax office checks whether delivery to a VAT registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and records the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, DR CLO processes all O_MCTL messages in the VIES system and sends them electronically to the local tax authorities together with the identification of the tax payers who have reported an incorrect VAT number in their SH.
Subsequently, the tax authorities invite the payer to submit an additional SH and the indication of valid VAT numbers, respectively the tax office will check the delivery of goods with the relevant payer when declaring an invalid VAT number in the submitted SH.
Data on the number of erroneous TINs related to intra-community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are given in the following table.
Of the total number of 41,728 VAT numbers of Czech payers listed in the Slovak Payers' Tax Register in the period from the 2nd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005, 929 were erroneous VAT numbers, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the total number of 62 997 VAT numbers of Slovak payers listed in the Czech payers' tax return during the same period, 416 were incorrect VAT numbers, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intra-community transactions made between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer erroneous VAT numbers in their SH than Slovak VAT payers.
During the examination of the activities of the financial and tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not in all cases provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities.
E.g.:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the tax entity's registration in the 4th quarter of 2004 on the request of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the O_MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer's registration in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the termination of the registration took place only on 1.1.2005.
- The SAO of the Slovak Republic also found that 6 tax entities filed tax returns with the wrong tax exempt number, but the O_MCTL reports did not contain this tax exempt number.
In SR, the submitted SHs are converted into electronic form at the tax offices and the data from them are sent to the DG CLO.
Following the subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, the DCI sends to the relevant tax authorities the so-called breakdowns of errors in the SH submitted by the tax entities for the relevant quarters.
The SAO of Slovakia compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH as of 26 July 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the audit) and as of 2 February 2006 (i.e. data processed after the completion of the audit).
The following table provides a comparison of the data.
From the above data it can be seen that the SAO SR audit had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with an incorrect VAT number (on average by 199 SH per quarter) but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-community deliveries indicated by the payer in the respective DAP rows is compared with the value of intra-community deliveries indicated by the payer in the quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data collected to determine the tax liability.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that the audited financial authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values given in SH and DAP in these cases amounted to CZK 537,231,000.
From the 3rd quarter of 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values given in SH and DAP up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-community deliveries according to SH as a match and to set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-community deliveries per quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a non-negligible amount, so tax administrators should not set the SH and DAP compliance in these cases without explaining the causes of the differences.
For example, the tax administrator set the match without verification in the case of a value difference of CZK 1,561,000.
The verification of differences in the Czech Republic and Slovakia was complicated by the fact that SH for each calendar quarter was submitted by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
Tax administrators could not compare the values of intra-community supplies listed in these DAPs with SH values for taxpayers with a monthly tax period at the time of submission of DAPs for the first two months of the calendar quarter.
In these cases, the tax authorities became aware of any discrepancy between the DAP and SH data only at the time when the tax liability or excess VAT was assessed or refunded.
5.1.2 Intracommunal acquisition
The VIES system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intra-Community transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Purchase of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the delivered data from SH filed by payers from other EU Member States (L1QD delivered) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the acquisition value indicated by the Czech payers in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods reported by the payers in DAP should be in the range of the minimum and maximum converted value L1QD (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is less than L1min, a so-called authentication order is generated for the payer with the most significant irregularities.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods alert problematic tax entities and are transmitted to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders concerning audited financial offices in the Czech Republic is shown in the following table.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that in 33 cases the audited tax authorities did not check for irregularities in the values of intra-community acquisitions, which were indicated by the received verification orders.
The total difference between the values given in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases amounted to at least CZK 148,319,000.
The SAO of the Czech Republic selected 533 files of tax entities for auditing, for which audited tax authorities received a verification order from the Ministry of Customs.
The audit found the following most common causes of differences between the values stated in the DAP of the acquirer and in the SH of the supplier: on the side of the acquirer (Czech payer) in 263 cases the acquirer did not declare the acquisition of goods in the regular DAP, in 93 cases the payer declared the acquisition of goods in a tax period other than that in which it was obliged to declare the tax, in 6 cases the acquirer entered the value of the acquired goods in the incorrect DAP line, on the side of the supplier (EU payer) in 88 cases the payer included the values in their SHSH in other cases included in the value of goods in the CR in 16 cases.
On the side of Slovak payers, the most frequent erroneous inclusion of the value of the services provided in the SH.
54 such cases were identified at the audited financial offices.
For example, during the investigation of the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 arose from the fact that the Slovak payer introduced into the SH for the first quarter of 2005 the provision of services (construction works and supplies of goods including assembly in the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of received advances in the SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers reported in the SH received advances from Czech payers, as a result of which an order was generated to verify the difference in the amount of CZK 3,580,000.
Orders to verify goods acquired are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently a change in the SH data in the EU Member States, such as a change in the buyer of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since the VIES system does not automatically draw attention to these changes, the locally competent tax authority of the person acquiring the goods may not be aware, without any other initiative, of the facts relevant to the correct determination of the tax liability on the goods acquired, and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
The audit of the SAO of the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer stated in the SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 the value of the delivery of goods for the Czech payer in the amount of 1 504 thousand SKK.
On 1 February 2005, the Tax Office of the Czech payer sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, as the Czech payer declared the acquisition of goods only in the amount of CZK 425,000.
On the basis of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer filed an additional SH on 1 March 2005 in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the supply for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand. Sk and increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from the amount of CZK 194,000. Sk to the value of 1 160 thousand. Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported in their SH for the second quarter of 2004 intra-community delivery to payers from the Czech Republic in the total amount of 10,240 thousand SKK (i.e. 8,183 thousand CZK).
However, Czech acquirers did not report intra-community acquisition in the DAP.
Based on the international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were in all cases delivered to another Czech payer, which was not mentioned in the SH filed by Slovak payers.
During the first quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased the value of intra-community deliveries for this Czech payer by a total of SKK 10,240 thousand in the additional SH relating to the second quarter of 2004.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not doubt the accuracy of the data in the submitted DAP for the second quarter of 2004, even if the actual acquirer did not comply with the obligation to declare intra-community acquisitions for this quarter.
The SAO of the Czech Republic found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the aforementioned Czech payer was additionally assessed for VAT in the amount of CZK 3,640,000 for tax periods 5 and 6/2004 and in the amount of CZK 3,305,000 for goods acquired in these periods for the third quarter of 2004.
It can be seen from the above that tax administrations had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences arising from errors in the acquirer's DAP, but also differences due to different reporting of intra-Community supply and acquisition data in different EU Member States.
Unifying the conditions for reporting such data would lead to more effective control activities of tax administrations.
Purchase of goods in SR
In SR, the APV DIS system allows comparing the data on the value of acquired goods obtained through the VIES system from other EU Member States with the data provided in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
The method by which the data are compared is called the ‘MIN-MAX method’.
Using this method, the values of deliveries listed in the HS of payers from other EU Member States are converted at the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the relevant quarter.
The MIN-MAX interval is created, which is used for comparison with the values of acquisitions of goods listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DG CLO will send the tax authorities information on the values of intra-community acquisitions listed in the DAP and the values of EU supplies in the VIES system.
The tax administrator decides which VAT registered persons will be checked for the difference, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
Based on the data provided by the SAO, the SAO selected 57 files of Slovak acquirers of goods from audited tax offices, of which 25 payers acquired goods from the Czech Republic, where the highest differences were found between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and the values declared in the DAP.
The audit performed by the SAO of Slovakia confirmed that the tax administrators did not thoroughly check the differences obtained by the MIN-MAX method and thus did not check the accuracy of the data stated in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
As part of the audit, the SAO asked tax authorities to conduct 47 local investigations of specific tax entities.
During the audit of the SAO SR at the tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies, for which the VIES system showed significant differences in MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU Member States, the following facts were found, among others:
In the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not provide the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The Tax Office found that a company from the Czech Republic mistakenly reported the VAT number of this payer in the SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while goods worth CZK 19,184,000 were actually delivered to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, in the 4th quarter of 2004 the Slovak company was to purchase goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria with a value of MIN 682 692 thousand Sk and MAX 715 105 thousand Sk.
This company filed DAP for the periods in which it stated the value of acquisitions of goods from the EU at only SKK 480 599 thousand.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation and found that the taxpayer purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not specify intra-community deliveries by invoice date, but by delivery date.
Due to other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the tax administrator will request verification of the value of the supplied goods through SCAC forms.
The acquisition of goods from EU member countries in the 4th quarter of 2004 was not mentioned by the Slovak payer in the DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer should have purchased goods worth MIN 11 286 thousand and MAX 11 845 thousand.
The Tax Office carried out a local investigation, which revealed that the tax entity had not purchased any goods from EU Member States in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The SAO recommended that the tax office ask for verification of supplies of goods from EU member countries using the SCAC form.
In the VIES system, the supply of goods to a Slovak customer was reported in the value of MIN 557 thousand SKK and MAX 565 thousand SKK.
In the DAP for the tax period 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not declare any acquisition of goods.
A local investigation by the tax administrator found that the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier from the Czech Republic for materials consumed during the repair of the hydraulic loader on 10 December 2004.
The SAO recommended a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR in 16 cases the tax authorities did not terminate the local investigations.
In 10 cases, the SAO asked tax administrators to perform tax audits on tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax audits will be submitted by the tax authorities after their implementation to the SAO of Slovakia.
Examples include:
The Slovak acquirer did not mention in the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004 the acquisition of goods from EU member countries and for the tax period 10 to 12/2004 he declared no tax and claimed a refund of excess VAT in the total amount of SKK 1 236 thousand.
The tax administrator conducted a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity purchased goods from the Czech Republic worth EUR 683,000 (approx. SKK 27,080,000).
The goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer issued an invoice for the amount of EUR 683 thousand for the customer in the Russian Federation, which was not mentioned in the submitted DAP.
The tax administrator carries out a tax audit of the tax entity.
The difference between the acquisition data reported in the Slovak payer's DAP for the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005 and the data on deliveries reported by payers from the EU Member States in each quarter totalled SKK 4,800 thousand.
The tax office found that the taxpayer purchased goods from suppliers in the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold these goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by the single export declaration.
The acquisition of goods in the DAP was not mentioned by the tax entity, according to the statement of the company's manager, the goods were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine under the transit procedure.
The taxpayer did not submit any VAT records in the on-the-spot investigation.
A tax audit has been initiated on the payer.
5.2 International L3 Information Exchange
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by the locally competent tax administrators, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as the “GI”) or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as the “SPI”) relating to a particular tax entity or transaction through the Ministry of Customs or the Ministry of Finance, respectively.
DG CLO to another EU Member State. The aim of the ŽOI is, for example, to prove the execution of the given transaction within the framework of intra-community transactions, to verify a specific VAT number, etc.
In the case of SPI, this is the communication of information relevant to a tax authority in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the EIT was set at 3 months in Article 8 of that regulation.
The conditions for the admissibility of applications are governed by the Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15.11.2004, which stipulates that, unless the participating States agree otherwise, the GI must relate to commercial transactions of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
If the GI concerns a commercial transaction with a value of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to reply in view of its workload.
The following diagram illustrates the procedure of handling incoming RUs by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the internal time limits set for processing at each organizational level.
In SR, the time limit for the discharge of the GI by the tax authorities was set at 2 months in order to comply with the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
From 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005, MF CLO received a total of 29 GIs and 3 SPIs from the Slovak Republic.
Of the 29 GIs received, 26 (i.e. 89.7%) were discharged within the prescribed period of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) were discharged after that period.
In the same period, DG CLO from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 RUs and 7 SPIs.
Of the 71 GIs received, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were processed within the prescribed period of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were processed after this period (for the remaining 2 cases it was not possible to determine the period of execution from the submitted materials).
The following chart contains more detailed data on the processing time of RUIs received by MF CLO, respectively DR CLO.
The following table contains the reasons for sending the RU, as stated on the SCAC forms.
Conclusion
Compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT, as well as the use of the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States, in particular for checking the application of the VAT exemption, was examined on the basis of international cooperation.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine selected intra-community transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
An examination of the selected transactions revealed that, on the basis of an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries had uncovered cases of companies carrying out fictitious intra-community business transactions in order to obtain excess VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers did not declare the correct amount of VAT on the received supplies of goods.
The audit also found differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of both countries.
The audit also pointed to problems caused by different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions of goods in different EU Member States.
Unifying the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the tax administrations of the Member States more effective.
An examination of the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system revealed that the tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal authorisations.
Furthermore, it was found that the VIES system did not in all cases provide up-to-date information on the supply of goods and on the validity of the VAT registration of tax entities.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the audit, with the data processed after the completion of the audit.
Comparison of these data showed that the audit of the SAO SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with erroneously reported DINs, but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH.
In case of discrepancies in the reported data, the SAO asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or tax inspections.
The SAO of the Czech Republic did not have such an option under the applicable legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the audit work showed that the VIES system provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-community transactions.
Given that there remains scope for tax evasion in this area, increased attention needs to be paid to intra-community transactions in the VAT administration.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in the Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Opening Word
This information document gives an overview of the progress and results of the parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of value added tax and excise tax administration.
The cooperation between the SAIs of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement on control activities concluded in February 2004.
The theme of the parallel control actions was chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes contribute significantly to the revenues of the national budgets of both countries.
The construction of value added tax, allowing the refund of excess deductions, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duties, especially on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
In view of the need to address this issue comprehensively throughout the European Union, the VAT Working Group has been created by the supreme audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union, in which the supreme audit institutions of both countries are actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but especially in the joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax administration in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The experience and knowledge gained will be used in the framework of the planned controls of indirect taxes, aimed in particular at the involvement of the tax authorities of both states in the VIES system, which makes it possible to control the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the audit of the administration of value added tax and excise duties for the years 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Object of control:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the procedure of the tax administrator in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On 11 February 2004, the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) and the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) of the Slovak Republic (SAO SR) were signed. The object of the contract was cooperation in parallel audits "Value Added Tax and Excise Tax", included in the Audit Plan of the SAO for 2004 under No. 04/07 and "Audit of the Tax Administrators' Procedure for Administration, Control and Enforcement of Value Added Tax and Excise Taxes", included in the Audit Plan of the SAO SR under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted in exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract concluded and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
In the contract, both parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from tax entity files kept by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain when checking the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the respective state.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic"), the audit was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of South Bohemia, North-East Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited bodies were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected financial offices: the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 3, the Financial Office in České Budějovice, the Financial Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Financial Office in Hodonín, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Kroměříž, the Financial Office in Písek, the Financial Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Velký Meziříčí.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "SR") was carried out by the Tax and Customs Administration Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO Expoziturami SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax Office Bratislava for selected tax entities, Tax Office Bratislava III, Tax Office Trnava, Tax Office Pooh-chov, Tax Office Banská Bystrica I, Tax Office Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax Office Žilina I, Tax Office Žilina II, Tax Office Košice I and Tax Office Košice IV.
Objective of control
The aim of the audits was to verify the fulfilment of the duties of the tax and tax authorities and customs authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise duties with a focus on the collection of these taxes on imports and exports of goods and services.
The aim of the international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the relevant financial and tax offices.
The audited period covered the years 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
Within the framework of international cooperation, the SAO provided 22,206 items of the Single Customs Declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia from the Czech Customs Database and the SAO provided the SAO with 30,221 items of the JCD from the SR Customs Database.
Comparison of selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic was performed.
Out of 5,883 selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic, a total of 43% of the related JCD items were assigned.
Out of the 12 343 selected JCD items from the SR Customs Database, a total of 26 % of the related JCD items were allocated.
On the basis of the unassigned JCD items, the tax authorities selected files of tax entities, whose reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Based on the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia and the financial and tax authorities, the realization of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified on the territory of the second state.
The SAO and the SAO of Slovakia conducted a joint pilot inspection at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, during which both parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of the data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The audit did not find any deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine trade transactions between trading partners from both countries and has highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of control results
In the area of international cooperation, the SAO and the SAO scrutinized imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their parts, as well as other goods.
The SAO requested verification of the realisation of exports of goods declared for 40 JCD with a total statistical value of CZK 15,301,093 and the SAO requested verification of exports with a statistical value of CZK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic found, among other things, the following facts:
- commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic,
- errors in entering data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, the corresponding imports to the Slovak Republic have not been demonstrated.
In such cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of improper application of value added tax deductions.
- tax subjects did not fulfil certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns;
- shortcomings have been identified in the activities of the tax or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise duties and in their interaction with customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise duties, attention to international trade will continue to be needed in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the quality of the work of tax administrators in the administration of value added tax.
Effective control of excise duties is based on control of document circulation, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on import and export of goods.
3. Description of the situation regarding value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") was levied by the tax or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out within the territory of the country and by the customs authorities on importation of goods.
The tax revenue was determined by the tax authorities by the difference between the collected own tax liability and the refunded excess VAT deductions.
VAT revenue at customs offices was determined by the amount of tax collected by them.
In accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, the tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the tax deductions applied at the tax or tax authorities.
For most tax and tax authorities, excess VAT deductions exceeded tax liability.
VAT is one of the key taxes in terms of state budget revenues, as it accounted for about 31% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic and about 42% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic in 2003.
Total VAT collection in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned totalled CZK 231.4 billion.
Total VAT collection in Slovakia amounted to SKK 83.8 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected 187.0 billion SKK in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned totalled 103.2 billion SKK.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as the ‘SPD’) was carried out by the competent tax and tax authorities and, when importing products subject to the SPD, by the customs authorities.
SpD's share of the tax revenue of the state budget in the Czech Republic amounted to approximately 16% in 2003 and approximately 19% in the Slovak Republic.
The total collection of State Treasury funds collected in the Czech Republic by financial and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to CZK 85.6 billion and in the Slovak Republic amounted to SKK 38.0 billion.
4. Progress of control action
The cooperation between the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic took place in two stages.
In the first stage, the comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was carried out; in the second stage, the results of this comparison were used for mutual verification of the implementation of selected trade transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and for inspections carried out on the territory of both countries.
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel VAT and VAT audits was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting was held at which, among other things, the selection of commodities - goods which presented a significant risk in complying with customs and tax rules: - alcohol and spirits, tariff lines Nos 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff lines Nos 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff lines Nos 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile telephones and their accessories, tariff lines Nos 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
The two parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out: a) from unallocated items found by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, b) from entities carrying out imports and exports regularly or in one lump sum in a large volume, c) based on findings from inspections carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
In the first stage, a mechanism of mutual assignment of JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
