JOINT FINAL REPORT on the Results of Parallel Inspections of the Administration of Excise Taxes in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint final report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Opening Word
The joint report presents the progress and result of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between supreme audit institutions of both countries was realized on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO of Slovakia and the SAO of the Czech Republic in the performance of parallel audits focused on the administration of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen based on the fact that both EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to find out how it is applied at national level, how the excise tax administration system is set up and how the systems in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefits of the control actions carried out were the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Last but not least, it was beneficial to find that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise duty administration is very limited without the implementation of parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrik,
President
President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel controls of the administration of the SPD in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia and their administration complies with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences have been found between the excise duty adjustment in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic; in the Czech Republic, it contributes to the effective administration of excise duties by verifying the economic stability of applicants for a permit and mandatory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils and certain other oils; In Slovakia, the distribution of control stamps is simpler than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome for tax administrators.
In the fight against excise tax evasion, the supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw material, the implementation of the fuel distributor institute and the registration of sellers of consumer alcohol packaging have proved to be good practice in both countries.
Revenues from excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's goals of reducing taxes on labour, introducing eco-saving measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, not least because there is no indexation of excise duty rates in both countries.
This results in a reduction in the importance of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, a real reduction in the tax burden of excise duties.
The introduction of environmental measures has long been financially supported by the State, but these measures have a negative impact on excise revenue, which will have to be replaced in the future by other revenues or by a reduction in government expenditure.
Administrative expenditure spent on administration of excise duties in both the Czech Republic and Slovakia has been growing for a long time, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency has been declining.
In the SR, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditure on the computerisation of the administration of excise duties (IT expenditure) and by expenditure on the wages of employees performing permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
The computerisation of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic has not significantly reduced the number of tax administrations.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend that the Slovak Ministry reconsider the validity of permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
In the Czech Republic, the effectiveness of administrative expenditure was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period that would lead to a reduction in the personnel requirements of the administration of excise duties.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax entities in the Slovak Republic is about a third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical exercise of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
Administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is administratively more demanding than in the Czech Republic and more costly due to the ratio of the number of tax transactions to the number of entities.
The computerisation of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In Slovakia, the administration of excise tax returns is fully electronized, in the Czech Republic, documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are electronically transmitted.
Both ways of computerisation support efficient administration of excise duties, and therefore the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure for the implementation of EMCS could not be compared as DG SR provided data on expenditure only for the upgrade of the system in the period 2011-2015, but expenditure was incurred before that period.
Expenditure incurred in the aforementioned period for the EMCS upgrade alone was approximately 20% higher in Slovakia than the expenditure incurred in the Czech Republic for both the introduction of EMCS and the upgrade of this system in more than ten years.
The excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the Slovak Republic the administration of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of the electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise products (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but to a lesser extent in the Slovak Republic, as significantly higher expenditure was spent on the introduction of the system and its modernisation than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation of the two audit institutions was carried out on the basis of the Cooperation Agreement during parallel inspections aimed at the administration of excise duties of 18.8.2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic agreed to perform parallel audits, which will primarily focus on the issue of excise tax administration and whose results will allow analysis, comparison and evaluation of the findings.
The common audit issues on which the parallel controls were based were agreed.
Characteristics of the subject-matter and objectives of the parallel check:
The aim of the parallel controls was to compare the performance of excise authorities, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the excise administration process.
In particular, the following main audit questions were to be answered:
Did the excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures?
Has the introduction of the Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient and has the cost of its introduction been expended effectively?
The parallel inspections carried out should have identified the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, especially in the area of legal regulation and in the setting of the organizational structure.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The General Directorate of Customs (DG) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (FR SR) have joined the joint declaration on mutual cooperation between the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include the area of excise duties, inter alia, the fight against fraud, exploring the possibility of harmonising legislation and seeking harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint activities to increase effectiveness in detecting fraud and sharing experiences and best practices.
1 EMCS is operated in accordance with Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products.
Identification of the audit performed by the SAO of the Czech Republic
Control number: 15/33
Subject of the inspection: Administration of excise duties
Aim of the audit: The aim of the SAO audit was to examine the customs authorities' procedures for the administration of excise duties, especially for monitoring of transport in the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and for securing the tax (customs debts); verify that the system of administration of excise duties is set up in such a way as to ensure the efficiency of the collection of state budget revenue.
Audit period: years 2012-2015 and, in case of relevant connections, the period before and after
Person audited: General Directorate of Customs
Identification of the audit performed by the SAO SR
Audit number: KA-023/2016/1050
Subject of the inspection: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the audit: The aim of the audit was an independent and objective examination of whether the Slovak DG and customs offices (CA) in the administration of excise duties operate economically, efficiently and effectively in accordance with generally binding legislation.
Audit period: years 2012-2015
Person audited: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
The excise administration legislation is divided into EU (see Annex 1) and national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/EC concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC defines excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the administration of taxes and the treatment of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This Directive allows other products to be subject to excise duties.
In particular, EU legislation regulates the minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for each type of selected product, the production, storage, processing and holding of taxable products, the chargeability of the tax, tax exemptions and refunds, the supervision of the transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows for the introduction of control procedures and institutes at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legislation on excise duties is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of mineral oil tax, alcohol tax, tobacco products tax, beer tax, wine and intermediate products tax and raw tobacco tax.
This law defines the forms of treatment of products subject to excise duties, the taxpayer, the authorisation procedure, the conditions for the transport of products, the declaration of tax and penalties for infringements of legislation.
The Act and subsequent Decrees further regulate certain other conditions for the handling of mineral oils (marking of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and storage of raw tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in parts 45 to 47 of Act No. 261/2007 Coll., on Stabilization of Public Budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are contained in special legislation. Act on Fuel No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, supply, distribution of fuel and keeping of records of fuel put into free tax circulation.
Act No 61/1997 Coll., on ethyl alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of ethyl alcohol.
Act No.307/2013 Coll., on the mandatory labelling of alcohol, and the relevant implementing regulations stipulate the mandatory marking of alcohol in consumer packaging, the conditions for handling control tapes and the conditions for handling alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, takeover, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Tax procedures, which are not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Penalties are imposed in accordance with the procedure laid down in Act No 500/2004 Coll., Administrative Code.
The conditions for the issue of a trade licence (concession) for the operation of the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, treatment and sale of fermentation alcohol, potable alcohol and spirits" are regulated by Act No.455/1991 Coll., on the trade licence business (Trade Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has made use of the authorisation to introduce control procedures and institutes to control the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to monitor compliance with the legislation in the treatment of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as in the treatment of selected products for which tax has already been paid.
These include the monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and raw tobacco, the labelling of certain other mineral oils, the labelling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic used the right to apply excise duty to other products and introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the Government of the Czech Republic Resolution No. 735 of 3 October 2012, the implementation of the "zero tolerance plan for the black market in spirits" resulted in major legislative changes in the Czech Republic in 2012-2015, which introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on excise duty on alcohol.
In the same period, there were also major changes in the legislation on the mineral oil tax, the tax on tobacco products and the criminality of preparing tax evasion.
Criminal law protection of tax revenue
With effect from 1 July 2016, the preparation of the offence of "tax reduction, fee reduction and similar compulsory payment" is made a criminal offence. The modification should allow police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, such as the deployment of operational means of investigation.
General provisions for the administration of excise duties
With effect from 1 January 2015, the issuance of a licence for the disposal of products subject to excise duty is subject to: reliability; indebtedness; economic stability; authorisation to operate a trade enabling the pursuit of activities related to the licence; a situation in which the applicant is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The aim of the legislation was, in particular, to address the problem of the build-up of tax arrears by reducing those entitled to dispose of products subject to excise duty.
The condition of economic stability newly allows the tax authorities to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the context of the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent those who do not have sufficient financial resources to properly comply with their tax obligations from disposing of the selected products.
In order to assess the economic stability of the applicant, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) have been established on the basis of which a financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, the administrative discretion of the tax administrator depends on the individual conditions of the procedure.
The law stipulates the frequency of verification of compliance with the condition of economic stability due to the timeliness of the data – the verification takes place once a year, following the deadline for submission of the income tax return.
The tax administrator has the possibility to determine other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the permit holder does not fulfil the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the permit or to revoke it with a delay.
Of the 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic audited the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of the tax collateral (e.g. repeated recipient).
Authorisations were revoked for ten entities, the other applicants increased their tax collateral, capitalised their contribution to the company or provided up-to-date accounting data showing that they already fulfilled all the conditions for authorisation.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must also be fulfilled by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member thereof, or by a natural person who, although not a statutory body of the applicant or a member thereof, performs this activity (chaining of legal persons in the capacity of a statutory body or its member, so-called connected entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 connected entities had been screened.
The registers kept under the Act on Excise Duties (Sections 37 to 40 and Section 60 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.) contain data on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, received, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment (suspension arrangement, importation, reintroduction into suspension arrangement, exportation, free tax circulation, captive use, loss);
the SEED ID of the recipient or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of occurrence and registration;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carriers, number of transport);
the registration numbers of the related documents;
the notification of the release for free circulation of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging marked with a control tape and the details of its distribution.
A record of receipt after transport shall be made without delay after the transport has ended.
In the case of records kept electronically, records must be kept or allow output in the format xls, xlsx, ods.
Ethyl alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures designed to provide a detailed overview of the activities of the operators (see Annex 3, Schema A) from the production of raw alcohol through the marking of the control tape to its distribution to the final seller or authorised user of the exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the production facility for the production of ethyl alcohol, which is not in operation, is also subject to supervision by customs authorities.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of alcohol processing and the production of spirits and to identify persons handling spirits in consumer packaging, to reduce the handling of spirits to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of production, receipt, stocks and issue of ethyl alcohol contain information on the quantity of ethyl alcohol by stage of production and processing of ethyl alcohol, with document numbers.
Limitations on the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and restrictions on the number of packages with broken surveillance tape at the point of final sale or delivery to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other container with a capacity of not more than one litre, or three litres if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits put up in larger packages are considered as unmarked and prohibited to be handled.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his or her personal use, there may be a maximum of one consumer pack with a broken control tape, or three if fitted with a one-way valve.
Compulsory registration of a person who places alcohol in products in consumer packaging having at least 15 % by volume of alcohol into free tax circulation and is: an importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under suspension of tax exemption, provided that personal and technical conditions are fulfilled.
The personal conditions – reliability, integrity and non-pronouncement of disqualification – must be fulfilled by the applicant and a person in the capacity of a statutory body or a responsible representative.
The applicant must provide a security deposit of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately €3,700 to €185,000) depending on the amount of control tapes taken.
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for alcohol marking and the equipment of the place of marking or tax warehouse with a camera monitoring device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
Registration labels for control tapes are introduced for the labelling of spirit drinks with a volume of more than 0,06 litre.
When control tapes are being transported, the identification of the control tapes shall be indicated on the transport documents or the customs declaration at export.
The control tape until 30.11.2013 contained a 10-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration sampling number, the code of the application for the allocation of control tapes and the code of classification according to the level of the ethanol concentration by volume.
The control tape from 1 December 2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the amount of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 °C, rounded down to the nearest millilitres.
The record of the control tapes for the labelling of spirit drinks contains daily records of the different ways of handling the control tapes according to the registration codes, as well as the documents on the basis of which the registration took place.
In the event of the destruction, loss or theft of specific control tapes, the holder of the control tapes shall electronically notify the tax authorities of the registration code of the control tapes in question and their number on the following working day after the operative event.
Introducing a new factual basis for offences and adjusting the level of penalties imposed for infringements of legislation when dealing with control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to the amount of the excise duty or may exceed it by a factor of 10 (e.g. destruction or loss of control tapes in excess of 0.1% of the total quantity of an individual order for control tapes, failure to return the control tape within the statutory time limit).
Restriction of the handling of control tapes only to registered holders, who may not transfer them to another person, with the exception of their provision to a foreign supplier for the purpose of marking spirits in consumer packaging produced outside the Czech Republic.
The control tapes exported must be placed on the consumer packaging and brought back no later than nine months after receipt from the tax authorities.
Compulsory registration of a distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging, provided that similar personal conditions are met as for a person obliged to mark alcohol and with the obligation to deposit a deposit of up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approx. €185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging.
Eligible persons shall be obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or to final sellers or may sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency practitioner, the administrative authority, organisational units of the State or unregistered persons in the course of tax execution.
Notices of the release for free circulation of ethyl alcohol or sales in consumer packaging are to be sent by the holders and distributors of ethyl alcohol to the tax administrator immediately on the day following the operative event via the information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or in accordance with the content in xml format.
The notification shall include the number of control strips used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the percentage by volume of ethyl alcohol, the European Commodity Code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller, as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
Tax entities sent about 10.5 million notifications in 2014 and 2015.
Compulsory concession (a specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and treatment of ethyl alcohol, but also for the sale of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or business natural person for his own internal use.
Licensed trades can be carried out only after a decision by the Trade Licensing Office, subject to compliance with professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of ethyl alcohol.
The benefit for the tax administrator is an overview of sellers and their establishments and restrictions.
trading to reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, about 94,000 licenses were registered in 2014 and about 104,000 in 2015 for the industry including production, treatment of ethyl alcohol, potable alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales.
Checks on compliance with legislation in the area of handling products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic are also ensured in their activities outside the tax administrator: trade licensing offices, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, authorities of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, authorities of the Czech Trade Inspection Authority.
If it finds that there has been a breach of duty or a breach of prohibition, it shall immediately inform the excise authorities thereof.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has put in place a comprehensive surveillance system (see Annex 3, Diagram B) to which mineral oils subject to excise duty, but also selected mineral oils not subject to excise duty, which have been used for tax evasion.
The system includes monitoring from the production of mineral oil through the storage, transport, marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils, the marking of certain other mineral oils up to delivery to the final consumer or user and, in some cases, the consumption of mineral oils.
The supervision of the customs authorities includes the production of marking agents for the marking and handling of mineral oils.
The mineral oils listed under CN codes 2710 19 25 (kerosene other), 2710 19 29 (other medium oils not elsewhere specified) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49 shall be subject to the marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils unless their marking is prohibited.
For example, benzol, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than motor propulsion are subject to the labelling of certain other mineral oils.
It is only possible to mark and dye selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marker substance on the basis of the permission of the tax administrator.

THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils which are a group of mineral oils falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than motor propulsion) whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and has at least one of the following characteristics: flash point less than 150 °C, distillation test distils at least 20 % of the volume including losses up to 350 °C.
These mineral oils were misused as an additive in the finished fuel, in particular diesel, or were directly used or sold for engine propulsion because the physical characteristics are very similar.
Registration with the tax authority is required for entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres.
The personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be fulfilled for the issuance of the registration, which shall apply throughout 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by firing.
No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 For example, when mineral oil is used as fuel (excluding navigation on water, unless it is a private pleasure craft) or as an ingredient for the production of fuel, when the marking is defective in its use.
registration.
As of 30 November 2016, the Register of Persons Handling Special Mineral Oils contained 54 valid registrations, upon the proposal of the holder of the registration, four registrations were cancelled.
The electronic register shall contain detailed information on the receipt, own consumption and the sale or transfer of the mineral oil, including document numbers, numbers of notifications of acquisition to the tax authorities, places of storage and consumption, the purpose of consumption, the place of storage and consumption or, on sale, the place of delivery and the customer's registration number.
Notification of any acquisition of a special mineral oil must be given to the tax authority between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of the trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the specific mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of consumption or information on the sale or transfer shall be reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed in the relevant year shall be submitted by the entity together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications of the purpose of use and marking, place of storage or consumption, identification details of the person to whom the special mineral oil is resold or transferred shall be given before any change.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically by means of smart forms or by a data container in PDFa format.
In 2015, 630 notifications were submitted by persons handling special mineral oils.
The seizure and forfeiture of special mineral oils or means of transport must be declared by the tax administrator in cases where he finds handling of special mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to fulfil his reporting obligation.
As in the case of non-compliances in the transport of excise products, these deficiencies cannot be corrected subsequently.
Registration of a fuel distributor is compulsory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Registered fuel distributors may only be persons meeting the following criteria:
Compulsory concession of the Trade Licensing Office (a specific form of trade licence).
The application for a concession or, where appropriate, the appointment of a responsible representative, shall be subject to an opinion by the customs office, which shall examine whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or the members of the statutory body of the applicant legal person and the designated responsible representative meet the condition of reliability.
If these persons meet the condition of reliability, the customs office issues a favourable opinion.
Reliable person means a person of good character in terms of criminal law, property, customs law and tax law.
Professional competence is a condition for the award of the concession.
Indebtedness of the same class of persons as in the case of reliability.
A debtor is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he or she will meet his or her payment obligations to the State in a proper and timely manner, i.e. he or she does not have arrears to the State budget and to the general health insurance.
A fuel distributor shall not be prohibited from operating by a court or administrative authority.
The fuel distributor shall not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit deposit (or bank guarantee) of 20 000 000 CZK (i.e. approx. 740 000 €), which can be reduced to 10 000 000 CZK (i.e. approx. 370 000 €) after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and fulfilment of other conditions.
The distributor shall be obliged to submit a fuel distribution notification to the customs office within 20 days of the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall contain details of the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The data to be reported are data on trading partners, document numbers, product selected, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The right to a refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
Refund of excise duty on mineral oils may be claimed only in respect of an activity which is clearly connected with the activity carried out on the land.
In 2015, there were about 64,000 claims for a tax refund totalling CZK 1,172,844,680 (i.e., EUR 43,401,720).
Since 2017, the Czech government has also introduced a refund of excise duty on fuel to livestock farmers.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, are engaged in the breeding of cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats will be newly able to exercise this right.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on sales of tobacco products with the old tax rate
In response to the long-term under-achievement of budgeted revenues from excise duties on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced a restriction on sales of tobacco products with the old tax rate in case of a change in the tax rate with effect from 1 December 2014.
Excise duty on tobacco products shall be paid by the use of tobacco labels.
The use of a tobacco sticker means placing it on a unit packet (Section 116 of the Excise Duty Act).
For the application of the rate of excise duty, the production of the tobacco product in the condition intended for the final consumer shall be taken into account, without its removal from storage, delivery, dispatch or sale or sale to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the rate of excise duty appears on the tobacco sticker together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, and the sticker indicates the number of items in the package or the quantity of smoking tobacco in kilograms.
The tobacco sticker has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the sale of unit packets of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco label bearing the previous (old) rate of duty was fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month following the entry into force of the new rate of excise duty.
The development of the removal of tobacco labels in 2014 and the comparison with the development in previous years shows that tobacco manufacturers significantly frontloaded tobacco products with the ‘old’ tax rate each year, effectively shifting the effectiveness of the ‘new’ tax rate by about one year.
Raw tobacco tax
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the manufacture of tobacco products without the permission of the tax authorities and the non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as measures against tax fraud.
With effect from 1 July 2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, has not been supplied to another Member State or to a third country, or for which the origin, the intended use or the person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been proved shall be subject to excise duty.
Restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, the marking of unit packets with a control tape and restrictions on sales in designated places have been complemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Manufacturing facilities for the processing of tobacco raw materials and the manufacture of tobacco products shall not be subject to customs supervision.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or treated.
A registered person may only be a person meeting the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative, which applies throughout the registration period.
The conditions for registration are: (a) authorisation to operate a trade allowing the activity of a person storing raw tobacco, (b) reliability, (c) indebtedness, (d) the fact that the person storing the raw tobacco has not been banned from carrying out his activity, (e) the fact that the person storing the raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) the provision of a security of CZK 20 000 000 (i.e. approximately EUR 740 000).
The electronic register shall contain the date of receipt or delivery of the raw tobacco, the document number, the identification of the business partner, the quantity and type of the raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco must be given to the tax authorities at intervals of 24 to 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
The details of the trading partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the storage address, the purpose of use and the details of the carrier shall be reported.
Notification of the expected quantities of raw tobacco received or dispatched in the relevant year shall be submitted by the entity together with the registration application or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
The notifications shall be submitted electronically by means of a data container in PDFa format.
Transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the requisite particulars.
Legislation on excise duties in Slovakia
The legal framework regulating the area of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its single tax system.
Individual types of excise duties are exhaustively determined by SR legislation, which is similar to that of neighbouring countries.
Definition of legislation in the Slovak Republic
Legislative regulation of excise duties is ensured by four laws according to the individual subject of the tax.
Harmonisation has been achieved by the adoption of the following laws on excise duties: Act No 98/2004 Coll., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106/2004 Coll., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530/2011 Coll., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609/2007 Coll., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All excise tax laws are substantive law rules and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No. 563/2009 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulates the administration of taxes, rights and obligations of tax subjects and other persons.
This legal framework transposed individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008 concerning the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC and transposed provisions of other European Community directives and legislation.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Slovak Republic
Since 2011, legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several major changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS system, the traffic monitoring of selected excise products under suspension of excise duty has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system where such traffic is monitored in real time.
Under the EMCS electronic system, the institute of suspending the access of tax subjects to the EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office has the possibility to suspend access precisely when there is a well-founded fear of an invalid or undetermined tax from previous tax years and its unenforceability.
This relates to the chargeability of the tax, since the transport of excise goods requires the lodging of a security, which is released when the transport is completed.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility to use so-called red diesel was abolished.
The gas oil, commonly called red diesel, was a mineral oil.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific legally defined purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of the abolition of red diesel was to reduce the public deficit, simplify the taxation system for mineral oils and reduce the administrative burden on the businesses concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel vendor.
The purpose of this legal amendment was to introduce an obligation to keep a register for all service stations.
The clarification of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely the fuel distributor and the fuel consumer.
This amendment has contributed to the elimination of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and has clarified the movement of these fuels (see Annex 4, Figure A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
In SR, however, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to be labelled with an indicator substance.
Excise duty on tobacco products
As part of the fight against tax evasion and the monitoring of tobacco raw materials, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Material Act has been extended and a new tax entity – a trader in tobacco raw materials – has been introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, the obligation to register technological installations for the manufacture of tobacco products was introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control marks for the labelling of consumer packages of tobacco products.
Cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco are marked with the control mark.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically, using the information system for the collection of control stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the taxpayer and the tax authorities.
One state-owned stamp control printer was established – in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of control stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system for printing control marks strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the control mark to easily verify whether the goods originate from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd digit) shall form the checksum; 3. the location determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4. place is the series identifier; 5.-8. place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12. The place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Furthermore, the price of the cigarettes, the symbol for the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in a consumer package and the length of the cigarettes must be indicated on the control mark used to mark the cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected ethyl alcohol, wine and beer, as the original three rules of substantive law were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was drafted mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the problem of taxation of alcoholic beverages, solution of their production, monitoring of movement, securing the tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, streamline the administration of the tax, reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
The new approach to the taxation of different types of alcoholic beverages introduced the application of a uniform rate of excise duty to alcoholic beverages and took into account the volume percentage of the actual alcoholic strength.
For still wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the final product shall be taken into account.
The beer concentration shall also be expressed as a percentage by volume of the actual alcoholic strength of the finished product.
A category of small-scale producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and that of his household up to a maximum of 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically, using the information system for the collection of control stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the taxpayer and the tax authorities.
One state-owned stamp control printer was established – in the Kremnice Mint.
The exercise of fiscal supervision over the printing of control stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Figure B) and the elimination of the falsification of control stamps.
The new system for printing control marks strengthens the system for checking goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the control mark to easily verify whether the goods originate from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd digit) shall form the checksum; 3. the location determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4. place is the series identifier; 5.-8. place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12. The place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on ethyl alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by a common law no. 353/2003 Coll.
The tax on solid fuels, the tax on natural gas and certain other gases and the tax on electricity are part of Act No. 261/2007 Coll.
In Slovakia, on the other hand, every excise duty is regulated by a special law, with the exception of the law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, which contains a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, as of 1 January 2015, the issue of an authorisation to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is subject, among other things, to proof of the economic stability of the applicants, which is verified annually by the customs authorities by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the Slovak Republic, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce the reinsurance tax.
FR SR performs tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control marks for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printer and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of control stamps is carried out by the state-owned Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control strips in the Czech Republic is not supervised by customs authorities.
Tobacco stickers and control strips will be taken from the printer by the authorized territorial office of the customs office in Kutna Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their purchasers in this territorial workplace, and alcohol labelling control tapes are further distributed to individual locally competent tax authorities according to the place of marking.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define manufacturers of tobacco stickers and control strips.
In the Slovak Republic there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or a part thereof, in the Czech Republic there is no such obligation.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco sticker bears the excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when the tobacco stickers are taken from the designated customs office.
In the Slovak Republic, on the other hand, the stamp does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, the refund of excise duty on mineral oils in case of their use for agricultural plant primary production, so-called green diesel, was introduced during the audited period.
As of 2017, this tax refund was extended to livestock production.
In SR such support for farmers is not introduced (it existed until 31.12.2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of CZK 20 million (i.e. EUR 740 thousand) was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic.
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1 891 entities in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1 717 tax entities).
In Slovakia, a similar fuel distributor institute is in place, but without the deposit required to ensure excise duty on mineral oils.
In Slovakia, 303 distributors were registered in 2014 and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
In Slovakia, there is an institute of fuel seller and fuel consumer, which is issued by the locally competent customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to labelling, in the Slovak Republic the labelling of mineral oils is not applied after the abolition of the so-called red diesel.
In the Czech Republic, the alcohol control tape contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of the alcohol and a twelve-digit registration code indicating the spirit content of the spirit drink, according to which the control tape is kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the control tape shall be entered in the register on the following working day.
The holder of the tape shall be obliged to notify their use within the same time limit.
In SR, the stamp intended for the marking of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number, which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax authorities and is used to verify the authenticity of the stamp.
The record contains the number of control stamps collected, used and reclaimed.
Both the Czech Republic and Slovakia have introduced the institute of compulsory registration or registration of the alcohol distributor.
In the Slovak Republic, registration is subject to the fulfilment of conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; an annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least EUR 100 000; or a paid-up capital of at least EUR 100 000; a minimum of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, the registration is conditional, among other things, on the deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. EUR 185,000) in favour of the tax administrator for the whole period of validity of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In the Slovak Republic, the permanent presence of the tax authorities is required for the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging.
In the Czech Republic, the production of alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of the person obliged to mark alcohol with the condition of lodging a deposit in favour of the tax administrator ranging from CZK 100,000 (i.e. EUR 3,700) up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. EUR 185,000) depending on the amount of control tapes taken and the installation of a monitoring device with continuous access of the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and Slovakia goes well beyond the EU minimum requirements for the subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as to risks identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax authorities to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as part of the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw material (e.g. leaves), an excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw material was introduced in addition to the EU legislation.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw material are not harmonised tobacco products, the Czech Republic and Slovakia monitor their movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic may recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the verification of economic stability of applicants for authorisation under the Excise Tax Act has proved successful because it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such verifications also in SR conditions.
The distribution of control stamps is more efficient in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden customs authorities with the costs related to transport between the printer and the purchaser of control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The financial administration of the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the existence and location of technological facilities for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the collection of tax on tobacco products is more effective, because the order of a tobacco sticker is a tax return with the subsequent payment of tax.
The financial administration in Slovakia has a better overview of the places of sale of fuel thanks to the introduction of the concepts of "fuel seller" and "fuel consumer".
The introduction of mandatory marking of mineral oils in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils with a reduced tax rate or exempted from tax.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and Slovakia (2014) a new control tape, or a stamp containing an identification code, was introduced.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains the registration code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation has abandoned its use.
Impacts cannot yet be evaluated due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark or tape is an effective measure to combat tax evasion.
The SAO of Slovakia and the SAO of the Czech Republic may also recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States.
SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-client approach that does not block the funds of tax entities.
On the other hand, the approach of the Czech Republic is rather restrictive, as it introduces a deposit burdening the cash flow of tax subjects, but it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Development of excise revenue
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State in order to increase the revenue of the State budget and also to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered to be harmful to individuals and/or society (the regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Commission Communication ‘EUROPE 2020 — A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth’ of 3.3.2010 under the Flagship Initiative ‘Resource efficient Europe’, the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, including by revising energy taxation with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfil the EC's objective, Member States should seek to shift the tax burden from labour to, inter alia, energy and environmental taxation as part of a more "greening" of tax systems.
The collection of excise tax revenue in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes the collection of excise duty on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share in GDP is monitored, inter alia, by the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Both supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to enter the query on the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share in GDP declined slightly according to OECD data.
The exchange rate of the European Central Bank (ECB) was used to convert the amounts in CZK into € on 31 December of the relevant year.
The nominal exchange rate of the CZK against the euro in 2013 depreciated by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25.140 to 27.425).
This was mainly due to the CNB Bank Board's monetary policy decision of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of collection of excise duties, rates of excise duties and per capita income in € decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the share of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off shortfall in excise duty revenue from tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of tobacco products with the old rate of duty.
The share of excise duties is also influenced by the growth in the collection of income taxes, which has increased significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation in the Czech Republic.
Excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the total collection of excise duties (about 55.7% in 2015), but this fell in spite of the significant growth of the economy compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although the registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as an anti-tax measure.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively reflected in the tax revenue.
Gas tax, solid fuel tax and electricity tax account for a negligible share, which is due to a low tax rate compared to neighbouring countries, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU.
If rates are not increased, their share will decrease in the future in view of the ever decreasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on ethyl alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a large-scale tax fraud case involving the putting into circulation of untaxed ethyl alcohol, ethyl alcohol containing methanol or under-denatured ethyl alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a number of measures against such behaviour and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the 2012 collection by EUR 4 million.
The proportion of the tax on tobacco products has increased as a result of rising rates.
The standard rates of excise duties changed between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on tobacco products, with an increase in the rate mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64/EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, excluding the tax on tobacco products, fell significantly. It has risen only slightly for tobacco products.
In relation to price growth, GDP or the standard of living, there is no indexation of the rate of excise duties, so the function of excise duties to regulate socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With economic growth in the Czech Republic and rising living standards, real rates of excise duties are decreasing.
7 Indexation – automatic adjustment of a certain economic quantity for inflation, this adjustment is made on the basis of a law or a contract (in the case of pensions paid by the state it is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
In the current legislation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the indexation of the level of excise duty rates and the evolution of consumer prices are not addressed because they are fixed.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Of all excise duties introduced in Slovakia, excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the state budget's annual tax revenues, while its share did not fall below 52% in the whole audited period.
Excise duty on tobacco products accounts for the second largest share.
This tax accounts on average for around 32% of total excise duty collection.
Between 2012 and 2015, there was an increase in the collection of excise duty per capita in Slovakia.
This development is due to an increase in the rates of excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The increase in the collection of excise duties per inhabitant of the Slovak Republic is constant and corresponds to the evolution of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decrease in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention in the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which in the Czech Republic is about 2.7 and 2.8 times higher, respectively, but per capita the collection of these selected products is only about 1/3 higher.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK against € for foreign consumers.
The tax on mineral oils is also caused by greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, growing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a significant impact.
Evaluation Real rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic were falling as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in total tax revenues is not increasing and there is no shift from taxation of labour to taxation of consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved value of the share of excise duties is consistently above the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is influenced mainly by the change in excise duty rates, the development of the economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures, which are subsidised by the State in various forms, will have to be compensated by other revenues or by a reduction in the State's expenditure.
The lack of indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and Slovakia reduces their regulatory function and insufficiently supports the EU's objectives of a Europe less dependent on environmentally friendly sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic is reflected in higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the administration of excise duties, i.e. it expresses the amount of expenditure per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The effectiveness of the tax administrator in administering the tax affects the scope and organizational organization of the tax administrator, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of electronization of individual activities.
The calculation of the administrative cost-effectiveness of the tax administration by the conversion rate method is based on the number of employees involved in the administration of excise duties in a line-managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is performed, among other activities, by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organisational unit of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of the tax is ensured by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs authorities are the internal organisational unit, costs and revenues are included for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility to compare the efficiency of the administration of excise duties, expenditures and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative tasks performed mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial control tasks are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
The excise duties are administered mainly by the following departments:
Directorate-General for Customs
Department 23 TAXATION
Department 231 – Tax Methodologies monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures the interpretation of legislation, methodically manages and coordinates: the execution of tax administration agendas and related regulations, in particular tax proceedings and related control and supervision activities, the administration of transport of selected products;
Department 232 – ELO and Search performs search and methodically manages transport controls of selected products and ensures international cooperation between ELO and EMCS;
Unit 233 – Tax Controls methodically manages and coordinates the execution of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Unit 301 — Legal carries out methodological work in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative proceedings, tax inspection process, registration proceedings, discovery proceedings, payment of taxes, fines for late tax claims, penalties and interest;
Unit 302 — Administrative Activities carries out decision-making activities in cases where the legislation establishes the competence of the DG, e.g. deciding on the delegation of the territorial jurisdiction of the entity to another relevant tax administrator, deciding on the attraction, i.e. taking over the matter by a superior tax administrator, appealing against decisions of the customs authorities and examining incentives for inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Unit 303 — Revenue and recovery management methodically manages, coordinates and performs international cooperation tasks in the recovery of tax arrears and insolvency proceedings;
Department 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION SUPPORT
Department 601 - Risk and Criminal Analysis provides and performs risk analyses and participates in the management of executive risks and the planning of control activities and control actions;
Unit 604 — Financial Analyses carries out financial analysis in the customs administration, in particular in the context of the authorisation procedure.
Customs offices carry out activities within the agenda at various locations in the region and even agendas are dispersed in several locations:
Unit 02 — Analysis and Information Support, which carries out risk analyses, risk profiles management and the collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1 Legal
Section 11 — Legal and administrative activities, which handles documents, opinions and submission reports for the Appellate Body, issues authorization decisions in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the Act on Mandatory Alcohol Labelling and the Act on Alcohol, decides to ensure payment of a tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Section 3 - TAX
Department 31 – Tax, which performs the following tasks: tax supervision in tax entities, e.g. checking compliance with the conditions laid down in the issued permits, supervising the functionality and accuracy of the production equipment for the production of alcohol and ascertaining the quantity and concentration of the produced alcohol, professional supervision in the denaturation of alcohol, physical checks in the area of administration of excise duties; non-tax inspections in the area of inspections based on laws indirectly related to excise duties, in particular checking the compulsory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils, checking the taxation of selected products, checking the labelling of tobacco products, checking whether the seller or buyer implements the Act on the quantity of fuel in connection with the Act on the Act on the price of fuel, the law on the fulfilment of duty in connection with the price of fuel in connection with the Act on the Act on the law on the price of fuel; the registration of economic operators for tax purposes, the registration of persons obliged to mark alcohol and of distributors of alcohol and the registration of distributors of fuel; the administration of taxes, in particular the conduct of tax proceedings concerning the assessment and prescription or refund of tax, the monitoring of the securing of tax and its use for the payment of tax, the conduct of searches;
Division 39 – Tobacco stickers and control tapes – is an organisational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and performs activities in the field of ordering, production and distribution and disposal of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
For the disposal of returned/damaged tobacco stickers, representatives of both the Customs Office and the DG are present to supervise the disposal process and to draw up a record of the disposal.
In the case of alcohol-labelled control tapes, the Director of the Customs Office shall appoint, by an internal management act, a three-member committee for the disposal of discarded, unsealed/returned control tapes by shredding.
After the physical shredding of the control tapes has taken place, the chairman of the Winding-up Committee shall ensure that the details of the destroyed control tapes are recorded;
Section 5 — CONTROL,
Department 52 – Tax Inspections performs tax inspections;
Section 6 - SUPERVISORY
Unit 61 — Supervision of Entities exercises supervision over Entities at points of sale, e.g. control of sales of spirit drinks and tobacco products;
Unit 62 – Mobile Surveillance carries out traffic checks on selected products en route.
Administrative costs of excise administration in Slovakia
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a demanding transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The creation of DG SR was also reflected in the staff composition of the newly created departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In the context of the excise administration, the excise administration activities within the organisational structure of DG SR have been integrated into a larger number of different sections and related departments.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Customs and Tax Section DG SR Excise Tax Department (Slovak-wide competence):
Excise Department – directs and coordinates excise administration activities; draws up expert opinions; makes proposals and comments on legislative changes; issues decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax subjects; assigns and cancels registration numbers;
the separation of the exercise of fiscal supervision – directs and coordinates activities in the field of the exercise of fiscal supervision and fiscal control; exercises fiscal supervision;
Department of ELO and SPD systems – directs and coordinates mutual administrative cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through SEED and ISA systems; provides management and updates in the SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
Control stamp department – directs printing and control stamp handling activities; performs tax supervision over the loading and disposal of printing sheets and control stamps in the printing works.
Department of the Vice-President of Financial Administration
Department of Excise and Customs Appeals (Slovak-wide scope):
Excise appeals department - review customs decisions on the basis of ordinary and emergency appeals; Appeals procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The Customs Offices Section was created in the course of 2012, directly incorporating individual Customs Offices (9 Customs Offices) which have a territorial competence determined by higher territorial units, with the exception of one Customs Office which was established inter alia to perform tasks in relation to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
Excise Division – carrying out methodological work in relation to customs offices' branches and customs offices' stations; for selected entities, the tax administrator performs direct acts and decides on registration (tax warehouse, authorized receiver, repeated receiver, registered sender), on the amount of tax security, determines and refunds the tax, performs tax supervision and tax control; decides to waive the lodging of the tax security; decide to waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee in a tax warehouse for ethyl alcohol;
Legal Division – decision-making in cases of tax infringements; activities related to ordinary and extraordinary remedies; tax execution proceedings;
branch of the customs office – decides on the registration (except for the tax warehouse, the authorised receiver for re-admission, the registered consignor), the amount of the tax security; prescribes and refunds the tax; performs tax supervision and tax control; decides on security and on the forfeiture of goods;
Customs office stations – the exercise of fiscal supervision over the possession and movement of excise goods; ensures the exercise of permanent tax supervision in the alcohol tax warehouse; decides on security and on the forfeiture of goods.
Expenditure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic on administration of excise duties is constantly increasing, as, with the exception of wage growth, investment in effective administration of taxes and computerisation of financial administration is increasing.
Although revenue from excise duties increased, expenditure grew faster as a result of IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
Wage expenditure in the Slovak Republic is significantly affected by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol, which the Czech Republic does not apply.
Expenditure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on administration of excise duties increased more significantly between 2012 and 2015 in 2015, this growth was mainly due to growth in wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise duties also grew at roughly the same pace.
Wage expenditures in the Czech Republic are positively influenced by broader competencies of the customs administration, e.g. weighing of trucks, monitoring of compliance with obligations related to tolls.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the Slovak Republic shows a slightly deteriorating trend year-on-year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee increased.
Also in the Czech Republic, the number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee grew more slowly than in the Slovak Republic.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, wage growth is an important factor in the impaired efficiency of administrative expenditure, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a high administrative burden in the administration of excise duties appears to be a negative factor, as is confirmed by the continuing presence of staff in the administration of excise duties.
In the Slovak Republic, however, the administration of excise duties with lower revenues is significantly more demanding in terms of staffing capacity.
Performance indicators for the administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties is a set of activities aimed at correctly identifying, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
