The main processes in the administration of excise duties are tax assessment, authorisation and registration, supervision of transport, control and search of tax subjects.
The numbers of administrative tasks and entities managed are indicators of the performance of the tax administrator.
The correlation between the monitored indicator and the number of tax administrators expresses the effectiveness of the tax administrator's activities and defines the cost of a specific activity.
Authorisation and registration are essential for the handling and transport of selected products for commercial purposes under a duty suspension arrangement.
The tax administrator is obliged to perform continuous administration with the entities with a permit or registration, focusing on supervision of compliance with legal regulations and conditions set by the tax administrator, for which adequate personnel resources must be allocated.
The indicator monitored was the number of valid permits or registrations for the activity at 31 December of each year.
The number of permits or registrations issued is not the same as the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in a matter.
The monitored administrative acts are often the most important acts of the tax administrator (tax claims, transport administration in EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of acts ending with a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Authorisation and registration for activities in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
The production, processing, storage, receipt or dispatch of selected products is possible on the basis of the tax administrator's permission to operate a tax warehouse.
Where a tax warehouse operator has more than one warehouse, the authorisation shall be issued for each one separately, including the securing of the tax.
Tax security is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administrator (i.e. the physical presence of the official and the securing of the establishment by the tax administrator's conclusions).
In the Czech Republic, permanent tax supervision is not applied.
The tax warehouse operator also registers for tax under § 125 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.
Authorisation to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products exempt from tax from the place of importation to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to the place of exportation in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (replacing the status of registered consignor under Article 4(10) of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include tax-free permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels analogous to tax warehouse permits.
The distillery produces ethyl alcohol at a reduced rate of 50% tax (14,300 CZK/hl ethanol) – fruit spirits for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the permit to operate is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced tax rate may be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per farmer's household for personal consumption during the production period (July-June).
The registers kept by the distillery operators and made available to the tax authorities must contain information on the producer, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The authorised receiver for the re-admission of selected products and the authorised receiver for the one-off admission of selected products shall, subject to the authorisation of the tax authority and the conditions laid down, be entitled to receive or re-receive selected products in a conditional system shipped from another Member State on a one-off basis.
The beneficiary is not a tax warehouse operator and may not store or dispatch the selected products under the duty suspension arrangement.
The user of selected products exempt from tax is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or according to § 52a or § 53 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll. sells selected products exempt from tax to another user; Users have the status of tax subjects without the obligation to register for tax.
Acceptance and use of selected exempt products shall be subject to a final authorisation only from the supplier indicated in the authorisation.
On the basis of the authorisation, the exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of the authorisation for use or to a user who is entitled to use mineral oils without authorisation.
Tax-exempt mineral oils may be sold without a licence in cases provided for by law, such as:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year if the user manufactured them himself or if they were produced by him;
selected exempt mineral oils in unit packets of not more than 20 litres intended for purposes other than motor propulsion or heat production and simultaneously intended for sale to the final consumer.
Selected exempt products may be transported with proof of exemption.
The distributor of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging is entitled to sell or otherwise transfer ethyl alcohol put into free circulation after compulsory registration with the tax authorities.
The storekeeper of raw tobacco shall be entitled to store raw tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco products, subject to registration with the tax authorities and to the conditions laid down.
A person handling special mineral oils shall be entitled to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils in bulk or in packages of more than 220 litres, subject to registration with the tax authorities and subject to the conditions laid down.
On the basis of the issued concession and registration of the tax administrator, the fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel on the territory of the Czech Republic under specified conditions, with the exception of the sale of fuel from a petrol station.
The transport of the fuel must be accompanied by a tax document, a sales note or a transport document, or a distribution plan and bottling slips.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent to the tax authorities before the transport begins.
The service station operator is the owner of the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where the sale or supply of fuel to the fuel tank is generally permitted under the authorisation of the Construction Authority.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators in the following subdivisions: registered – normal sale or issue of fuel usually for fuel tanks of vehicles; with a defined access – operation usually in various business premises (e.g. quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organisations, construction yards), sales are made here for the other party on a limited basis based on specific contractual relations; non-public – fuel dispensing points for the operators' own consumption only.
A service station is not a construction or installation in the form of a service tank placed in operation (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is supplied only for own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to authorisation by the tax administrator and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may, subject to authorisation by the tax authorities, buy, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free circulation for resale.
They must also be authorised when they purchase or procure liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption of more than 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of actions. Tax inspections shall be carried out on tax obligations, claims made by the taxpayer or other circumstances relevant to the correct determination and determination of the tax relating to a single tax procedure.
Tax control may be carried out jointly for more than one tax procedure of a single tax entity.
Repeated tax inspections may be carried out only under the conditions and justifications laid down by law at the time the inspection is initiated.
The tax inspection is carried out within the three-year tax assessment period, which is extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. filing of additional tax proceedings, initiation of criminal proceedings in connection with the tax in question), or is suspended (judicial proceedings, international cooperation).
The tax assessment period shall end no later than 10 years after the deadline for making a proper tax claim.
There is no obligation for the tax authority to carry out a tax inspection of each tax entity.
The commencement of the tax inspection suspends the time limits for the possibility of filing a supplementary tax return or additional statement by the taxpayer (Section 141 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.) and restarts the time limit for the determination of the tax (Section 148 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
On the basis of its result, the tax may be levied ex officio.
Local investigation is an individual, time-limited act (one day) in which the tax administrator searches for evidence and searches premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging at the premises of tax subjects and other persons involved in the tax administration, in a place outside the premises of the tax administrator (e.g. at a tax entity, at a point of sale, on the way during transport).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and items, to take samples or to secure them.
On the basis of the results of the local investigation, the tax cannot be assessed separately, but the taxpayer may be required to submit a supplementary tax return (Article 145(2) of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
Checking EMCS traffic data is not a local investigation.
Orders for alcohol marking control tapes can only be placed by a registered person obliged to mark alcohol to the tax authorities of the locally competent place of marking and are made by means of intelligent forms which are automatically imported into the application of the register of alcohol markers.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the ordered amount of control tapes and orders the production.
He does not oversee the production of surveillance tapes.
Production is provided by the State Printing House, state enterprise.
The purchaser of the control tapes receives the control tapes from the tax administrator of the locally competent place of marking.
Ordering tobacco stickers to mark cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco fulfils the function of a tax return.
The value of the tobacco sticker corresponds to the amount of the tax liability, and the purchaser of the tobacco stickers is obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their removal from the tax authority.
The purchaser is obliged to calculate the value corresponding to the tax liability of the tobacco labels ordered in the order itself.
This period shall apply only if the value of the tobacco labels is guaranteed.
The order for tobacco stickers shall be made on a form established by the Ministry of Finance in writing or via a data box with the option of using intelligent forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is carried out by the State Printing House, a state-owned company.
The authorized tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (territorial workplace Kutná Hora), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, who further distributes them and further checks their transport, storage and use at the customers.
Tax claims include regular tax returns, supplementary and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco stickers, filed by tax subjects.
Excluded is not the declaration of tax under customs procedure on the basis of customs declarations and the claim for refund of: mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrol used in the course of a business other than for the production of heat or the propulsion of engines, mineral oils used for primary agricultural production.
The fines imposed include an administrative procedure for dealing with established infringements, involving a series of consecutive administrative actions. The International Exchange of Information on Tax Entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes place in the form of: a request for administrative cooperation, a response to a request for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, an event report, an inspection report.
Transport under the conditional exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States – the Czech Customs Office is the tax administrator of the receiving or sending tax warehouse or the authorized recipient.
Performance indicators in SR
Authorisation and registration for activities in Slovakia
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is mainly ensured by the customs offices and the excise tax department of the Customs and Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, whose procedure in the administration of excise duties is regulated by the individual laws on excise duties and the Tax Code.
These laws stipulate not only the scope of the authority for the CÚ and FR SR in the administration of excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax subjects in connection with the registration or payment of excise duty.
The biggest year-on-year increase in tax subjects (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, which was due to an increase in issued permits within tax warehouses, an increase in registrations of authorised receivers for re-admission and the registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation clarified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils, as well as the notification obligation if they are transported in bulk or in packages of more than 150 litres and 230 litres respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to control and procedure during transport to other goods, such as anti-knocking products, oxidation inhibitors, bituminous inhibitors, viscosity enhancers, anti-corrosion products.
A mandatory indication of the kinematic viscosity of lubricating oils has been introduced.
An approximation of the registration process with selected tax entities in the sense of national legislation in the Slovak Republic is given in the following parts of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a tax warehouse operator in all objects of excise duties, a person who wishes to operate a tax warehouse must simultaneously apply for registration and issue of a permit to operate a tax warehouse.
The resulting decision in the registration process is the certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, by which the tax warehouse operator acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA issues a tax warehouse operating permit which entitles the tax warehouse operator to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under the duty suspension arrangement.
In the event that the tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in more than one location, the tax administrator issues a separate tax warehouse operating permit for each tax warehouse.
The movement of excise goods under suspension of duty is monitored electronically through the EMCS.
A unique reference code is generated for each shipment, the so-called
The ARC code under which the traffic can be monitored online and therefore in real time.
If the tax warehouse operator is also the person authorised to distribute the spirit, he shall notify electronically to the CA the commercial name of the consumer packaging of the spirit, the volume and volume concentration of the spirit in the consumer packaging of the spirit and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free circulation, at the latest on the date of its release.
Registered Sender
A registered consignor is a special type of taxable person who cannot also be registered as a tax warehouse operator at the same time, even if he dispatches an excise item under a duty suspension arrangement after its release for free circulation.
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a registered consignor as part of all excise duties, a person who wishes to dispatch an excise item under a duty suspension arrangement after it has been placed under the ‘free circulation’ customs procedure must simultaneously apply to the CA for registration and authorisation to dispatch an excise item under that arrangement.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and at the same time also issues an authorisation to dispatch the excise goods under the duty suspension arrangement after their release for free circulation.
Growing spirit
The basic task for the operation of the distillery distillery is to obtain a licence for the production of alcohol in the distillery factory from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the authorisation from the Ministry alone does not entitle the holder of the authorisation to operate the distillery.
In order to operate a distillery, a person must submit to the CA an application for registration and the issue of a certificate of registration of the distillery operator.
The CA issues a registration certificate for the relevant excise duty, which also entitles the operator of the distillery to produce ethyl alcohol in the distillery.
The purpose of the distillery is to provide services to growers.
Growing liquor cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislature allows a reduced tax rate of 50% of the basic tax rate, i.e. 540 €/hl, to be applied to alcohol produced in the distillery.
The reduced rate of duty shall apply to ethyl alcohol produced in a distilled distillery up to a maximum of 43 litres per producer and his household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year and it is therefore possible to apply a reduced rate of duty to the ethyl alcohol produced more than once in one calendar year, since the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
This is the production of ethyl alcohol outside the suspensive regime, which means in practice that the ethyl alcohol produced is in free circulation for tax purposes.
The grower pays the distiller not only the excise duty and value added tax, but also the price for the services provided.
The grower's distillery shall issue the grower with a removal order, which shall serve not only as proof of the origin and method of acquisition of the alcohol, but also of payment of excise duty.
The transport of ethyl alcohol thus produced is not subject to monitoring by the tax authorities.
Consumer packaging importer
National legislation allows persons intending to import consumer packages of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country in the course of their business and to place them in free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The importer of consumer packaging does not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA issues him with a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate entitles the importer to import consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol or consumer packaging of cigarettes from the territory of a third State.
At the same time, before issuing the control stamps, it must lodge a tax guarantee equal to the amount of tax attributable to the quantities of ethyl alcohol or cigarettes it wishes to put into free circulation.
The importer of the consumer packaging must put into free circulation only the consumer packaging bearing the control mark.
For this reason, they must present to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the control marks exported to the territory of the third State.
On importation, the importer shall be obliged to have the number of control marks imported back from the territory of the third State certified by the customs office of importation.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer proceeds in the sense of customs legislation, where the customs debt also includes the amount of excise duty.
In the event of release for free circulation of the consumer packaging, the tax security lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
Where the importer of a consumer packaging of spirit is also the person authorised to distribute the spirit, he shall notify electronically to the CA the commercial name of the consumer packaging of the spirit, the volume and volume concentration of the spirit in the consumer packaging of the spirit and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free circulation for tax purposes, at the latest on the date of its release.
Seller of consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of ethyl alcohol in free tax circulation and eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for sellers of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a sales licence must apply to the CA for a licence and fulfil the legal conditions (business licence; good repute in relation to intentional economic offences; has not had its sales licence withdrawn for 10 years; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As the goods are packaged for consumption in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of those goods.
An invoice, for example, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove how the consumer packaging of the alcohol is purchased.
The holder of the authorisation shall keep, for each establishment, for each calendar month, a record of the number of units of alcohol wrapped for consumption, the number of units of alcohol wrapped for consumption, the stock of alcohol in alcohol wrapped for consumption on the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of packages of alcohol accepted and issued.
The holder of the authorisation shall be obliged to purchase the alcohol in consumer packaging or otherwise to purchase it in the course of business only from the person authorised to distribute it.
Distributor of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free circulation and eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute, the distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a distribution authorisation must apply to the CA for a distribution authorisation.
The applicant must fulfil the statutory conditions (trade licence for a commercial trade; a storage area exceeding 200 m2; an annual turnover of at least €100,000 from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol or a paid-up capital of at least €100,000; a minimum of 10 employees; has no arrears vis-à-vis the customs office; has no arrears in compulsory contributions; good repute in relation to intentional economic offences; has not had its authorisation to sell withdrawn for 10 years; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As the goods are packaged for consumption in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of those goods.
An invoice, for example, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation, is sufficient to prove how the consumer packaging of the alcohol is purchased.
The holder of a distribution authorisation shall keep, for each establishment, for each calendar month, a record of the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol accepted, the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol on the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol accepted and issued.
The holder of the distribution authorisation shall be obliged to purchase the alcohol in consumer packaging only from another person authorised to distribute it.
The person authorised to distribute shall report the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel Seller
In order to monitor fuel in free circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely the fuel vendor.
There is no specific regulation governing petrol stations in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
That is why petrol stations are incorporated in national legislation as fuel sellers.
A person wishing to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free tax circulation in the course of a business activity in the tax territory is required to apply to the CA for a sales licence before commencing the sale and to provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with a suitable verified measuring device enabling the quantity of mineral oil to be measured at reception and at issue, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the seller of the fuel is a tax warehouse operator, authorised consignee or registered consignor, the CA will also issue an authorisation to sell the fuel to automatically registered persons.
The fuel vendor is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep a record of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG in a calendar month and also to notify the CA of the new fuel supplier (distributor).
A fuel vendor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of those goods.
However, when the fuel is delivered by means of a car tank, the distributor prints a so-called stationary from the measuring device installed in the car tank when the fuel is pumped to the dealer.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the vehicle assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
An invoice, for example, which also contains the fuel distributor number allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove how the fuel was acquired.
In the exercise of fiscal supervision of mineral oils, the tax authority in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion connected with the transport of this type of goods.
Above all, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks during transport, so hauliers use secondary roads, bypassing the toll collection system because of the more difficult monitoring of actual traffic.
The transport of mineral oils in converted double-bottomed tanks is also carried out.
It is often the case that illegal traffic is accompanied by a vehicle which reports possible mobile patrols to the haulier in order to change the route and avoid a roadside check.
Fuel is also mixed with light fuel oils or waste oils.
Fuel distributor
In order to monitor fuel in free circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of taxpayer, namely the fuel distributor, has been introduced.
A person who wishes to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation in the tax territory in the course of a business activity shall, before distribution begins, apply to the customs office for a distribution authorisation and provide proof that the storage facility is verified and equipped with an appropriate verified measuring device, as well as a list of suppliers and customers.
The fuel distributor is required, among other legal obligations, to keep a separate account for each establishment of the petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold in a calendar month.
A fuel distributor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
A fuel distributor may sell in the tax territory only to a fuel distributor, a registered person or a fuel consumer.
However, when delivering fuel by means of a car tank, the distributor prints a so-called stamp from the measuring device embedded in the car tank to the fuel seller or to the fuel consumer when the fuel is pumped.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the vehicle assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
As the fuel is in free circulation for tax purposes, no accompanying document is required for the transport of the goods.
An invoice, for example, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor or registered person, allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove the method of acquiring the fuel.
Fuel Consumers
Fuel consumers have a special place in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation for his own consumption in the tax territory and stores that mineral oil in a storage facility of 15 000 litres or more shall be required to notify the customs office no later than before the first placing in the storage facility.
Consumers of fuel shall be entered in the register by the customs office.
In addition to the legal facts, the latter must indicate the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
Storage equipment must be verified and fitted with a measuring device enabling the quantity of propellant to be measured at reception and dispensing (gauge, measuring rod).
The tank shall meet technical standards.
Fuel consumers must purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport.
However, when the fuel is delivered by means of a car tank, the distributor prints a so-called stamp from the measuring device installed in the car tank when the fuel is pumped to the consumer.
That document shall contain, in addition to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the vehicle assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
An invoice, for example, which also contains the fuel distributor number allocated by the tax authorities, is sufficient to prove how the fuel was acquired.
In the exercise of fiscal supervision of mineral oils, the tax authority in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion connected with the transport of this type of goods.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer in the course of the business and fulfils the legal conditions.
Provided that the statutory conditions are met, a small independent brewery may apply a reduced rate of tax, i.e. EUR 2,652 per hl/per cent of the volume of actual alcohol content.
The annual production of beer is limited to quantities of up to 200 000 hl of beer.
As the beer is produced outside the suspensive regime, the transport does not require an accompanying document as it is in free circulation for tax purposes.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, they are small family businesses that also operate restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own-produced beer for sale.
Administrative tasks in Slovakia
This sub-chapter describes the performance of tax supervision of the administration of excise duties for selected tax entities in the sense of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The biggest year-on-year increase in administrative operations (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, due to more EMCS traffic.
On the contrary, the biggest decrease was recorded in 2014, by up to 4.3%, which was due to fewer completed tax inspections and fewer filed tax returns.
That decrease concerned legislative changes.
Tax controls
By carrying out tax audits, the CA identifies or verifies the facts decisive for the correct determination of the tax.
When performing a tax audit, the employees of the CA are required to produce a tax audit mandate which includes, among other things, the purpose and subject of the audit and the scope of the audited tax years.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period can be one month, but also more tax periods.
The extent of audited tax periods is determined by the CA.
The tax inspection begins with the writing of the report on the commencement of the tax inspection.
The CA will confirm receipt of the documents.
The CA is obliged to return the borrowed documents within 30 days from the completion of the tax audit.
The CA employee shall draw up a report of the tax inspection.
If the tax inspection reveals a difference in the sum that the audited taxpayer should have paid, reported or claimed a refund, the CA shall, together with the protocol, also send the audited taxpayer a letter of formal notice to comment on the findings in the report.
The tax inspection shall end on the date of receipt of the report.
The time limit for carrying out a tax audit shall be no more than one year from the date of its initiation.
Tax inspections of registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once before the date of expiry of the right to determine the tax, which is 5 years.
DG SR issued an internal management act which modified the above deadlines due to the uniform procedure of the tax administration in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
Local investigation
Local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator, in which it searches for evidence, examines and ascertains facts that are necessary for the purposes of tax administration.
The local investigation is recorded by the CA employee and a copy is given to the taxpayer.
In carrying out a local investigation, the CA employee has the right to unrestricted access to land, operational buildings, rooms and locations, including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The accounting for the quantity of ethyl alcohol produced shall be established by means of a local investigation.
The established facts are the basis for carrying out a tax audit.
Also in the course of local investigations, the CA is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the item.
DG SR issued an internal management act regulating the performance of tax supervision and local investigations for individual subjects of excise duties in order to unify the procedures of the tax administration.
Permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1 May 2004, there was also a change in the administration of excise duties.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in the administration of excise duty on alcohol, the improvement of the business environment in the area and the introduction of legislative instruments for more effective suppression of the grey economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in connection with the administration of excise duties.
One of the measures introduced by the new legislative amendment was not only the transfer of the excise tax administration from the tax authorities to the customs authorities, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administration to be present in the alcohol tax warehouse.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation defines exhaustively that it is only possible to receive, issue, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse in the presence of an employee of the CA.
This shall not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or dispatches ethyl alcohol only in a consumable container of ethyl alcohol.
At the same time, the CA is obliged to secure employees in the tax warehouse in order not to restrict the receipt, supply, production or processing of alcohol.
The tax warehouse operator is obliged to provide working environment conditions for CA employees.
On the basis of the contract concluded with FR SR for the premises provided, the CA pays the tax warehouse operator the rental costs on a monthly basis.
In a tax warehouse for the production, processing or storage of ethyl alcohol, the production facilities for the storage of ethyl alcohol must be adapted so that the quantities of ethyl alcohol produced, processed ethyl alcohol and ethyl alcohol stored, including the stocks of ethyl alcohol and the alcohol contained therein, can be ascertained at any time.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Where ethyl alcohol is not accepted, issued, produced or processed in a tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee and shall secure that area by means of a customs office seal.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often, as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators use a legal option within the meaning of Act No 467/2002 Coll. on the production and marketing of ethyl alcohol and use the production facilities for the production of ethyl alcohol in the distillery for cultivation burning and also for the purposes of the distillery for distillates, which must be a tax warehouse.
Approximately 250 customs officers provide permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
Issuing of vouchers for the collection of alcohol control stamps
The basic act for the collection of control stamps is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration sampling number and to issue a voucher for the collection of control stamps for ethyl alcohol.
Alcoholic beverages, which are ethyl alcohol, are goods of Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength exceeding 1,2 % vol.
The control mark is intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
A sealed container filled with ethyl alcohol intended for direct human consumption is considered to be a consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Consumer packaging falling within CN codes 2207 and 2208 may be put into free circulation in the tax territory only if it bears a control mark.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorised consignee and the importer of the consumer packaging, who will place it in free circulation for tax purposes, may mark the consumer packaging.
The control mark shall contain, inter alia, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical character. The identification number shall contain the registration number (1st-6th digit), the volume of ethyl alcohol (7th-11th digit) and the volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer packaging (12th-14th digit).
Original alcohol control mark model:
The CA shall assign the registration number to each purchaser of the control mark separately.
Only a control mark, the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of the consumer packaging, the volume concentration of the alcohol in the consumer packaging and the customer's control mark, may be used to indicate the packaging of the alcohol for consumption.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced a new information system for inspection marks.
The aim of the new information system for control stamps was to simplify and computerise the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control stamps for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee, the importer of the consumer packaging and the consignee (buyer) of the alcohol may mark the consumer packaging of the alcohol.
A purchaser of control stamps who wishes to collect control stamps under the ‘new system’ must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of control stamps is obliged to apply for their issue, to notify data resulting from national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control stamps.
The number of pieces of control stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
The tax administrator also communicates with the customers of control stamps via the electronic control stamp system, especially when notifying the number of control stamps that the buyer of control stamps can remove, or when determining the date of receipt of control stamps by the buyer of control stamps in the printer.
The purchaser of control stamps is obliged to deposit funds corresponding to the price of control stamps into the tax administrator's account before taking over the control stamps, which he can collect and the quantity of which is notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the check mark takes into account the amount of printer compensation. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice is entitled to print the inspection marks.
FR SR performs tax supervision over the handling of control stamps and their disposal in the printing works.
The FR SR is obliged to ensure the presence of a member of the staff of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling control stamps.
FR SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the customer of control stamps in the printer.
Check stamps can only be removed at the printer from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of control marks for tobacco products
The purchaser of the control mark must ask the CA to assign a registration number and issue a voucher for the collection of the control mark.
Consumer packs of cigarettes may be put into free circulation for tax purposes only if they bear a control mark.
It is only possible to mark consumer cigarette packs with a control mark in a company that produces cigarettes.
Only a tax warehouse operator, a beneficiary or an importer of tobacco products who wishes to place tobacco products in free circulation in the tax territory may be a purchaser of control marks.
Only a control mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of cigarettes, the particulars of which correspond to the relevant price of the cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the package, the length of the cigarettes, the character of the valid tax rate and the registration take-off number.
Consumer packs of cigarettes may be sold for final consumption only at the price indicated on the control mark.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced a new information system for inspection marks.
The aim of the new information system for control marks was to simplify and computerise the system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control marks for the marking of consumer packages of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A purchaser of control stamps who wishes to collect control stamps under the ‘new system’ must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of control stamps is obliged to apply for their issue, to notify data resulting from national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control stamps.
The state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice is entitled to print the inspection marks.
FR SR performs tax supervision over the handling of control stamps and their disposal in the printing works.
The FR SR is obliged to ensure the presence of a member of the staff of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling control stamps.
FR SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the customer of control stamps in the printer.
Check stamps can only be removed at the printer from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
A tax warehouse operator or an importer of tobacco products may mark consumer tobacco packages with a control mark.
A tax warehouse operator, importer of tobacco products or authorised consignee may mark consumer packages of cigars or cigarillos with a control mark.
Only the control mark shall be used to indicate the consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos, the particulars of which correspond to the character of the validity of the rate of excise duty.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes may be marked with a control mark only in the undertaking which manufactured them.
The number of pieces of control stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
Within three working days at the latest, the CA shall electronically notify the purchaser of the control stamps of the number of control stamps which he may withdraw, the price of the control stamps and the account number of the FR SR.
The CA may reduce the number of pieces of inspection stamps ordered if there are circumstances on the basis of which it can reasonably be assumed that a tax infringement may occur.
FR SR will determine the date of receipt of control stamps by the purchaser of control stamps, but no later than within 10 days.
The date of receipt of the control stamps shall be notified by the Slovak Ministry via the electronic control stamp system to the purchaser of the control stamps.
Surveillance stamps are issued by the tax office exclusively in the printing works, but only after the receipt of the funds corresponding to their price to the relevant account indicated in the customs office electronic notification.
The purchaser of control marks is obliged to keep a separate register of control marks in the electronic system of control marks for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Pursuant to Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the ELO and SPD systems unit of the Excise Department of the Slovak DG is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information following a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent financial authorities.
These are, in particular, requests for verification of bodies within the excise administration, requests for information concerning the administration of excise duties, as well as requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications shall take place in electronic form within the EMCS.
The following actions are included in administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on excise administration, request for confirmation of registration in the SEED); response to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; check report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Authorisation and registration
In the Slovak Republic, tax warehouses for alcohol are subject to permanent tax supervision, in the Czech Republic this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administrator through a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are tax warehouses, in the Slovak Republic they are only registered by the tax authorities.
In Slovakia, there is a registered consignor institute, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In the Slovak Republic, with a reduced rate of excise duty on ethyl alcohol, 43 litres can be burned in the case of cultivation burning.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of tax on ethyl alcohol can only be applied to 30 litres.
A distillery in the Slovak Republic must be authorised not only by the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also by the tax authorities.
In the Czech Republic, only the Ministry of Agriculture allows distilled spirits.
In Slovakia, besides the tax warehouse operator, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol is also carried out by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Authorisation of the importer shall be subject to registration of the applicant with the excise authorities.
In the Czech Republic, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol does not require any special permission from the tax administrator.
In Slovakia, the sale of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol is subject to the issuance of a tax authority permit for the seller.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep records of, among other things, purchases and sales.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for final sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of alcohol by the trade licensing office; The final seller does not keep any special records.
In the Slovak Republic, the seller of the fuel must have permission from the tax authorities to sell it.
National legislation in Slovakia does not regulate any special regulation of petrol stations, all activities related to petrol stations are regulated only in the Excise Tax Act on Mineral Oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by a special law on fuel, but the tax administrator does not issue any permit for the sale of fuel.
Gas stations are registered and a list of them is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In Slovakia, it is not technically possible to obtain a list of petrol stations from the financial management system.
In SR, the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities has increased significantly since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits decreased significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of a deposit for fuel distributors.
Administrative tasks
In the Slovak Republic, substantive legislation stipulates the obligation to exercise tax control over selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified in an internal management act issued by the Slovak Ministry of Finance due to the application of the uniform procedure of tax administrators in the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, substantive legislation does not regulate the obligation to carry out tax inspections; procedural law only provides for the possibility to carry out inspections at the latest by the deadline for tax assessment.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax inspections and local investigations carried out in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is the fact that the internal management act of the Slovak Ministry of Finance specifies in which cases and within what time limits the tax administrator must carry out a tax inspection, while in the Czech Republic the correctness of the declared amount of excise duty or its refund is verified mainly by a local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative operations in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 as a result of an increase in the number of EMCS traffic and also as a result of an increase in the number of submitted tax returns.
In SR, the number of administrative operations showed a slightly increasing trend between 2012 and 2015, which was influenced by the increasing number of EMCS traffic and the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the numbers of comparable permits and the registration of tax entities were reflected in the different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period.
In Slovakia, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds of the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for approximately the same number of administrative operations.
From this it can be concluded that the SR is more focused on carrying out administrative operations by the tax authorities, e.g. carrying out physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, emphasis is placed more on remote surveillance, e.g. tracking devices, immediate data transmission via a web interface and risk analysis.
Electronicisation of administrative procedures
Electronicization of administrative operations in the Czech Republic
The tax return can be filed via the data box.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced the so-called interactive forms of tax returns, which, however, can no longer be processed automatically.
The data must also be credited to the personal tax account of the taxpayer.
The benefit is a reduction in the error rate of the submitted tax returns (DAPs), which saves the actions of the tax administrator related to the procedure for corrections of erroneously filed DAPs.
The DG is working on a new application for electronic processing of DAP.
Smart forms can also be used to: submit tax or business registration applications and notifications of data changes, claim refund rights, fulfil reporting obligations for handling special mineral oils, handling raw tobacco and fulfilling biofuel obligations.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax subjects in the information system ORO WebClient, which is available for registered entities for registration by the tax administrator of specified data.
Transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the conditional exemption regime must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transport of selected products in free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic may always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, a document exempting them from excise duty, a decision of the customs office to place selected products under a customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision on the assessment of excise duty.
The required content of the data is determined by law.
In order to facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to the data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
The JIK serves the purpose of control by the customs authorities on the way and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
For the largest operator of the tax warehouse of fuel in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of fuel into free tax circulation, CS ČR has on-line access to the electronic registration system, into which the entity automatically stores the issued tax documents.
CS ČR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for registration and monitoring of transport of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should make use of 70% of the current functional EMCS specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for both declarants and customs officers.
It will also be linked to the Global Guarantee Scheme, the Tax Entity Register or the Risk Analysis System.
The system should provide an overview of traffic in free circulation between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of documentary evidence without registration and the sharing of serial numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure of recording the transport of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in misuse of the simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronization of administrative operations in the Slovak Republic
In the administration of excise duties, the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic uses electronic communication when monitoring the movement of goods in the EMCS system under the conditional exemption regime, check marks, filing of tax returns and also when registering and registering tax entities.
One-way electronic communication between tax subjects and the tax administrator was also introduced in 2014, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
In the framework of electronic communication, the taxpayer has access to a personal internet zone, the so-called electronic personal mailbox, which is designed for communication with the financial administration, after entering the access data.
Within this zone, the taxpayer has access to an electronic mailroom through which he submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents relating to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication via the personal internet zone does not concern all tax subjects.
National legislation defines tax entities that are obliged to communicate electronically with the tax administrator.
These are mainly VAT payers, tax advisers representing the tax entity and lawyers representing the tax entity.
During the audit, the SAO of the Slovak Republic also addressed the issue of the scope of computerisation of the administration of excise duties.
These were only fully electronic transactions, namely tax returns and electronic communication within ELO.
Apart from EMCS transport, there has been an increase in the computerisation of selected comparable administrative operations, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In the Slovak Republic, the fully computerised processing of the tax return is already in place, from its submission to the registration of the tax liability.
In the Czech Republic, electronic processing of tax returns is not set.
In the Czech Republic, it is possible for tax subjects to insert on the website mandatory documents for individual transport operations in free tax circulation.
In the future, the declaration of transport in free tax circulation in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system is being prepared.
Evaluation
The system of reporting of transport in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thus eliminating transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of the legislation.
This can be recommended as good practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to good practice in Slovakia in the field of electronic tax returns, the SAO of Slovakia and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend completing the electronic processing of tax returns in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organisational structure and staffing in the area of excise duties
The organization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has undergone major changes.
Organizational arrangement of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic since 1 January 2013 consists of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
The DG is the accounting unit for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out the comprehensive administration of excise duties since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
CS ČR also performs:
(a) control:
ശശ in the field of road transport (weighing of trucks, payment of road user charges, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and in matters of international passenger transport),
ശശ waste and packaging material management,
ശശ the safety of imported food,
ശശ in the field of consumer protection and protection of intellectual property rights,
ശശ employing foreigners,
b) Customs administration – a comprehensive application of customs legislation, trade policy measures and formalities for the import and export of goods;
(c) the collection and recovery of pecuniary payments imposed by other public authorities under shared management;
(d) activities of the police authority (designated customs authorities) in proceedings concerning offences committed in breach of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administrator.
Although the scope of competences (concurrent control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are economies of scale as the public administration does not have to spend the costs for the status of the control group for each subject of control separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden of the auditees is reduced by the re-inspection.
10 Since 1 December 2016, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic also exercises powers to verify compliance with obligations in the registration of sales (Section 2(2) of Act No. 112/2016 Coll., on the Registration of Sales) and, since 1 January 2017, to supervise compliance with the Act and the conditions of operation of gambling, including the imposition of penalties (Section 116 of Act No. 186/2016 Coll., on Gambling).
Within the project Modernization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-stage structure to two-stage structure with effect from 1 January 2013, while the central link of the procedure (Customs Directorates) was abolished.
The DG spent about CZK 51 million on the project (i.e. about €2,031,000).
CS CR since 1 January 2013 consists of the DG and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competences are determined by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial offices.
The territorial offices are the internal organisational units of the customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is authorised by decree to establish and abolish territorial offices and determine their material scope.
The legislation does not provide for any competence for the territorial workplace; The territorial offices shall exercise the powers of the customs office on its behalf.
Organizational structure until December 31, 2012
Organizational structure from 1. 1. 2013
Until 31 December 2012, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the DG, eight DGs and 58 CA units (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 departments and units.
As of 1 January 2016, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the DG and 51 departments in the CA and their territorial offices, as well as by eight departments of the legal department of the DG and by the CA departments providing mobile supervision, i.e. about 60 posts.
The costs of CS ČR most significantly affect wage expenditure.
As a result of the reorganisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there were no savings in staff resources.
The main processes are carried out by customs officers in service under the Law on the service of members of the security forces.
The possibility to reduce the numbers of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, because according to the provisions of Section 42(1) of Act No. 361/2003 Coll., on the employment relationship of members of the security forces, they can be dismissed from the service only in cases exhaustively defined.
Reduction of posts due to organisational changes in the security corps is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure that the members are assigned appropriate posts within the corps, or to provide posts in another security corps (e.g. the Police of the Czech Republic, the Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise it will transfer them to the reserve for the temporarily non-attached, in which the members of the security forces are entitled to 80% of the average service income according to the law.

Organizational arrangement of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic
As part of the 2012-2016 programme declaration, the Government of the Slovak Republic has set as one of its priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS programme, which will secure additional budgetary resources by harmonising the collection of taxes, duties and levies and by curbing tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic into the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the creation of the financial administration.
The Slovak Ministry of Finance was established on 1 January 2012 by Act No. 333/2011 Coll., on State Administration Authorities in the Field of Taxes, Fees and Customs, as amended, as a budgetary organization which has its seat in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the State Budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
FR SR, CÚ and the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No 199/2004 Coll., the Customs Act and amending and supplementing certain Acts, as amended, are customs authorities when they perform tasks according to customs regulations.
Within the meaning of Act No. 333/2011 Coll., on State Administration Authorities in the Field of Taxes, Fees and Customs, as amended, together with the Tax Authorities form the Financial Administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competent Centre for Financial Operations, the tax authorities, the Tax Office for selected tax entities, tax office branches, tax office contact points, customs offices, branches of customs offices (branch of the Czech Tax Office, branch of the Czech Tax Office combined, branch of the Czech Customs Office) and customs office stations.
The main mission of the Slovak Ministry of Finance is the effective collection and administration of taxes and duties, i.e. also excise duties, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the Slovak Ministry of Finance is the President of the Financial Administration, who is appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The president of the financial administration is responsible to him for the activities of the entire financial administration and therefore also for the activities of the Slovak Ministry of Finance, which he manages and represents in full.
Organizational Structure of the Slovak Ministry since 1. 1. 2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in the territory of the Slovak Republic, in addition to the branches of customs offices (38 branches) and stations of customs offices (18 stations), the excise department (9 departments) and the legal department (9 departments) also provide excise activities and processes.
