Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In the framework of the organisational structure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic, 74 organisational units with a total number of 1 300 employees were involved in the administration of excise duties in 2015 in addition to the Slovak Ministry of Finance; These services manage almost 48 000 tax entities.
Within the organisational structure In 2015, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic dealt with the administration of excise duties by approximately 60 organizational units with a total number of 1 011 employees, which are managed by approximately 114 000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual activities of the administration of excise duties is divided among several personnel independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is addressed through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax declaration, tax inspection) in the field of administration of excise duties is divided between the department of excise duties and the branch of the customs office, within which the agenda is often dealt with by the same employees of the tax administrator.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, approximately one third of the number of tax subjects in the total number of employees in the field of administration of excise duties is compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the impact of the higher number of employees on the efficiency of administration of excise duties is not clear.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products, the purpose of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information on the transport and to carry out the prescribed checks, to facilitate the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty.
When implementing the scheme, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of the EP and Council Decision allows the inclusion in the EMCS of a national specification, a national database forming part of the system and such hardware or software as the Member State considers necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionality of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by a system of registration of selected products (EVV), which was operated from May 2004 until the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously updated with European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
The so-called Customs Module and the Declarant Module were introduced in the Czech Republic.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
In addition to the Community system, in the Czech Republic the EMCS system monitors shipments under the conditional tax exemption regime initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The system provides for the automatic transmission of information to the Registry of Tax Entities following the approval of the notification of the receipt of a consignment intended for a single receipt by the authorised consignee, followed by the invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including sending replies with attachments in any format and providing translations.
It is also possible to accept the manual export termination report in the ECS (in the EU, only the transmission of the automatically generated report is implemented).
The risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
EMCS will not allow approval of e-AD or receipt notifications without a response from the competent customs authority to the risk profile (risk profile cannot be ignored).
The Declarant module is available for tax subjects free of charge, it takes the form of a web application into which the user logs in with a username and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with CS ČR.
Any action against the customs module EMCS shall be accompanied by a valid electronic signature in the declarant module EMCS.
The Declarant Module allows tax entities to directly record data on commenced and terminated transport operations under the conditional exemption regime, so that tax entities do not have to spend money to acquire the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module allow data to be read and stored offline (saving time for frequently used data), to fill in the data of the recipient based on the SEED ID check and to require mandatory completion of data that are optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows to block the securing of excise duty for each consignment sent from the Czech Republic in real time in the corresponding amount of taxable performance up to the time of termination of the transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS.
Without sufficient collateral, it is not possible from the EMCS declarant module to send the e-AD proposal to the CA of dispatch for approval.
Each guarantee has a unique number and contains the ARC of the transport (including the amount of the blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The tax entity can administer its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it can see the actual amount of the blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantee.
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The development of EMCS was realized on the basis of eight contracts with fulfilment from 2006 to 2017 in the total amount of CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. EUR 1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. EUR 1,640,401.10) excluding VAT between 2006 and the end of 2015.
During the audited period, expenditure amounting to CZK 14,545,454 (i.e. EUR 547,438.99) was spent on the EMCS system upgrade.
The amount spent on upgrading EMCS in the audited period and converted into one transport inserted into EMCS amounts on average to 16.49 CZK (i.e. 0.62 €), excluding national transport, this expenditure amounts to 24.40 CZK (i.e. 0.92 €) per transport between the Czech Republic and EU Member States.
EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four performance contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, a total amount of CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. €281,389.77) including value added tax was invoiced.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 per transport entered into the EMCS since 2010 is 6.18 CZK (i.e. 0.23 €).
The invoices for both development and technical support related to the national solution and led to the development of the EVV application, which was already operated by the DG before EMCS itself.
The invoices were paid under the programme financing from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of deliveries of services to other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor movements of excise goods between Member States under a duty suspension arrangement.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document – SAD, which was used before the system took effect, thus ensuring better control and management of traffic.
It has been introduced in the Slovak Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented by requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, the so-called ‘reference code’.
The ARC code under which the traffic can be monitored online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS
The EMCS provides for the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by those taxable persons who are authorised to use the EMCS, thereby greatly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The greatest development of functionalities occurred in 2011, when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The introduction of EMCS was implemented as an additional SysNeD application equipment module and therefore it is not possible to determine the exact cost of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of the EMCS was to replace a system based on paper-based transport administration.
The benefits of EMCS are a comprehensive overview of intra-EU transport between Member States from the notification of the start of the transport to the end of the transport – a significant reduction in administrative costs for tax administrations and tax subjects to process, transmit and archive documents.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, a national functionality was introduced into the EMCS system allowing monitoring of traffic in a conditional system between two locations in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, respectively.
In addition, automatic functionality of on-line monitoring and guarantee of excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
National functionality is also introduced, which monitors the risk of the taxpayer, virtually transportation, followed by a mandatory response from the tax administrator.
SR and the Czech Republic record a comparable number of intra-EU traffic in the EMCS system.
Expenditure spent in the Slovak Republic on upgrading this system, however, was €744,310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO SR obtained data from the Slovak Ministry on the upgrade of the EMCS system only for the period from 2011, even though the system was introduced and operated earlier.
Despite this, the expenditure spent on upgrading the EMCS system in Slovakia was €188,134.44 higher than the expenditure for introducing and upgrading the EMCS system in approximately ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
During the audited period, the volume of expenses related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in Slovakia in terms of one transport exceeds by 2.3 times the expenses of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
Cooperation between the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic met the objectives.
Both audit institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the system of administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in the two tax systems which affect the efficiency of the administration of excise duties.
In parallel, examples of good practice have been identified that could contribute to reducing tax fraud, which will become increasingly important as tax rates rise.
Procedures to reduce the cost of administering excise duties have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons, unless mutually coordinated due diligence checks are carried out with the tax administration.
In this respect, the role of supreme audit institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel inspection of the VAT administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Opening Word
The Lima Declaration of 1977 stresses that supreme audit institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled as far as possible.
Organisation The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers taxation to be one of the most important components of public revenue.
The VI EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 addressed the audit of public revenues carried out by the SAI.
The development of a specific strategy for the audit of public revenue is an important step towards optimising the control activities of the SAI.
This applies in particular to taxation as the largest source of public revenue most susceptible to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of another State's SAIs.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the revenues of many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs carrying out inspections in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation between themselves.
It was at the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea arose of carrying out an audit of the administration of value added tax (VAT) and the VIES system in the framework of the cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
This was followed by careful preparation, with both parties first having to familiarize themselves with the legal environment and procedures in the administration of VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was made for inclusion in the control programme.
Achieving an effective and efficient VAT administration is a long-standing challenge and individual Member States (in particular the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve the system, simplify and make the collection of VAT more transparent.
We believe that the results of our audit can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrations, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the VAT administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 – 2005 – 1215
Object of control:
(CZ) Administration of Value Added Tax after the Czech Republic's accession to the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the audit operation in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of value added tax after the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as the EU) connected with the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to exemption from value added tax on intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax, with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the above-mentioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
System of exchange of information on value added tax The auditing operation was carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as the BRH) in cooperation with each other on the basis of a contract concluded between the two auditing institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected business transactions between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as the German Federal Republic), the use of information obtained through international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of the VAT administration systems of both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the audits was prepared in accordance with the European Directive No. 31 for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards.
The audited period covered the period from 1.5.2004 to 31.12.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Parallel control in the area of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
Beyond the main point - the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 - the audit covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the audit included the legal situation in the area of international passenger bus transport and a comparison of some statistical data.
A comparison of the VAT administration systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-community transactions.
In Germany, taxpayers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different forms of registration cause problems, the playing field should be levelled across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International passenger bus transport.
In the Czech Republic, international passenger bus transport is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2).
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic taxpayers file VAT returns only for individual tax periods (months or quarters), in Germany taxpayers are obliged to file so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they have to file an annual VAT return.
Unlike the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of an obligation to submit VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
(4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic payers file summary reports at financial offices, in Germany payers file summary reports at the Customs Office.
The data from the recapitulative statements are therefore available to the tax authorities in the Czech Republic immediately after their submission.
The information from the recapitulative statements is only available to the German tax authorities after they have been processed into the CLO.
Combating VAT fraud requires up-to-date information on intra-community transactions to be available as soon as possible.
Monthly recapitulative reporting would shorten the time lag between the transaction date and the update of VIES data.
This would in turn allow a timely verification of the taxation in the acquirer's Member State (see 4.4).
However, this would require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for the submission of the recapitulative statement.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech Customs Office monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for information requests received.
The German CLO does not follow the elapsed time.
As a result, the German tax authorities dealt with a significantly lower percentage of applications received within the prescribed period.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a continuous alert (see 4.6).
(6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (RMS), which has both strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the SAO warned that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5).
As part of the cooperation, both SAIs examined selected cases of intra-community transactions carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, 31 cases of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their completion or suspicions of VAT evasion were examined using the Customs legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained through international cooperation to assess the VAT liability of the payers.
In these cases, the payers either improperly claimed the VAT exemption of the supply or failed to declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used because of different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases have been identified where payers have erroneously reported commercial transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the data in the VIES were incorrect and the tax administrations had to check these cases (see 6.).
Progress of control action
Progress of the audit operation in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and March 2007 by the State Budget Revenue Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited bodies were: the Ministry of Finance (hereinafter referred to as “MF”) and 10 financial offices – the Financial Office in Humpolec, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kadani, the Financial Office in Liberec, the Financial Office in Nymburk, the Financial Office in Otrokovice, the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 4, the Financial Office in Sokolov and the Financial Office in Třinec.
The audit conclusion from this auditing operation was approved by the SAO College on 23 April 2007.
Progress of the auditing operation in Germany
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and February 2007 by the Indirect Taxation Control Group and the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
The audit was part of the 2006 audit plan and was therefore notified to the Federal Ministry of Finance in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases selected by BRH and later selected by the SAO, BRH had to notify the audit to a number of federal states.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance and the CLO, the audit was carried out in the following federal states:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine-Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich - FÚ for corporations/legal entities (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich V, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg-Central (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-North (Hamburg-Nord) and Hamburg for large enterprises (Hamburg für Großund-Berlin, Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn (Frankfurt-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Bonn-Kössssssssssssssssss

Cooperation between the two audit institutions

Participants in these meetings became acquainted with the organisation of tax administrations, the legislation on VAT issues and the VAT administration system in both countries.
The topics of the test phase were agreed at a meeting held in May 2006.
The results of the test phase were evaluated at another joint meeting in August 2006.

The report on the results of the parallel controls of VAT administration between the Czech Republic and Germany was prepared at a working meeting in July 2007.
4. Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payees who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
According to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter "Act No. 337/1992 Coll."), a taxpayer, a taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person defined by law as a tax entity shall be considered a tax entity.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421 865 tax subjects were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
As of 1 December 2005, the number of tax entities registered for VAT increased to 457 590.
A taxable person who has his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic and whose turnover exceeds the amount of CZK 1 000 000 (EUR 33 575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months shall become a taxable person from the 1st day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (Article 94(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 235/2004 Coll.”).
Applications for registration must be submitted by that person within 15 days of the end of the month in which he/she exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow a taxable person to be registered so-called retrospectively in cases where the reason for registration is to exceed the legal registration limit.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with the right to deduct may become a taxable person even if he does not exceed the turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if he fulfils any of the other conditions specified in Act No.235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not fulfil any of the conditions laid down by law may apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
Delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator initiates the registration procedure according to Act No. 337/1992 Coll.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate on the VAT registration form the date from which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator will check the data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed registration application with all annexes.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall invite the taxpayer to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After verifying that the taxpayer fulfils the conditions for registration, the tax administrator issues a decision in the form of a certificate that the taxpayer is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (TIN).
The tax administrator shall indicate on the certificate the date of effect of the VAT registration and the frequency of the VAT tax period.
The tax period is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period is the calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year amounted to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and shall notify the tax administrator of this change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the TIN in the registration certificate is always constitutive and the taxpayer is obliged to state it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TIN contains the code ‘CZ’ and a tribal part consisting of a generic identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is a birth number, or another general identifier if a special law so provides, and for a legal person an identification number (Article 33(12) of Act No 337/1992 Coll.).
If a taxpayer has not fulfilled its registration obligation even at the request of the tax administrator, the local tax administrator shall register it ex officio without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issuance of an ex officio Registration Certificate, which is delivered to the taxpayer.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has obtained a business license is allocated a tax exempt number at the moment of its first registration for any tax.
The same VAT number is used by the taxpayer even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., which is effective from 1 January 2005, the tax administrator may, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, impose on the taxable person compensation of up to 10% of the total income or income for taxable transactions that this person has carried out without tax, for the period from the date on which he should have been a registered taxpayer by law to the date on which he became a registered taxpayer by decision of the tax administrator (provisions of Section 98, paragraph 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined is considered a tax payment (Section 98(3) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a penalty.
The cancellation of the VAT payer's registration when the statutory conditions are fulfilled is possible for two reasons:
1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover that does not reach the registration limit (Section 106(1) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer shall be entitled to apply for the deregistration at the earliest after 1 year from the effective date stated on the registration certificate.
2) Cancellation of registration "ex officio" (Section 106(7) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), if: a) the payer has not performed a transaction for 12 consecutive months without notice to the tax administrator, b) the payer has not fulfilled his obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Taxpayers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who carries out a transaction with a place of performance in the Czech Republic and is a person obliged to declare and pay tax on this transaction pursuant to § 108 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. (the so-called "non-established payer"), becomes a payer on the day of performance of the transaction.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the Tax Office for Prague 1 no later than the date of performance.
The application for registration must mention all the TIN allocated to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If a "non-established" payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Financial Office for Prague 1 will register it retroactively, because according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the taxpayer became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
In the case of retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires from tax entities proof that the transaction has been performed (invoices or explanatory letters).
If a "non-established" taxpayer applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable transaction takes place, then the Financial Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the transaction will take place.
As of 31 December 2004, 473 “non-established” payers were registered at the Tax Office for Prague 1, including 124 payers from Germany, and as of 31 December 2005, 951 “non-established” payers were registered, including 233 payers from Germany.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 106(9) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a “non-established” payer on 31 January of the following calendar year if no obligation to declare and pay the tax arose during the current calendar year.
The SAO's audit revealed that if a "non-established" payer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the statutory regulations at the time of filing the tax return, the tax office often does not have it available on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant to the possibility of cancelling the registration are known to the tax office later than 31 January, it is no longer possible to cancel the VAT registration of the "non-established" payer in the Czech Republic in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (Sections 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter ‘AO’), anyone carrying on a business is required to inform the municipal/municipal authority or the competent tax authority.
The deadline for submission of information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the Municipal/Municipal Office for the Financial Office.
If the tax office identifies an enterprise that has started but has not registered, the relevant tax office may register the payer ex officio – and retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-residents in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria laid down in Paragraph 2 of the German Law on VAT (the UStG).
That obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover which they generate.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax offices for entrepreneurs residing abroad.
For example, for those who have their registered office in the Czech Republic, the relevant Tax Office is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; As of 1 March 2006, a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
BRH found that these special tax offices often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As the work permits of employees from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
Those undertakings do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs laid down in Paragraph 2 of the UStG, since they are usually dependent on a single employer to determine their working hours and the way in which they carry out their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must fill in a questionnaire from the relevant tax office, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding for all tax offices in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by departments with a general focus, which are responsible for the assessment of taxpayers.
This form is used to carry out a risk assessment of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions follows certain rules:
The first three digits provide information on the relevant tax office, the next three (or four) provide information on the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are to distinguish the payers, the last being always the check-digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to engage in intra-Community trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an exempt intra-Community supply.
The Customs Office shall assign a VAT ID at the request of the trader if the trader is registered in Germany and has a VAT number.
The Customs Office will automatically assign VAT IDs to businesses when the payers include intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns.
The VAT ID structure is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
The registration of an entrepreneur may be revoked: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activity), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all marketing years) and 2. if the tax administration realises that he is no longer engaged in business activity.
The validity of the VAT identification number is normally linked to the validity of the VAT number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the Customs Office of the cancellation of the tax number so that the Customs Office can terminate the validity of the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (Paragraph 19(1) of the UStG), tax residents in Germany are not liable to pay VAT in the event of (1) that the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and (2) that it is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000 in the following year.
So-called small entrepreneurs (‘Kleinunternehmer’) are not entitled to invoice VAT to other entrepreneurs and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not liable to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that he will not apply Paragraph 19(1) of the UStG.
That declaration shall be binding on him for the following five years.
The trader can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For non-residents, there is the possibility of appointing tax representatives (Paragraph 22a of the UStG).
It is a prerequisite that they carry out only exempt commercial transactions and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who does not have to register for VAT.
Invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If a tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the specified limit, it has the possibility to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration process is standardized in Germany, but differences may occur as a result of different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the taxpayer is assigned a VAT number at the moment of his first registration for any tax.
In case the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same VAT number also in intra-community transactions.
In Germany, the tax number is assigned to the payer when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and the SAO found, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-community transactions.
On the other hand, the two-tier system allows for retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax office about their business.
This retroactive registration allows for a correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax period, in particular a precise estimate of VAT liability.
As different ways of registering cause problems, the playing field should be levelled across the EU.
The German Parliament has recently decided to introduce a Tax Identification Number (TIN).
The Federal Tax Office will assign the TIN at the birth of a natural person.
This TIN will be valid for the entire life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will apply for an economic VAT number, which will be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of the VAT ID.
Work on the implementation of the IT resource to manage the TIN has not yet been completed.
International passenger bus transport
Legislation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., with effect from 1 May 2004, the transport of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax.
That transport is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by traders who are registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return journey shall be considered as a separate journey.
If "non-established" tax subjects in the Czech Republic do not carry out other economic activities besides international bus transport of persons, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International passenger transport in the Czech Republic was exempt from VAT on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V, Chapter 5, paragraph 1, letter b), where it is stated:
‘For the purposes of Article 28(3)(b), the following shall be added: Pursuant to Article 2(b) of Directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt from value added tax international passenger transport under point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 28(4) of the Directive is fulfilled or until the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier. “
Description of legislation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in Article 3b(1) of the German VAT Act, the place of supply of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) is the route (i.e. the place) where the transport takes place.
The German tax system therefore makes no distinction between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable supply of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also makes no distinction between residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident taxpayer transports passengers via Germany, the part of the route that takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable supply of transport.
A non-resident taxpayer must declare his intention to provide passenger transport to the relevant tax office before performing his services in Germany.
The tax office registers this non-resident for tax purposes (cf. 4.1.2) and issues a special certificate for any bus or coach mentioned in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable supplies of transport in the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers operating in the passenger transport sector.
If the passenger transport is provided to a resident taxpayer who is liable for VAT, the non-resident taxpayer does not have to pay the VAT himself to the tax office.
Instead, the entity liable to pay the VAT to the tax office and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident taxpayer is the resident taxpayer who receives the services; This process is known as reverse charge and is in line with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition to the notification of the non-resident taxpayer and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have several means of assessing the correctness of the taxable supplies of passenger transport declared.
The Customs office's mobile inspection teams audit the certificates of buses licensed for foreign transport, which are used to transport passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile control groups send a control report to the relevant tax authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to require the bus driver to pay VAT before proceeding with the next transport.
A non-resident taxpayer may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may declare its intention to carry out an audit, which must take place in the office of the tax office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident taxpayer refuses to pay the amount of VAT charged in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If the VAT return or the non-resident taxpayer’s obligations are to be examined, BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour-intensive compared with the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable passenger transport services.
In particular, auditing the accounts of a non-resident taxpayer entails disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration has to audit foreign accounting, which means not only the need for foreign language knowledge, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of the tax resident, but this audit is limited to those passenger transport services carried out in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident taxpayer may not only accept the right to carry out checks which is the responsibility of his national tax authorities, but also the right to have an audit carried out by other Member States in which he carries passengers.
Moreover, in each Member State in which only one passenger transport service is carried out, the taxpayer is required to comply with all the tax obligations applicable to him in those Member States, in all the languages and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
Real taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore entails disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in the two countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the transport of persons between individual EU Member States, or between Member States and third countries, is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
If this transport is provided in Germany for the first time by a non-established payer, he is obliged to notify the relevant tax office in advance.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare taxable supplies of part of the transport in the tax return in Germany.
The implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three out of four Czech payers registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are in the passenger transport business.
Compared to the effort, tax revenue, if realised, is rather low.
Member States collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are subject to time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive outcome.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs for charging VAT, the supply of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the country where the transport begins or where the provider is based.
Such taxation would require an adaptation of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
VAT returns
Submission and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to submit a VAT return using the form prescribed by the MoF within 25 days after the end of the tax period, even if he has not become liable to tax, unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is due within the deadline for filing the VAT return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the importation of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., for which the tax due is determined by customs regulations.
If a repayable excess arises as a result of the assessment of the excess deduction, it shall be returned to the payer without request within 30 days of the assessment of the excess deduction.
The deadline is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings concerning the taxpayer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73(11) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., the right to deduct may be exercised in a regular VAT return at the latest for the last tax period of the calendar year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
After the expiry of that period, the right to deduct may continue to be exercised within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the right to deduct could have been exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible by submitting a supplementary VAT return.
The amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, allows the filing of a supplementary VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct could be exercised for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit a supplementary VAT return if (a) the sum of the corrections increases the tax liability, (b) he makes a correction in which the last known tax liability does not change, but only the data previously claimed by the taxpayer, (c) he makes a correction of the tax rate and amount pursuant to Section 49 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit a supplementary VAT return if the aggregated corrections reduce the tax liability.
The additional VAT return must be submitted by the payer by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The submission of VAT returns in electronic form can be done either via the Internet or on a technical data medium.
Internet submissions may be made as a submission with a data message bearing an advanced electronic signature or as a submission with a data message not bearing an advanced electronic signature.
In the case of submission with a data message without a guaranteed electronic signature, submission in written form is still required, i.e. delivery of the computer report to the tax administrator (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
The values of acquisitions of services are shown on specific lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The values of supplies of goods to other Member States to persons registered for tax in other Member States shall be compared with the data provided in the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech taxpayers.
The values of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with those obtained through the VIES system from the recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
A credibility test of VAT returns is carried out at the tax office under the ADIS system.
This test is automatic, as VAT returns cannot be assessed without a test.
The credibility test involves calculating the credibility criteria and evaluating the risk types of VAT returns.
Under Section 37(1) of Act No 337/1992, the tax office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply with a non-monetary obligation arising from this or a special tax law or imposed by a decision pursuant to this Act within a specified period of time.
Automated tax information system used by the FA for technical support of tax administration.
The SAO audit found that the tax authorities did not usually use the option to impose a fine on the payers for not filing VAT returns.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not liable for VAT are required to submit an annual tax return.
As a general rule, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which VAT is incurred (Paragraph 18(2) of the UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year, or if the business is a newly established business, the trader concerned is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if a refund of more than EUR 6 136 was made last year (Paragraph 18(2a) of the UStG).
VAT returns do not have to be submitted if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant VAT liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax year in which the VAT accrued.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FC.
There are no (statutory) time limits for processing tax returns and refunding excess VAT.
In order to obtain a timely refund, a security may be offered for the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Code provides for the possibility of extending that period (Paragraph 18(6) of the UStG).
Such an extension must be requested separately.
It allows the submission of a VAT return and the payment of the corresponding VAT liability one month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the trader must submit a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be submitted by 31 May of the following calendar year, has been registered with the tax office, the trader cannot correct the incorrect provisional VAT return, but only the annual VAT return.
The correction of the annual VAT return for or against the payer shall be possible during the following 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally only be corrected in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Taxpayers are obliged to submit preliminary VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule in order to avoid undue hardship.
The annual VAT return can be submitted on paper or via the Internet, with or without certification.
If it is carried out without certification, the payer must submit the return once more on paper with personal signatures.
If the payer fails to file a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late submission, a penalty payment (maximum 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000) may be imposed on the payer.
During a previous inspection, BRH found that the tax authorities often do not calculate this standard penalty.
In other cases where the tax authorities have imposed a fine, the amount has been assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard fine therefore fails to meet its objective of reducing the average delay, in particular when submitting the annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
The values of acquisitions of services are shown on specific lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate VAT return line.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted in paper form, a copy must be made either by scanner or by staff specifically authorised to do so.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically are immediately available to the tax office employee.
Once all the data are fed into the system, RMS staff will go through them and select cases that meet certain criteria.
The VAT returns collected must be checked by a tax office employee on the basis of a control report prepared by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration has to make a rough estimate of the amount of VAT the taxpayer has to pay, the estimated tax has to be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers file VAT returns within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
The tax period is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month, depending on the amount of the payer's turnover.
In Germany, taxpayers submit preliminary VAT returns, depending on their tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days after the end of a calendar quarter or a month.
By 31 May of the following year, taxpayers are required to file an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in the (monthly preliminary) tax returns by submitting a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the declared intra-community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the recapitulative statement is made;
– the Länder do not normally compare VIES data on intra-Community acquisitions of German taxpayers before the annual VAT return is processed.
In accordance with the registration (see 4.1.3), German taxpayers are required to file an annual VAT return regardless of the amount of their turnover.
This obligation enables the German tax authority to verify the maximum turnover limit for small businesses.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare the annual VAT returns with the direct tax returns and the final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from filed income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are obliged to submit VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of an obligation to submit tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The recapitulative statement (hereinafter referred to as “SH”) is submitted pursuant to the provisions of § 102 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. by a payer who has made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State.
Data on the value of supplied goods are always presented in Czech currency, broken down by individual tax entities with their VAT ID, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services provided shall not be included in the SH.
SH is filed by taxpayers with both monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days after the end of the period to the locally competent tax office.
Correction of erroneous data shall be performed in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
The incorrect data in the SH shall always be replaced by the data in the subsequent SH.
As well as tax returns, payers can submit SH in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not file the SH or subsequent SH and should have filed it under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator will invite him to file it and at the same time inform him of the consequences in the event of failure to file the SH or subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax administrator is entitled under Section 37 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll. to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for non-monetary obligations.
The SAO audit found that the tax authorities did not usually use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for non-compliance with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of filing the SH, there is insufficient incentive for tax subjects to fulfil their obligations, as the non-filing of the SH does not affect VAT liability.
The tax administrator is obliged according to § 102 paragraph 5 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. to check the data in the SH, or in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and to use the data for the determination of tax liability.
In case of inconsistency of the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (the payer with the monthly tax period) or the relevant (the payer with the quarterly tax period) VAT return, the tax administrator should verify the correctness of the declared tax obligation stated in the VAT return.
Incorrect data in the SH shall be corrected by the taxpayer himself or he may be required to do so by filing a subsequent SH.
The tax administrator will correct the data on the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
– the payer does not prove the data specified in the SH (or subsequent SH) and corrects them by filing a subsequent SH,
– the tax administrator proved that the data given by the payer in the SH or subsequent SH are not true.
By inserting a correction without submission of the subsequent SH by the payer, the tax administrator does not replace the submission of the tax entity, only modifies the data in the VIES database so that they are up-to-date, complete and accurate.
SH data shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They can only be sent and received by a national financial administration authority designated for cooperation with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic this function is fulfilled by the Ministry of Finance, Department of International Cooperation in VAT Administration (CLO).
O_MCTL is an automatic message received by the CLO from other Member States.
Contains all incorrect VAT IDs listed in the SH lines sent.
If the wrong VAT ID is used in one of the transferred normal lines of SH or subsequent SH, a record is made in the wrong VAT ID table.
The table contains the so-called "Notice of Doubt on VAT ID".
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare the VAT and indicate the values of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of the acquired goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return and in the value of the supplied goods as stated by the payers from other Member States in their SH are sent from Customs to the tax office for verification.
Tax authorities are obliged to investigate irregularities.
Three situations can arise:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant VAT return lines is lower than the value of the supply declared by EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator checks the accuracy of the data.
b) The difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects his SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech taxpayer himself files a supplementary VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax authority whether, despite this fact, it will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States, as stated by the Czech taxpayer in the relevant VAT return lines, is higher than the value of the delivered goods declared to the EU taxpayer.
Here too, it is at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the difference and explaining the causes of its occurrence, the tax administrator enters the result of the verification into the ADIS.
The results of the verification are transmitted back to the CLO.
The numbers of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for verification for each quarter of 2005 are shown in Chart No.1 (NB: MF).
Graph 1 above shows that the number of cases transmitted from the PRC to the tax authorities decreased for each quarter of 2005.
The number decreased significantly in the fourth quarter of 2005. The CLO increased the minimum threshold, inter alia with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT return data and EU data may not always be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error due to the fact that certain types of transactions may be reported to the SH in different ways in different EU Member States.
The most common reasons for irregularities in the values of reported transactions found at the audited financial offices are given in Table 1.
Submission and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intra-Community deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or engage in triangular transactions are required to file a quarterly SH listing intra-Community deliveries by recipients (Section 18a(1) UStG).
The SH must be filed by the 10th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this deadline is granted in the case of preliminary VAT returns, this also applies to the SH.
SH must be supplied to the CLO.
They must be submitted electronically from 1 January 2007.
Exemptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realise that incorrect information is included in the SH, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not file an SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of such a report.
This procedure includes: – a first reminder; – a second reminder with the threat of a fine/periodic penalty payment; and – the imposition of a periodic penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows fines of up to EUR 25 000 to be imposed (section 329 AO), the Customs Authority determines the fines in three steps, in amounts of EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a(1) No 5 of the UStG provides that payers act unlawfully if, intentionally or negligently, they fail to properly file the SH, file it incomplete, do not file it in time or if they fail to correct or correct the SH at all.
This offence can be punished by a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intra-community deliveries cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office, as the processing of SH is the sole task of the CLO.
SH data are only stored in the CLO system.
Therefore, the data from the SH are only visually available to the tax office after they have been processed into the CLO.
The deadlines for processing SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
SH data must be stored during the three months following the calendar quarter in question.
Where incorrect VAT IDs are entered in the SH of German payers, the CLO receives the O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
The CLO contacts a particular entrepreneur and asks for the correct information.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is referred to the competent tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
During the inspection, the BRH found that most traders had corrected the VAT ID at the request of the Customs Office.
However, the challenge, the threat and the imposition of three additional fines take up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the competent tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The tax office refused to exempt declared intra-community supplies in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file a corrected VAT ID with the Customs office, as the tax authorities cannot correct the VIES data themselves.
BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the submission of the corrected SH, so the payers often did not comply with the request.
In view of the fact that the Customs Office does not have access to the VAT return data, the comparison of the data on the supply of goods declared in the VAT return and in the SH will not take place before the submission of these data to the Customs of the other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied when preparing the VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed into a CLO.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then submitted to the relevant Member States.
These data are used for the purpose of control of acquisition by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, they are checked by the CLO on the basis of a comparison with data from previous calendar quarters.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is generated and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is produced at a later stage and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the assessment procedure shall subsequently check these data against intra-Community data.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State shall submit SH within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax office.
The tax authorities process the SH and transmit the data to the CLO.
The values of the supplies of goods to another Member State, indicated by the payers in the SH, are compared at the tax offices with the values of the supplies of goods to another Member State, indicated by these payers in their VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made an intra-community delivery are obliged to submit a quarterly SH by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers submit to the CLO, since 1 January 2007 in electronic form.
The information from the SH is only available to the tax authorities after it has been processed into the CLO.
Taxpayers from the Czech Republic and Germany list only the supply of goods in the SH, the provision of services is not mentioned in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the incorrect lines submitted by SH on their own.
As a result of this limited access to the German VIES data, the incorrect VAT ID was not corrected even if the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FÚ.
The German tax administration does not compare the data on intra-Community supplies contained in the VAT return of the German taxpayer with his SH.
Differences between the data of these two statements are usually not detected before the German CLO provides the VIES data to other Member States.
In view of the BRH findings, it is clear that a comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in the VIES.
Data on the delivery of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT returns.
The comparison shall be carried out by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are transmitted to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in the tax returns of the payers.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intra-community acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax administration controls the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions of other payers only if the RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is designated for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities of the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of RMS.
Combating carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if payers submit a monthly SH.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, because most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file monthly VAT returns – and SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, the filing of the SH may be combined with the filing of a VAT return.
However, the obligation to administer the SH monthly would cause more temporal discrepancies between the reporting of intra-community delivery and intra-community acquisition and could increase the flow of data between the different CLOs.
In 2006, the German Federal Government considered a general provision for monthly SHs.
Its implementation has failed due to doubts of the federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of VIES data to other Member States' CLOs could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly SH and monthly data reporting obligations were to be effective, the monthly VIES update would require a European monthly SH standard.
Statistical data on delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In terms of foreign trade, Germany is the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intra-community transactions in goods between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of incorrect VAT numbers or VAT IDs contained in O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The figures show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
International Information Exchange Level 3
Implementation of international information exchange in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States regarding intra-Community commercial transactions and the payers who carried out those transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between two basic categories of exchange of information, namely exchange of information upon request and exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information on request takes the form of so-called requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "GIs"), using standardised SCAC forms.
Tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their GI, or replies to the received GI, through the Financial Directorate to the Customs Office, which ensures the translation of the information provided on the standardized SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The Customs Office also ensures the receipt of GIs from other Member States and the replies to the dispatched GIs, their translation into Czech and their distribution to the locally competent tax authorities for processing.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 provides for a maximum time limit of 3 months from receipt of the request for the discharge of the EIT.
The SAO audited all SAIs submitted between the Czech Republic and Germany during the audited period.
Out of the total number of 94 GIs received from Germany in the Czech Republic, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were processed within the three-month deadline, another 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were processed after this deadline and the remaining 1 case was not sent a response to Germany by the time of the SAO audit.
Graph 2 provides more detailed information on the deadlines by which replies to RUs received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic.
Out of the total number of 335 GIs sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) received a reply within the three-month deadline, another 179 (i.e. 53.4%) received a reply after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) did not receive a reply from Germany by the time of the SAO audit (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine when the response from Germany was received).
Chart 3 provides more detailed information on the deadlines by which replies to the RUs sent to Germany were received in the Czech Republic.
Graph 4 contains the percentage of intra-community transaction values reported in the RU transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany.
As can be seen from the graph above, the value of the commercial transactions examined through the GI was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
International exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax administrations from other Member States are often provided, without prior request, with information that may be of interest to them in managing VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at the CLO.
The information shall be transmitted electronically between Member States.
Under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, ‘automatic exchange’ means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals.
‘Structured automatic exchange’ means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax administrator from the form of the Delivery of a new means of transport pursuant to § 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
