When processing the aforementioned form, the tax administrator fills in the necessary data in a specially created template and transmits it in turn to the contact person at the financial directorate where the data are collected and within the stipulated deadline, i.e. no later than two months from the end of the quarter in which the information was available, transmitted to the Customs Office for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States.
In addition, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions that appear to be unauthorised and information on potential "missing traders".
This information is sent to other Member States by spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of the international exchange of information in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the local tax office.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form by e-mail directly to the German CLO, which forwards the SCAC forms to the foreign CLO.
The tax authorities have been instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information checked by BRH were sent in order to ensure the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German customs authority receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supplies of goods or services specified in the request for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
If there are no reasonable grounds for such a request, the German CLO shall reject any request containing an amount lower than the limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
In order to respond to a request for information, the CLO sends the request to the relevant tax office, referring to the three-month period.
There are no further deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor past deadlines, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to draw the attention of the tax authorities to replies to blank requests for information.
The tax authorities obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit covering any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only cover one recent transaction.
This short and ﬂexible type of audit requires no notification to the taxpayer and has proven its usefulness in investigating individual taxable transactions.
Under the automatic exchange without prior request, the FRG provides information to other Member States: – on the VAT IDs allocated to taxpayers resident in other Member States, – on the refund of input tax to taxpayers resident in other Member States.
In addition, the FRG has undertaken to provide the following information to other Member States through structured automatic exchange:
a. Supply of new means of transport to businesses without the use of their VAT ID, b. dispatching or catalogue sales in other Member States which are not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intra-Community acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intra-Community supply of goods which the German payer did not declare in the SH because it treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. potential "trader" who carried out intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "missing traders" or misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The dispatch of the RU or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the locally competent tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech – English) and translates the information sent into English or German, the German tax authorities follow the instruction that they should write the ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German using the monolingual form.
The German CLO does not provide translation of German texts.
The SAO found that 74.5 % of the submitted applications were processed by the Czech Tax Administration within the three-month period, while only 40.6 % of the cases were processed by the German Tax Administration in the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005.
Although the German CLO alerts the tax authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not monitor the time limits that have elapsed.
The result of missing notifications is a large number of delayed replies to the ZOI.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended regular warnings to the CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO is now alerting the tax authorities to reply to the unfinished replies to the RUI.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at different organisational levels of the tax administration deal with VAT risk management.
Within the MF, the following departments deal with the issue of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
VAT Methodology and Performance Department and within it a report Risk management in the field of VAT, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates the trends of these risks at domestic and Community level.
It coordinates the functioning of the role nationwide. The credibility of VAT returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-community transactions.
On the basis of trade balance data, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, prepares conceptual risk management in the field of VAT and cooperates in this area with relevant EU institutions and other Member States.
The International Cooperation Unit for VAT Administration, which inter alia provides information exchange in the field of VAT, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, provides information to the public and provides other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of incorrect VAT numbers or VAT IDs contained in O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The figures show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to different bases for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was filed, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
The Tax Control and Search Methodology Unit, which, among other things, carries out risk analysis in the framework of the methodological management of tax controls and, in accordance with risk analysis, prioritises the targeting of tax controls in the plans of the Financial Directorates, carries out risk analyses in the framework of the reduction of tax evasion, including the collection of lessons learned from the tax administration and from other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Search units are set up in the financial directorates, which carry out, among other things, searches of tax entities and areas that are at risk from the incidence of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searches of unregistered tax entities from the point of view of the risk of tax evasion (e.g. from internet services, job placement, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of links of chain fraud and transmission of information to local tax authorities.
Specialised control units are set up in the 12 tax offices selected.
They have regional competence and carry out tax inspections outside the territorial competence of the tax authorities on the basis of a mandate.
The need to set up a specialised tax inspection unit has arisen on the basis of increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, mainly involving entities linked to chains.
These units focus on the control of tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with a specific activity and multinational companies and tax entities with a large scale of activity in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms have been integrated into the ADIS system to limit VAT risks: – the role of Trust in VAT returns, to evaluate the risk of tax returns submitted; – the role of Selection of tax entities for control, to allow for the selection of payers for control on the basis of the chosen criteria; – the role of VIES, through which tax administrations have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, among other things: – to verify the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States; – to obtain from other Member States the values of goods delivered to the Czech payer declared in the SH by all his suppliers from other Member States; – to generate a report of payers who have not filed the SH; – to carry out a formal check of the data provided by payers from the Czech Republic in the SH before sending these data to other Member States; – to generate a report of payers for whom the data on the delivery of goods to other Member States listed in the VAT returns do not match the data of all other Member States.
As part of their activities to reduce the risk of tax evasion, tax administrators have access to registers of state administration bodies such as the Commercial Register, the Land Register, the Register of Motor Vehicles, the Register of Business Enterprises, etc.
More detailed information can be found in Chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (in particular the CLO) and the tax administrations of 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At the level of the CLO, the ST I 2 (hereinafter referred to as KUSS - Coordination Unit for Special VAT Audits and Tax Investigations) collects audit findings concerning tax fraud in a specific database called OPUS.
KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has set up a new database called ZAUBER, designed to transfer the names of missing traders' companies.
KUSS coordinates related cases of domestic and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of KUSS is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other departments of the CLO and MF are entrusted with the duties and powers associated with the RMS.
At the level of the CLO, there is a formal check of the composition of other Member States' VAT IDs in the SH filed by German payers.
This formal check is made prior to the provision of SH data to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Validation of VAT IDs listed in SH is done on the basis of O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure to correct an invalid VAT ID, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS on the CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and creates several types of control reports based on several characteristics, which usually figure in so-called carousel trading operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders".
The federal tax authorities are instructed to draw up these audit reports and, in some cases, report the results of their findings to the CLO.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all the available characteristics if a case of tax fraud (instead of focusing solely on the company’s turnover) is to be assumed with a sufficient degree of probability.
The BRH therefore suggested to the IMF that various characteristics should be taken into account in the reporting process.
The RMS should also cover other issues such as the payment behaviour (morale) of the taxpayer, the sector (economic activities) or the shareholder structure.
The second level of the RMS is processed in the federal tax administrations and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, the RMS generates a list of those payers who have reported intra-community deliveries in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the full submission of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-community acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with VIES data.
The tax administrations of the Länder try to avoid comparing quarterly data because such comparison would reveal too many disapproving data that are attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
– different execution times for the intra-community transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
– different accounting for sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different presentation in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT returns and the VIES system, many Länder have introduced elements of the RMS which are based on data from VAT returns and some other elements (such as the structure of the company name, the age of the shareholders, the number of employees and the payment behaviour/morale of the taxpayer).
Bavaria has introduced a RMS based on rules that allow a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to programme their own rules for the identification of potential tax evaders.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
The competent tax authority will therefore receive the recommendation made by the RMS before the determination of VAT.
As this RMS is unable to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers need to adjust the relevant rules based on feedback from the tax authorities.
The district of Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania has programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data from tax files where a check revealed tax evasion.
On the basis of this data, RMS is able to ascertain the characteristics of the tax evasion.
The RMS establishes once a month a list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities shall use this list as a basis for deciding on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
Following the audit, auditors must report their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The administrative region of North Rhine-Westphalia uses an adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on a large amount of data from the VAT returns under consideration and some other facts, this neural fuzzy or data-mining system calculates the probability that a taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential fraudsters.
The local tax authorities use this list as a basis for the selection of the relevant taxpayers for inspection and report the findings of the inspection to the data processing centre.
The implementation of one of these three RMS in the other Länder is ongoing.
As none of the three RMS is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for tackling tax fraud.
It remains to be seen whether this system will produce the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific criteria of RMS in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State developed its own RMS.
Like the different approaches in the three federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
New trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud are currently being discussed by the tax authorities of the EU Member States.
VAT fraud – especially carousel fraud – does not turn out to be a national problem, but rather a European one.
Taxpayers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State but in several States.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
A VAT loss due to fraud in the EU may not affect the Member State of the instigator of the fraud.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and discussion on the RMS.
Selected audit findings when verifying commercial transactions
Within the framework of the cooperation on the implementation of parallel audits, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
In addition, the two audit institutions jointly scrutinized the execution of several commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution, or discrepancies in the way the payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT returns, respectively SH.
At the request of BRH, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases concerning commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
In addition, in 43 cases, the SAO audited the values of intra-community transactions with Germany reported by Czech payers in their tax returns and SH based on BRH warnings.
At the SAO's request, BRH examined a total of 23 cases involving commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the Customs.
Examination of the selected cases revealed, among other things, that the different way of registering in the EU Member States leads to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 60 500 from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
As the Czech payer declared the acquisition of goods only in the value corresponding to EUR 29 869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the supplied goods.
In its reply to the RUI received from Germany, the German side stated that in the second quarter of 2004 the German payer delivered goods to the Czech payer in the value of EUR 27 381, in the third quarter in the value of EUR 31 997 and in the fourth quarter of 2004 in the value of EUR 10 276.
The reply also showed that the VAT ID of the German payer had only been valid since 28 September 2004, but the German Customs in 2006, on the basis of an additional request from the German payer for a VAT ID validity certificate, issued a VAT ID validity certificate retroactively from 1 May 2004.
The German payer corrected the SH.
On the basis of this information, the Czech payer was involved in the acquisition of goods.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer, on the basis of an investigation by the tax administrator, submitted additional VAT returns for individual tax periods in 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States and at the same time exercised the right to deduct VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, it was not possible for the Czech tax authorities to determine unequivocally from those supplementary VAT returns whether the values of the supplies from the abovementioned German supplier were also included.
Based on the SAO’s request, BRH found out that the German supplier had been registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not apply for a VAT ID when registering, he was only given an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although in Germany it is usually not possible to assign a VAT ID retroactively to a VAT payer, in this case the German tax official in 2006 assigned a VAT ID retroactively to the aforementioned German VAT payer as of 1 May 2004.
The German CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively if the German entrepreneur did not cause a delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by the CLO after the payer's VAT ID application.
In this case, the VAT ID is allocated retroactively by the Customs Office because the trader does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community supplies pursuant to Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
By contrast, the German beneficiary does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier in order to declare intra-community acquisitions.
Because of these different practices between Member States, the German CLO in this specific case has allocated the VAT ID retroactively.
2.
As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested verification of the German taxpayer's VAT registration.
The VIES indicated the date of registration as 5.3.2005, while the date of 1.10.2004 was indicated on the German payer’s registration certificate issued by the German tax office responsible for the place.
In the reply received from Germany, the German authorities stated that the German taxpayer had been registered since 1 October 2004, but that the VAT ID had not been provided to him in Germany until 16 February 2005 for organisational reasons.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator and found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a VAT audit of the Czech tax payer for the tax period from the third quarter of 2004 to the second quarter of 2005.
By this audit, the tax office found that the Czech payer included in the VAT return services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314) provided to the German payer in the period before his VAT registration (i.e. before 1 October 2004).
For the tax period of the third quarter of 2004, the tax office charged the taxpayer VAT amounting to CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
On the basis of the SAO's request, BRH found out that the German payer was not assigned a VAT ID until 16.2.2005 when it informed the tax office about its business, which it had started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively as of 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer declared an intra-community acquisition from the Czech Republic worth EUR 160 (about CZK 5,000).
3. The Czech payer declared the delivery of goods worth CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) to the German payer in the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for the third quarter of 2004.
During the verification of the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax administrator found that his registration was valid from 11 November 2004, i.e. after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer filed an additional VAT DAP in which he declared the tax base of the effected transactions in the Czech Republic in the amount of CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) and VAT in the amount of CZK 21 777 (EUR 692), which he paid.
The SAO inquired at the local tax office in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer subsequently filed a request for a retrial in the matter of the additional VAT declaration and submitted as evidence a confirmation from the German tax administration that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
It was apparent from the reply received from Germany that the German taxpayer was not granted a VAT ID until 11.11.2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the application for a retrial.
BRH found that this was not an intra-Community acquisition of goods, as the German payer did not obtain a VAT ID until 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared the VAT on that acquisition by claiming an input tax refund of the same amount.
However, since there would have been no change in the value of the VAT payable by the German taxpayer, the tax authorities in Germany did not correct the data in his VAT return.
BRH also found that the name of the German taxpayer, mentioned in the GI, had been changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech payer in the first quarter of 2005 in the amount of EUR 22 686 from a German payer.
The SAO inquired with the local tax authority in the Czech Republic and found that the tax authority had carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, during which it verified that the delivery of the goods had taken place and the Czech payer had accounted for and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not declare the acquisition of goods in the VAT return because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intra-community transactions only from 21 April 2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German tax payer's registration certificate so that he could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech Tax Office assessed the commercial transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer in Germany and therefore did not charge the Czech payer additional tax on the commercial transaction.
The BRH found that, under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not need to have a VAT ID in order to exempt intra-Community supplies of goods from VAT.
The supplier must only have the VAT ID of the customer from another Member State and be able to prove that the goods have been transported to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, this was therefore an intra-community transaction and VAT should be charged in the Czech Republic.
In any event, it is important that the Czech tax authorities noticed this transaction, since the supply of the machine at this value was not the main business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to reply to the EIT relating to intra-Community transactions of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax audit of the tax entity for this tax period.
In the context of international administrative cooperation, he asked the German tax authorities to verify the supply of those goods using the SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never traded with the German company and that the acquisition of the goods was not recorded in his accounts.
The German tax administration rejected the request to provide evidence – contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents – on the grounds that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no other explanatory reasons were given.
Since the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence to assess the tax on the acquired goods, he terminated the tax inspection without finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
Based on the SAO’s request, BRH found that the German payer acted as a so-called “fiscal representative” (Section 22a – e UStG).
The German payer declared these deliveries in his annual VAT return and in the SH.
He was entitled to the exemption of the supply.
On the basis of BRH's notification, the German tax office will send to the Czech Republic the documents necessary for the assessment of the tax on the acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in chapter 4.6.1, the replies to the RU sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the three-month deadline more often than the replies from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO audit found that the Czech tax administration sent a request for information to Germany on 5 October 2005 concerning the verification of the value of the delivered goods for the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German payer declared in the SH for this period the supply of goods to the Czech payer in the value of EUR 86 307, but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only in the value corresponding to EUR 35 314.
In its reply to the ŽOI, received in the Czech Republic on 9.5.2006, i.e. after the expiry of the deadline for processing laid down in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German party stated that the application could not be processed as the German firm had ceased to operate at the end of 2005.
As the German tax administration did not comply with the deadline for completing the ŽOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the documents needed for tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator, using the SCAC form, requested an examination of the deliveries of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German payer made in the third and fourth quarters of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that there was no response from Germany to the ŽOI by the time of the audit.
The SAO also inquired with the local tax administrator that the Czech payer did not include in the VAT return deliveries of new means of transport for the German payer in the amount of CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375,472).
The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity filed the subsequent SH.
Based on the SAO’s request, BRH found that the German Customs Office had not submitted the above mentioned RUI to the local tax office for verification due to technical reasons.
Following the BRH's warning, a check was carried out at the German purchaser's premises in Germany, which established that the acquisition of all cars had been properly taxed and that the cars in question had been sold to a sub-payer in Germany.
8. According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 from the German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was not declared by the Czech payer.
By enquiring with the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
Tax returns were not filed by the Czech payer even after requests from the tax administrator, so the tax office charged him VAT in the amount of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004 on 23 May 2005.
On 2.6.2005, the Customs Office drew attention to the aforementioned supply from the German payer.
Since the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, the tax administrator sent the Tax Inspectorate to Germany regarding the above-mentioned supply.
As the reply to the SAO was not received in the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained by the international exchange until the end of the SAO audit.
The tax office cancelled the VAT registration of the Czech payer due to non-compliance with obligations arising from the VAT Act on 23 August 2005.
In some cases, only a partial response was sent to the SAO, because the audit performed by the tax authorities at the payers was not completed at the time of the SAO and BRH audit:
9.
In 2005, the Czech tax administrator, using the SCAC form, requested an investigation into the delivery of a car worth EUR 16 991 to a German payer in the third quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
In its reply to the ŽOI, the German tax authority stated that it had only an invoice issued by a Czech taxpayer for a delivery of EUR 16 335.
Based on the SAO’s request, BRH found that the audit carried out by the German tax office at the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
The German acquirer declared the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice, in the tax returns for August and September 2004.
10. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator, using the SCAC form, requested an investigation into the delivery of cars to a German payer worth EUR 198 167, made in the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent to the Czech Republic a partial reply to the ŽOI, in which it confirmed the acquisition of certain cars by the German payer and further stated that the investigation in Germany had not been completed.

The SAO found that the local tax office carried out several local investigations at the Czech supplier in order to verify the use of excessive VAT deductions, during which it did not detect their unauthorized use.
BRH found that the German payer had declared in his VAT returns the acquisition of goods from other Member States for a total value of EUR 579 114 during that period and that the check carried out by the German tax office on the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
Chapter 4.4.1 describes the reasons for the differences between the values of the intra-Community acquisition of goods declared by the recipient in the tax return and the values declared by the supplier in its SH.
The audited cases showed that the most common reasons for differences were not the time shift or the incorrect value of the intra-community delivery of goods in the SH:
11.
According to the VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 35 716 from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005, but the Czech payer did not acknowledge this acquisition.
Since the Czech taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not carry out any activities at the company's registered office, the Czech tax administrator requested to verify, as part of the international exchange of information, how the German taxpayer communicated with the Czech taxpayer.
The reply to the ŽOI received from Germany showed that, according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech taxpayer was unknown at the address communicated and that the goods had been taken over by the agreed carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only delivered goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false confirmation of the payment of EUR 155 153 to the German payer.
After discovering fraudulent behaviour on the part of the Czech acquirer, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the supplied material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7 916.
The SAO inquired at the local tax office in the Czech Republic and found that the tax administrator charged the Czech taxpayer VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States in the amount of CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).
On the basis of the SAO's request, BRH confirmed that the German supplier only reported the delivery of goods to the Czech payer in the amount of EUR 7,916 after repairs.
According to the German legal situation, the German payer declared the corrected values of the goods and the reduction of the taxable amount in the quarter in which the correction was made.

12.
In the context of the international exchange of information, the German tax authority requested to verify, by means of an SCAC form, the supply of goods and services effected in the third quarter of 2005.
According to this GI, the Czech payer was to deliver goods totalling EUR 396 126 to the German payer during this period and to provide services amounting to EUR 11 885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation to verify this supply with the Czech payer.
In reply to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer supplied the German payer with a production line including assembly.
The individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic entered the EU and after 1 May 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of the order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because it claimed to have defects.
In the third quarter of 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for the amounts of EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer accepted the issued invoices but did not recognise them and did not pay them.
The SAO also inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that all invoices are duly registered in the accounts of the Czech payer.
In the VAT returns for the third quarter of 2005, only the amounts that were documented by the Czech payer and that relate to invoicing after 1 May 2004 are shown.
BRH found that on the basis of a reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax authority in Germany concluded that the transaction concerned the supply of goods from the Czech payer to the German payer, including services for assembly.
In this particular case, the place of so-called performance of work is where the assembly of the production line took place.
Under the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the service is liable to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient may deduct VAT on the same amount.
As there would have been no change in the value of the VAT that the German taxpayer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax office.
13. According to VIES data, in February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth EUR 58 000 from German payer C.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify this supply.
In its reply to the ŽOI, the German side stated that the machine had already been supplied to the Czech payer B by the German payer C in 2004, but that the machine should have been returned to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to information from the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but was transported to the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the reply to the request for information showed that the German payer C had sold the machine to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
As the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-Community delivery of goods.
The SAO inquired with the tax administrator of the local tax payer B and found that according to VIES data, the German tax payer C delivered goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech tax payer B in the third quarter of 2004.
Tax payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the locally competent tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the ŽOI to Germany.
According to the reply to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Further investigation by the Czech tax administrator found that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in the accounts of the payer B, and that it could be of the same type as the one supplied by the organizational unit of the German payer C to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax administrator of the local tax payer A carried out a local investigation of the payer.
The tax administrator was in possession of an invoice from the German payer C dated 7 February 2005, on which the payer A was listed as the purchaser of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found out that payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payee A had a leasing contract with another Czech company where the lease was for a machine of the same type.
The machine was handed over from the leasing company on February 9, 2005, the transport of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax office to determine the tax liability of A.
BRH found that the German payer C did not deliver the machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable transaction in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax authorities did not recognise the German taxpayer's VAT exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to Czech payer B.
Under German law, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that the German payer C had indicated in its SH for the first quarter of 2005 the delivery of a machine worth EUR 58 000 to the Czech payer A.
That supply was not verified during the tax audit carried out by the German tax office.

14.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administration received a request for information from Germany on 4 October 2005, in which the German tax administrator requested verification of an intra-community delivery from a German payer in the amount of EUR 879 680 625 to a Czech payer.
According to the German tax authority, there was a suspicion that this was a sham intra-Community supply of goods.
It was further stated in the EIT that the German payer had not engaged in any active commercial activity since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator conducted a local investigation of the Czech payer.
According to the managing director of the Czech company, the abovementioned case appeared to be a claim of a German payer against the German tax administration, which the Czech payer had filed as a partner of a German company with the German tax authority.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator has no information that the German tax administration has solved the issue related to the Czech taxpayer.
According to the available information, this was not a supply of goods, yet this value is still included in the VIES system as an intra-Community supply of goods to a Czech payer from Germany.
The main reason for the following discrepancies was that the beneficiaries did not declare intra-Community acquisitions of goods in their tax returns (see also chapter 4.4.1):
15. According to VIES data, the German payer delivered goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the Czech payer between the third quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005. The Czech payer did not acknowledge this acquisition.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested verification of the supply of goods from Germany.
In response to this request, the German tax administration stated that the German payer had sent part of the goods to the address of the Czech payer, while the remaining goods had been collected by the Czech payer himself.
By enquiring with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech tax payer submitted additional VAT returns for the above periods before receiving the reply to the Tax Office.
Despite this submission, the differences in the acquisition values were not resolved, so the Czech tax administrator recommended a tax inspection of the Czech payer.
The check has not yet been carried out.
16. According to the VIES data, the German payer delivered goods worth EUR 46 854 to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004.
For the same period, the Czech payer granted intra-community acquisitions only in the amount corresponding to EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator requested verification within the framework of the international exchange of information of the value of the deliveries made.
The reply to the ŽOI, delivered from Germany, was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total value of 31 999 EUR, i.e. the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer and the VIES data.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that after receiving a reply from Germany, the Czech tax administrator contacted the Czech tax payer's accountant and agreed with him that after examining these invoices, he would discuss with the owner of the company the submission of a supplementary VAT return for the third quarter of 2004.
The additional VAT return has not yet been filed.
The Czech tax administrator told the SAO that he would continue to proceed in order to comply with the deadlines for a possible additional assessment of VAT for the relevant tax period.
17.
The German payer was to deliver goods worth EUR 11 600 to the Czech payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
In the context of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator asked for confirmation whether the Czech payer actually existed because the alleged partner of the German payer had set up several fictitious companies in Germany.
When examining the commercial transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of the goods to the tax office.
According to the Czech payer, however, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were resold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer submitted documents on the sale of goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, he did not declare or pay the tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic or Germany.
All these facts suggested tax evasion in Germany and were communicated by the Czech tax authorities to the German tax authorities in their reply to the EIT.
The SAO inquired at the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer submitted an additional VAT return for the fourth quarter of 2004, including the value of the acquisition of goods from the German payer and at the same time claimed the right to deduct tax on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
He did not include VAT on the sale of goods in Germany in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return after a local investigation without changes.
According to the Czech legislation, this case did not involve the acquisition of goods from other Member States because the goods were neither dispatched nor transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore wrongly concluded the local investigation.
BRH found that immediately after receiving a reply from the Tax Inspectorate stating that the goods had not left Germany, the German tax authorities corrected the German taxpayer’s tax return and demanded VAT of EUR 1 600.
In addition, the relevant tax office sent a warning to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of those goods was correctly taxed.
In the following cases, payers reported intra-community transactions that probably did not actually take place:
18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
The application was accompanied by a copy of the certificate of registration of the Czech taxpayer for VAT.
A copy of the passport of the person who, as has been said, was to carry out the transport of that car was also enclosed.
The Czech tax administrator's investigation revealed that it was a stolen passport, the person mentioned in it did not import any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax authorities.
This information was included by the Czech tax administrator in his reply to the ŽOI together with the statement that he could not confirm the acquisition of the goods – the car in question.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer did not reside at the address given in the Commercial Register and the company manager was not in contact.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech taxpayer's tax liability in the amount of CZK 0 after the complaint procedure for the tax period of February 2005.
Further investigation by the Czech tax administrator revealed that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity, which had purchased it through an advertisement on the internet.
BRH found that, on the basis of the Czech reply to the ŽOI, the competent German tax authority would not recognise the German taxpayer’s entitlement to exemption from VAT for that supply.
19. During the inspection, the German tax office was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3 000 between the value of the goods acquired declared in the tax return of the payer and the value provided from another Member State.
It was reported that the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth EUR 89 424 to the German payer during the fourth quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the VIES data, the German tax authority requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the context of an international exchange of information.
In its reply to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the sole managing director of the Czech company had been removed from the Commercial Register on 8 July 2005 and the new managing director had not been registered.
The German recipient of the goods appeared to be a relative of a member of a Czech company.
The Czech payer filed VAT returns with the SH, which were signed by an unauthorized person – the said partner of the company – after deletion of the agent from the Commercial Register.
The accountant of the Czech payer confirmed to the tax administrator that the company partner deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
No cash receipts were issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic inquired at the local tax office and found that the tax administrator granted the Czech tax payer an exemption from VAT on the delivery of goods to another Member State in the amount of CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) in the fourth quarter of 2004 and in the amount of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548) in the first quarter of 2005.
BRH found that the tax authority in Germany had not corrected the VAT return of the German acquirer because a German judge had in the meantime confirmed the insolvency of the German taxpayer.
As the previous inspection did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the tax liability assessed.
20. According to VIES data, a German payer purchased goods from the Czech Republic worth EUR 4 251 196 in 2005 after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.
In the tax return for 2004 and in the tax return for 2005, the German payer did not declare an intra-community acquisition.
Nor did it show any reasonable supply.
Because of these differences, the German tax office sent the ŽOI, relating to the fourth quarter of 2005 and the first quarter of 2006.
The Czech supplier reported intra-community delivery of goods to the German payer in SH for these two quarters for a total value of CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6 September 2006, the ŽOI was delivered, in which the German side asked to check whether the intra-community deliveries declared by the Czech payer had taken place.
In its reply to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the request of the German party could not be met because the Czech payer had no agent.
As can be seen from the documents provided by the SAO by the relevant tax administrator, on 30 March 2006 a report was drawn up with the agent of the Czech payer on the initiation of the VAT audit for the fourth quarter of 2004 and January to December 2005.
At the same time, the taxpayer was asked by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the aforementioned periods, but he did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the only managing director of the Czech payer ceased to hold office on 16 May 2006, and the new managing director was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech payer has stopped filing VAT returns.
In cooperation with BRH, the SAO scrutinized several cases of intra-community deliveries between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the cases examined was transmitted between the two SAIs via the two countries' CLOs.
21. The Czech company (ECR), which is not resident in Germany, has informed the relevant tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Because of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005 but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the delivery of these wind farms in the name, at the risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of its own capacity, the Czech company handed over part of the order to a German payer (ED) based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relations and the way wind power plants are transported:
According to the German legal situation, the place where such transactions take place must be determined in accordance with the following rules:
– A Danish entrepreneur (DK) sent wind farms to be installed under his name, at his own risk and on his own account in Austria.
As the installation of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
- As the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started - in Germany.
Although the wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the beneficiary is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of the German subcontractor (ED) could not obtain the tax exemption because the other Member State of destination differs from the other Member State of residence of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (CZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery to the Czech company (ECR) is also determined at the beginning of the transport.
Transport of some wind power plants started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- The supply of those wind power plants that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- The supply of other wind power plants produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (ECR) carried out both intra-community delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-community delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (ECR) did not record any intra-community acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany, nor did it submit SH to the German Customs Office.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intra-community deliveries uniformly as intra-community deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that the ECR reported no intra-community deliveries to Austria, but intra-community deliveries to Denmark.
Examination of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), although this case does not show any evidence of tax fraud or evasion.
In addition, the SAO and the SAO scrutinized the transactions to highlight the differences between the tax declaration declaration and the VIES data, which were caused by different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes in legislation require time for the application of new legislation in practice by both payers and tax authorities:
22. In the SH for the second to fourth quarters of 2004, the Czech payer reported intra-community delivery to the German payer for a total value of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
For the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported intra-community delivery to another German payer for a total value of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above supplies in the SH in accordance with the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., valid in 2004.
Further examination of the above-mentioned transactions revealed that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal regulation of the supply or acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers recorded the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid version of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intra-Community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legislation in force in 2004 it was not an intra-Community acquisition, but a taxable transaction with the place of performance in Germany.
The difference in legal regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., which amends certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2005.
23. During the examination of selected intra-community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was also found that the Czech payer reported intra-community deliveries to the German payer in SH for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2005 with a total value of CZK 240,411,163 (EUR 8,071,823) and another Czech payer reported intra-community deliveries to the German payer in SH for the same period with a total value of CZK 263,470,776 (EUR 8,846,050).
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, in the case of the supply of electricity, the place of performance is the place where the customer has his registered office, place of business or where he has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have reported the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
By reporting the intra-community supply of electricity in SH, both above-mentioned payers distorted the VIES data by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation fulfilled the goals of the Czech National Bank and the SAO.
Both SAIs gained a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed differences between the two systems and showed that the VAT administration legislation differs.
Suspicious cases of intra-community transactions were identified during the parallel controls.
Some of them are worth checking out afterwards.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs made recommendations concerning the administration of VAT.
The follow-up of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation between the two audit institutions is the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT management checks.
Communiqué
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise duty administration inspections between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Opening Word
The joint report informs about the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, aimed at the administration of excise duties in the period after the accession of both countries to the European Union.
The cooperation was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement on control activities concluded in February 2006.
The subject of parallel controls was chosen in view of the fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties which took place in the context of the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union as from 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the European Union's internal market requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow goods to circulate unencumbered up to the date of their final supply.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under a suspension arrangement.
The system places great demands on the tax authorities and presupposes close cooperation between the competent administrative authorities of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise administration controls for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (CR) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of the audit: (CR) Administration of excise duties (SR) Procedure of customs authorities in administration of excise duties
The Supreme Audit Office (SAO) of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO") and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO SR") concluded the "Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activities" on 8 February 2006.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel audits “Administration of excise duties”, included in the audit plan of the SAO-CR for 2005 under No. 05/34, and “Control of the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties”, included in the audit plan of the SAO-CR for 2006 under No. 48/11.
Parallel checks had the character of a coordinated check.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information which could not be obtained by the contracting parties during an inspection of the administration of excise duties in their national territory and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the inspections in the sense of the European implementing directives for the implementation of the INTOSAI auditing standards - Directive No 31.
On the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic"), the auditing groups from the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Western Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Northeast Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia performed the auditing in the period from 7 February to 2 June 2006.
27 auditors were involved in the audit.
The audited bodies were the Directorate-General for Customs (‘DG’) and 11 tax offices.
Within the DG, 12 selected customs offices out of a total of 54 were audited.
The auditing operation on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Slovak Republic) was carried out by the Finance and Taxation Section of the SAO of Slovakia in cooperation with the SAO of Slovakia Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
Eight inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel controls was to examine the customs authorities' handling of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation was focused on the procedure of tax administrators when supervising the transport of excise goods, in particular on the registration of initiated and terminated movements under the conditional exemption regime, and on the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the excise tax administrators of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
2. Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was performed by the financial authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken over by the customs authorities, which have so far collected excise duty only on importation.
In the Czech Republic, mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The state budget revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic totalled CZK 82.8 billion in 2004, and excise duties accounted for 19.5% of the state budget revenue from taxes and duties amounting to CZK 424.7 billion.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the share of the state budget revenue from taxes and fees amounting to CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duty on mineral oils for the State Budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it amounted to 90.9%.
The difference to 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
All excise duties in Slovakia have been administered by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duty on mineral oil, which they have administered since 1 January 2002.
Until then, excise duties were administered by the tax authorities.
In Slovakia, mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The revenue of the state budget from excise duties in the Slovak Republic in 2004 was a total of SKK 43.4 billion and the total tax revenue of SKK 209.5 billion was accounted for by excise duties of 20.7%.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise duties was SKK 50 billion and the total tax revenue was SKK 222.6 billion. Excise taxes accounted for 22.5%.
Graph 1 — Comparison of revenue of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenue of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenue from excise duties
- Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products (hereinafter referred to as ‘Directive 92/12/EEC’), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as ‘Regulation No 2073/2004’), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty (hereinafter referred to as ‘Regulation No 2719/92’), - Commission Regulation (hereinafter referred to as ‘excise movement within the Member State of excise duty) No 3649/EEC) for excise goods accompanying movement within the Member State of excise duty.
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll., on Excise Taxes, as amended (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 353/2003 Coll."), which has been in force since 1 January 2004.
In the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are, inter alia, bound by the following generally binding legislation: - Law No 98/2004 Z. z. o spotrebnej dani z minerálneho oleja v znení neskorích predpisov (hereinafter ‘Law No 98/2004 Z. z. z.’), - Law No 104/2004 Z. z. z. o. 
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty between Member States of the European Union
The conditions of movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty shall be governed by Directive 92/12/EEC in Title III — Movement of goods Articles 15 to 20.
According to those provisions, the transport of those goods may be effected only by an authorised warehousekeeper, who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
The consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, but who may not store or dispatch such products under the duty suspension arrangement.
Authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and Slovakia means the operator of a tax warehouse, the economic operator is the authorised recipient for the repeated or one-off receipt of products subject to excise duty.
The movement of excise products under suspension of excise duty is possible under Directive 92/12/EEC only with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be drawn up by the consignor in four copies before the transport begins, unless a further copy is required by the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch.
2.2 Procedure for the commencement and termination of the transport of goods under the conditional tax exemption regime between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for the commencement of transport is governed by Section 25(3) of Act No 353/2003 Coll., which states, inter alia:
‘The operator of the tax warehouse shall, before the transport of the selected products begins, inform the customs office which is locally competent of the tax warehouse from which the transport is to begin;
The transport of the selected products may be initiated only with the consent of that customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax has been fulfilled.’
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of the transport only if a guarantee of tax equal to the amount of tax due on the transported products is provided.
The consignor shall be obliged to draw up an accompanying document in five copies before commencing transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document the consent to the start of the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copies No 2, 3 and 4 shall be handed over by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorising the transport.
Under Slovak law, the consignee in Slovakia keeps copy No 2 of the accompanying document. They shall confirm receipt of the products on copies No 3 and No 4 and present both copies to the customs office with geographical jurisdiction.
Copy No 3, certified by the customs office, shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which the products were received.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
The transport is terminated by the receipt of the products by the consignee.
The customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the start of the transport, shall decide on the release of the tax guarantee within 5 working days after the presentation of copy No.3 of the accompanying document, which shall be confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Graph 2 — Circulation of the accompanying document for transport started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic
Transport from Slovakia
The procedure for the transport of ethyl alcohol and tobacco products from the Slovak Republic to another Member State of the European Union was amended as follows until 31 December 2005:
Pursuant to Paragraph 26(4) of Law No 105/2004 Z. z.
‘When transporting a lieh from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorised consignee, or to a tax plenipotentiary in the inom Member State, an odosielatel’ (supplier) is obliged on the day of the start of the transport to send a copy of the first diel of the sprievodného document electronically or by fax to the customs office of Poprad; that copy is required to be sent to the customs office in writing to the piatich of the working days from the start of the transport. “
Pursuant to Article 22(4) of Law No 106/2004 Z. z.
‘When transporting tobacco products from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorised consignee, or to a tax plenipotentiary in the inom Member State, the odosielatel’ (supplier) is obliged, on the day of the start of the transport, to send a copy of the first diel of the sprievodné document electronically or by fax to the Colné úrad Poprad; it is obliged to send that copy to the colný úrad pisomne najor to those working days of the start of the transport. “
In respect of the transport of other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) during the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as the ‘audited period’), the taxpayer was not required to notify the Poprad Customs Office or the competent customs office of the start of the transport under the duty suspension arrangement.
The tax administrator became aware of the transport of these products only during a local investigation or tax inspection from the accompanying documents and accounting documents of the taxpayer.
The consignor in Slovakia is obliged to draw up an accompanying document in four copies before the transport begins.
Copy No 1 shall be retained by the consignor (for the transport of ethyl alcohol and tobacco products, a copy of copy No 1 shall be sent electronically or by fax to the Poprad Customs Office and the competent customs office).
Copy No 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods being transported.
According to the Czech legislation, the consignee in the Czech Republic keeps copy No. 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in the Slovak Republic and confirms receipt of the products on copies No. 3 and 4.
Confirmed copies No 3 and No 4 shall be sent to the locally competent customs office in the Czech Republic no later than the first working day after completion of the transport.
The customs office shall keep copy No 4 and return copy No 3, on which it shall check its accuracy and validity, to the consignee.
The consignee shall send copy No 3 to the consignor in SR no later than the working day following receipt of the copy.
Transport in Slovakia is considered to have ended on the date of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The consignor proves the completion of the transport by submitting copy No.3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the consignee and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Graph 3 — Circulation of the accompanying document during transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in the Slovak Republic and ended in the Czech Republic
In 2006, the Slovak Republic gradually adopted amendments to all laws on excise duties, according to which the consignor of goods under suspension of duty is obliged to send a copy of copy No.1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the consignor with territorial jurisdiction before the transport begins.
The document proving completion of the transport of ethyl alcohol and tobacco products shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and his competent tax authority.
Document No 3, certified by the consignee, showing that the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer has ended.
Confirmation by the tax authorities of another Member State of receipt of the said goods by the consignee shall be required if the latter is required, under the legislation of the Member State concerned, to endorse copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Registration of initiated and terminated transport operations kept by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
There is no single electronic system in place to monitor the transport of goods under suspension of tax between Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products requires Member States and the European Commission to introduce, from 1 July 2009, an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) to enable excise authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently only used in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under the suspension arrangement and to ensuring more effective control of the movement of untaxed products within all Member States.
National transport databases of the Member States will be part of this system.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport operations initiated and completed on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module Records of Selected Products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of transport carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, tax administrators can obtain information about the start or end of the transport immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in the EVV.
The customs office shall release the tax security for the transported products provided by the consignor at the time of registration of the end of the transport by the customs office of the locally competent consignee.
Customs offices in Slovakia use a database based on the application software SysNed, which ensures the automation of their activities in the administration of excise duties and communication with the systems of the European Union.
By registering the tax warehouse, the tax warehouse operator or the beneficiary in the SysNed application software, this data is automatically transferred to the System for Exchange of Excise Data (SEED) database.
3. Preparation and conduct of cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO-CR and representatives of the SAO-SR took place in January 2006.
The two parties have become acquainted with the legislation on excise duties and with the organisation of the administration of excise duties in both countries.
Particular attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia in authorising, respectively starting and ending the transport of products subject to excise duty under the duty suspension regime and the exchange of information between the excise tax authorities of both countries.
