At the meeting it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak parties: - will process the total data on the quantity of excise products transported from the Czech Republic to Slovakia and vice versa, whose transport started during the audited period, - will compare the data on mineral oil transport, - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and ethyl alcohol, - Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the conditional exemption regime initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the periods examined were extended by the months of October and November 2005 and during those months the transport of tobacco products under suspension of excise duty was also inspected.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of excise products transported under the duty suspension arrangement between Czech and Slovak tax subjects during the audited period.
4. Comparison of transport registers of goods under suspension of excise duty
The SAO-CR provided the Slovak side with a database of transport completed in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5 876 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 5 738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items of ethyl alcohol and 4 items related to tobacco products.
The SAO of Slovakia provided the Czech side with a database of transport completed in Slovakia, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 696 items related to mineral oil, 2,066 items of ethyl alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared data on transport operations listed in the register of commenced transport operations in the Czech Republic with data on terminated transport operations registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are presented in Table 3.
The SAO-CR compared the traffic data in November 2004 and September 2005 with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which the SAO handed over at the beginning of the audit.
The database did not contain data allowing reliable approval of individual transport operations, and therefore only 63% of the traffic initiated could be assigned.
Individual transports were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. consignor, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Data on transport operations initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in Slovakia in October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93 % of the initiated transport operations were unambiguously assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the quantity of mineral oils were given in litres or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of ethyl alcohol was in most cases expressed in litres, but this could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the percentage of alcohol indicated in the database.
The quantities of tobacco products were given in pieces, in thousands and in kilograms, depending on the type of tobacco products.
In the case of transport operations initiated in the Czech Republic, the termination of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or the quantity of products transported did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
Documents accompanying 487 shipments of ethyl alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were checked.
The audit of these documents was carried out at the customs offices, where the SAO-CR performed the audit.
For transport operations authorised by other customs offices, accompanying documents were requested through the DG.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the realization of 141 transport operations for which the customs offices in the Czech Republic did not document the confirmed copies No.3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products indicated on the accompanying document did not match the quantity of products indicated in the database.
In addition, data on transport registered in the Slovak database were transmitted to the Slovak side, but this data was not included in the transport database of the Czech customs administration.
The SAO of Slovakia searched the database of the Slovak customs administration for 95 transports.
The verification of the remaining 46 shipments was requested by the locally competent customs offices, which proved their completion with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side copies of accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport services were identified also in the Czech database, with the exception of the transport operations carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of initiated transport operations.
Examination of these cases revealed:
- in the Slovak transport database, 11 alcohol transports in the total amount of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 alcohol transports in the total amount of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005 were registered.
The SAO-CR found that these were transports of taxed products, for which the consignor does not need the tax administrator's consent.
The consignor informed the tax administrator in writing of the start of the transport. The transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under a duty suspension arrangement;
- in the Slovak transport database, a total of 94 mineral oil transports, code of the Combined Nomenclature 2710 11 21, were registered in the total volume of 173 thousand litres carried out by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005 the tax entity carried out transport of 102 thousand litres of untaxed mineral oils without the appropriate authorisation.
The taxpayer held a special authorisation for the receipt and use of exempt products, under which he could supply untaxed products only to the holder of the same authorisation.
He did not notify the customs office in the Czech Republic of the start of the transport and did not provide a tax guarantee of CZK 1,207,680 for the transported products.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the taxpayer transported 71 thousand litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of SR. Again, he failed to fulfil a legal obligation by failing to notify the customs office of the start of the transport operations.
Transport of products put into free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State may be initiated by the consignor in the Czech Republic without the consent of the customs office, but the consignor is obliged to inform the customs office in writing before the transport begins.
A taxpayer purchasing products put into free circulation in another Member State is required to declare the quantities and ensure the tax before they are taken away.
Products may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are governed by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also allows the use of an accompanying document for movements under suspension of duty, but this document must clearly indicate that it is a ‘simplified accompanying document for tax control purposes (products subject to excise duty)’.
The same rules on the transport and admission of products put into free circulation in another Member State apply in the Slovak Republic.
In those cases, the taxable persons transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under the suspension arrangement, the 3rd and 4th copies of which were submitted by the recipient to the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic for verification.
The customs authorities in Slovakia registered these transport operations in the database of transport under the suspension arrangement, as the accompanying documents did not state that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO of Slovakia compared the transport database of the Czech customs administration with the transport database of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- in the databases, the quantity of products transported was given inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, in hectolitres or in kilograms; ethyl alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it more difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported;
- the quantity of ethyl alcohol transported in the invoices did not correspond to the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were listed in the databases,
- two alcohol shipments from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic carried out in November 2004 in a total volume of 47 237 litres of alcohol were registered in the database of the Slovak customs administration, which were not found in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Until 30 June 2005, the conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for administering excise duties were governed by Council Directive 77/799/EEC concerning mutual assistance by the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxation of insurance premiums.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004 entered into force, laying down the rules and procedures allowing the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office which shall liaise with other Member States in the field of excise duty administration and shall be responsible for exchanging information on movements of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the “Excise Liaison Office” (hereinafter referred to as “ELO ČR”) was set up in the DG to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union.
With effect from 1 May 2004, the ELO at the Poprad Customs Office was responsible for ensuring the management of the systems for controlling the movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the Slovak Republic.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of ELO are carried out by the ELO Unit (based in Poprad) of the Excise Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as ‘ELO SR’).
Under Article 3(3) of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible in particular for: - the exchange of data held in the electronic register of the SEED, - the Early Warning System Excise (EWSE), - requests for verification of movements of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the Movement Verification System (MVS).
The content, scope and functions of the SEED, EWSE and ISA systems are governed by Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - system for the exchange of information on tax subjects trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national excise registers and allows tax authorities in the territory of the European Union to ascertain whether products subject to excise duty are traded by a person authorised to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union are able to obtain confirmation of the information held in that database.
In accordance with § 41 of Act No 98/2004 Z. z., s § 39 of Act No 104/2004 Z. z., s § 46 of Act No 105/2004 Z. z., s § 40 of Act No 106/2004 Z. z. and s § 39 of Act No 107/2004 Z. z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, authorised recipients and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering the tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in the SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data are automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO of Slovakia found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the audited period usually once a month, exceptionally several times a month.
SR Customs received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
The data are transferred to the SEED database in the Czech Republic from the national register in which all persons authorised to handle products subject to excise duty and issued authorisations for handling such products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international database SEED.
Requests from customs offices to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through ELO ČR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods, through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
Transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits laid down in a European Commission regulation and transport assessed as a risk by the tax authority are considered to be risky consignments.
The exchange of information takes two forms:
- information - sent when the specified limits are exceeded,
- a warning message - to be sent if the carriage of goods is assessed as risky.
When assessing the level of risk of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database to send an alert message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
If the data in the SEED database do not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR shall draw up an alert message to be sent to ELO of the Member State of the consignee of the goods.
In drawing up the reports, ELO follows the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which, among other things, determine the type and quantity of goods in the respective measurement units for the production of information and warning reports.
During the audited period ELO SR sent one warning message to ELO ČR.
In the Czech Republic, information on initiated transport of products in quantities exceeding the specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database at the time of transport approval.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates the shipment as a risk based on his own analysis, he will process the so-called warning message, which he will send to the relevant Member State through ELO ČR.
In 2005 ELO ČR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The ISA - the system for controlling the movement of goods - makes it possible, through the ISA's requests, to check the individual movements of products subject to excise duty, as well as to check the specified route of transport between the bodies mentioned in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information takes place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is used in particular in cases where the consignor accepts copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requests e.g. a refund of excise duty, and in cases where the information contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the SEED international database.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent 33 requests to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.
ELO ČR sent ELO SR 25 requests to MVS.
Customs offices in the Czech Republic most often checked the data contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantity of products received or dispatched or whether the consignor of products mentioned in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of products subject to excise duty if this fact could not be verified in the international database SEED.
The MVS applications received were forwarded in both countries to the customs offices locally responsible for the consignee or consignor of excise products.
The customs authorities examined the required data and communicated the result of the investigation to the other Member State via ELO.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the SAO-CR and the SAO-SR enabled to compare the basic legislation governing the area of excise duties in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the initiation and termination of transport of products under suspension of tax exemption between the two states, the registration of such transport and to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities within the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Comparison of legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia revealed differences:
(a) the procedure followed by tax entities and tax authorities when initiating the transport of products under a duty suspension arrangement.
Transport of products under the conditional exemption regime can be initiated by a tax entity in the Czech Republic only with the consent of the tax administrator, who authorizes the commencement of transport on condition that the transported products have been provided with a tax guarantee in the amount of the tax to which they are subject.
The commencement of the transport of products under suspension of duty in the Slovak Republic is not subject to authorisation by the tax authority.
During the audited period, the taxpayer was obliged to notify the tax authorities of the start of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
He was able to start the transport of mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax authorities.
In 2006, the Slovak Republic gradually adopted amendments to all laws on excise duties, according to which the consignor of goods under suspension of duty is obliged to send a copy of copy No.1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office competent for the consignor before the transport begins.
(b) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copies No. 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification no later than the following working day after the end of the transport.
Verified copy No 3 must be sent to the sender no later than the following working day after receipt from the tax administrator.
The consignee in Slovakia is obliged to send to the consignor of the products copy No 3 certified by the tax administrator and the consignee of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following that in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of transport of products under the conditional exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping this register is not regulated by law in the Czech Republic or Slovakia.
The customs authorities in both countries enter in the register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
For the monitoring of the movement of goods under suspension of duty between Member States of the European Union, there is currently no single electronic system allowing excise authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
According to Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring movements of excise products is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of the agreement on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of transport of products under suspension of duty initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 876 entries for mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products transported.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side a database of transport of products under suspension of duty initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3 319 entries for mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products transported.
The Czech side compared the data on transport operations listed in the register of commenced transport operations in the Czech Republic with the register of transport operations terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared the data on the transport of goods under the conditional exemption scheme started in the Slovak Republic and ended in the Czech Republic.
Comparison of data was hampered by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not uniformly reported in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to unambiguously attribute the data of individual transport operations in both registers, the accompanying documents were checked and no violations of the suspensive regime or cases of tax evasion were detected.
Based on the findings of the parallel controls, it can be concluded that the transport register can provide Member States with valuable information to improve the administration of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the movement and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow the electronic transmission of the movement document and more effective control of movements under suspension of excise duty within the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was drawn up in the Czech, English and Slovak languages.
The report was signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic.
Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Opening Word
Taxes are generally a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus their attention on this area.
An example is value added tax (VAT) fraud.
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated each year in the European Union (EU).
Already in 2005, the participants of the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
In the framework of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (SAO) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, BRH) conducted the first parallel audit in the field of VAT in 2006.
The report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not confined to a single country but is widespread throughout the EU, close cooperation between SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to address this problem.
Both SAIs therefore decided to further develop their cooperation in this area and carried out a parallel follow-up.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with SAO (follow-up)
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the auditing operation was to examine the procedure of the tax authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The auditing operation was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
It was also intended to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended to be compared with established good practice (if any).
The audited period covered the years 2006 to 2008 and, in the case of relevant connections, the preceding and following periods until the end of the audit.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The subsequent verification of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
During previous parallel inspections, suspicious cases of intra-community transactions were detected.
Some of them required further examination.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations concerning the administration of VAT.
The follow-up carried out was to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine the selected suspected cases.
The audit also focused on selected cases of high-risk intra-community transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of claims and the implementation of VAT checks on large tax entities.
During the audit of the VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors came to the following audit findings:
1. Previous inspection recommendations
• Recommendation 1: Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU
In previous parallel inspections, a comparison of the VAT registration systems in the two countries revealed differences.
As the different ways of registering pose problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registering payers within the EU.
This recommendation has been put forward at EU level.
The proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the VAT payer tax identification number database.
He also amended the common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
The SAIs expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of the document, agreed by the EU Member States in the ECOFIN framework, no longer covers the issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to see this intention as a relevant prevention tool in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly Summary Reporting
In the context of international cooperation, a previous monitoring exercise recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements to allow for a more timely verification of intra-community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the period for which recapitulative statements of intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit monthly recapitulative statements was not introduced by the deadline in accordance with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted BRH’s recommendation and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing the successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit found that our two Member States have different risk management systems which have their own strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO audited EUROCANET, which allows the exchange of information within the EU, while BRH focused on the German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected intra-community transactions
During the previous audit operation, business transactions where there were doubts about their completion or irregularities in the reporting of business transactions in tax returns or recapitulative statements by taxpayers from both countries were jointly examined.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for follow-up, which included intra-community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The inspections carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned have not been concluded by the date of completion of our previous joint inspection operation.
The subsequent audit operation verified that most of the tax procedures related to the selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany were concluded and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional adjustment of VAT or avoidance of input tax refund).
3. Check selected risk intra-community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-community transactions carried out by EU payers included in EUROCANET were selected for the audit.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risky tax payers within the EU.
Member States' participation in the scheme is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active scheme participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not participate in the EUROCANET data exchange, it was not possible to obtain any information on which suppliers with the German VAT ID were assessed as being at risk.
As part of the audit, the SAO found cases of common commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent behaviour related to VAT.
Tax authorities have limited possibilities of controlling risky transactions, especially with regard to missing traders, and mere physical verification of documents can hardly prove any fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer.
A similar situation arises for the tax authorities when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel shops.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in transport documents and also to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively participate in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools are being used to detect high-risk taxpayers, which have so far proved useful to the German tax administration.
There is a need to communicate and exchange experiences between EU Member States in this area.
The EU Council reached a political agreement on a draft regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in using EUROCANET should feed into the creation of this new VAT fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which requests for international recovery assistance are handled is the same in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and the SAO compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent inconsistencies.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAIs agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to produce, on the basis of more detailed statistics, an analysis to help Member States to strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with low recovery rates to increase their recovery rates to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Scrutiny of large tax entities
SAI analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control of large tax entities (VDS) in both countries.
In addition, they gathered information from tax authorities by means of a questionnaire on the areas that SAI considered essential for managing this issue.
It is clear from the replies received that the situation in the two countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system in place to guide the selection of risk-prone cases based on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax inspections carried out, data from balance sheets and profit and loss statements, etc.).
This ensures efficient management and analysis of VAT control in general.
A dedicated financial office for the management of VDS is planned to be established in 2012.
A similar system does not yet exist in Germany, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT controls in general.
Germany has so far focused more on selecting the individual cases in question, in particular on the basis of data from the VAT return and recapitulative statement.
The analysis of these data relies on different risk management components, which will be reinforced.
3. Progress of control action
3.1 Progress of the audit operation in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by the Division II of the State Budget Revenue Department and the territorial departments IX. Plzeň, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited bodies were: the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also “the Czech Ministry of Finance”) and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter also “FÚ”): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ Břeclav, FÚ Domažlice, FÚ Hodonín, FÚ in Hradec Králové, FÚ in Cheb, FÚ in Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ in Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Ostrava, FÚ FÚ in FÚ, FÚ FÚ, FÚ FÚ in Prague, FÚ4.
The audit conclusion of this audit operation was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 The follow-up in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Indirect Tax Inspection Service and by the staff of the designated Regional Audit Offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of a sample of cases, a number of Länder were informed of the mission of the inspection operation.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, the auditing operation took place in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hessen, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
Included were the tax files of the following tax authorities: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Tax Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, discussions took place with the tax offices of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-jih) and with the tax directorates of Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
As part of the preparation of the parallel control actions, a meeting of representatives of the two audit institutions was held in September 2008 to discuss and determine control topics.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the leaders of both SAIs signed an agreement to cooperate in the implementation of parallel controls.
At the Bonn meeting in June 2009, the audit teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the audit, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague from 2 to 4 December 2009.
The inspection teams exchanged previously collected findings and agreed on a timetable for the preparation of the joint report.
Both SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report; • screening of selected cases of intra-community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were not resolved during the previous parallel check; • screening of selected cases of intra-community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were classified as high-risk cases; • checking of the tax administration's progress in the area of international assistance in the recovery of VAT claims; • tax audits of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during a workshop in June 2010.
4. Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from previous inspection
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU.
Based on the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended modification of the conditions of VAT registration and introduction of a new rule for cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
The modified conditions should make it possible to reduce more effectively the risk of possible evasion of VAT collection.
In this context, it was found that the tax authorities in some cases did not use the right to cancel the VAT registration of taxpayers who did not comply with the obligations arising from Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as the "VAT Act").
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed an amendment to the provision introducing an obligation for tax administrators to cancel VAT registration for taxpayers in case of repeated non-submission of VAT returns.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator may cancel the registration of the tax payer “ex offo” in cases where: (a) the payer has not performed, without giving the tax administrator a reason, for a period of twelve consecutive months of performance; (b) the payer has not fulfilled his obligations under this Act; (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous audit, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the Tax Office for Prague 1 to cancel the VAT registration on 31 January of the following calendar year for so-called non-established payers who did not incur any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The FCO for Prague 1 often did not cancel the VAT registration of these payers, because the relevant provision provided for insufficient time for the cancellation of the registration.
This problem was remedied by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the non-established taxpayer in case the taxpayer has not supplied any taxable goods or services or exempt goods or services with the right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly Summary Reporting
In the context of international cooperation, a previous monitoring exercise recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements.
The Council Directive reduces the period for which recapitulative statements of intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to submit recapitulative statements in electronic form.
The payer must also submit a recapitulative statement where the services for which the place of supply is determined in accordance with Paragraph 9(1) of the VAT Code are supplied to a taxable person in another Member State and where the customer is obliged to declare and pay the tax on those services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to achieve greater reliability of VIES data This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration compares data on intra-community transactions reported in VAT returns and recapitulative statements of Czech payers automatically in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
The proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore an area of priority concern and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, inter alia, by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the eligible and the actual VAT collected in the 25 EU Member States (hereinafter "EU-25") during the period 2000-2006.
On the basis of an analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated loss of uncollected VAT for this period is between EUR 90 and 113 billion, with an average of 12% of eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18%.
In the context of international cooperation, a previous control action noted that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in every EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO audited the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-community transactions carried out by EU tax payers included in EUROCANET were selected for the audit (see chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and improving the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved by setting up the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of the responsible authorities in a way that allows fraud to be detected in its infancy.
This network should also become an important source of information for the risk assessment of intra-Community transactions at a later stage.
The ECOFIN Council already approved the creation of EUROFISC on 7 October 200812, setting out the basic principles that will guide the network.
The image of EUROFISC is the already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information EUROCANET, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of the recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report revealed the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised across the EU.
The German tax administration has set up a well-functioning tax payer registration system based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance drew the Commission's attention to this system in October 2007.
Improvements to the system shall be made on an ongoing basis.
Currently, the questionnaire data are processed electronically and will subsequently be used for the survey as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to secure the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly Summary Reporting
The Act on the transposition of EU Directives into national law was adopted on 8 April 2010.
This law contains provisions on the monthly submission of recapitulative statements of intra-community deliveries.
Those provisions entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
A joint working group composed of workers from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance was set up.
The group has developed a strategy for the automatic comparison of data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the Task Force looked at a tool designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany participates in this exchange within the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of such a platform and, following a written consultation on 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 Action Plan.
The members of the Platform are further divided into sub-groups dealing with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • influencing negotiations, • evaluation, • updating the Risk Management Guide.
Reports on the performance of these sub-groups were published in early 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and deregistration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including the database of VAT payers' tax identification numbers.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
The issue of registration and deregistration has for the time being been left to the national legislations of the EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political agreement on that draft regulation.
The aim of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States have to implement national procedures and are only required to report these to the Committee on Administrative Cooperation.
Both SAIs deplore the failure of the Commission to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts by the Commission in this direction.
Monthly Summary Reporting
In the context of international cooperation, a previous monitoring exercise recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements, allowing for more timely verification of intra-community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions reduces the period for which recapitulative statements of intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010; in Germany, it took effect on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to submit recapitulative statements monthly according to a set calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in line with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH recommendation and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO audited the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU (see chapter 4.3).
In this area, BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected intra-community transactions
In the previous audit, the implementation of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their completion, or irregularities in the way the payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT returns or recapitulative statements, was jointly examined.
The two audit institutions selected nine cases involving intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany for follow-up, the verification of which carried out by the tax administrations of both countries had not been completed during the previous joint audit operation.
1)
In the first quarter of 2005, a Czech payer purchased goods worth EUR 22 686 from a German payer.
This acquisition of goods was not declared by the Czech taxpayer in his VAT return, because the German taxpayer did not have a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that, under the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not need to have a VAT ID in order to exempt intra-Community supplies of goods from VAT.
Subsequent audit of the SAO found that on the basis of an audit carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech payer submitted a supplementary VAT return in which he declared the acquisition of goods in the stated value and at the same time claimed the right to deduct VAT in the same amount in this tax return.
2)
The Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and did not appear in his VAT return.
Upon request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administration refused to cooperate as the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax authority did not obtain evidence, it terminated the inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
Subsequent audit The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator received two spontaneous information from Germany pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in the regular VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 from the German payer.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not declared by the Czech taxpayer.
Since August 2004, this payer has not filed VAT returns, so the tax administrator has charged VAT of CZK 0 for this quarter.
On the basis of information obtained from Germany in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, in March 2007 the tax administrator invited the payer to submit a supplementary VAT return, which was not submitted by the payer.
Subsequent inspection revealed that the tax administrator carried out further tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the passenger car in question had been sold by the Czech payer to a used car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax authority issued a tax assessment notice for the December 2004 tax period, which additionally assessed VAT on the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295 379.
By order of the Regional Court, the Czech payer was dissolved with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of enforcement of the taxpayer’s attachable assets, this arrears appears to be irrecoverable.
4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005 for a total value of EUR 198 167.
The response to the request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that open tax and criminal proceedings were pending against the German entity in Germany.
During a follow-up, BRH was informed that, following the conclusion of the tax proceedings in Germany, it had been established that the German taxpayer had been involved in fraudulent activities.
The intracommunal acquisition of goods was taxed at a value of EUR 182 424 (2004) and EUR 369 690 (2005).
The SAO found out that the Czech payer was involved in carousel shops with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the verification of supplies of goods, a VAT audit was initiated with the Czech tax entity for the tax years April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the audit findings and information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT for the period May 2005 at CZK 703 031 and for the period June 2005 at CZK 726 551.
5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine from a German payer for a total value of EUR 58 000.
This German payer was supposed to deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004, but the payer B denied this acquisition of goods.
Subsequent audit of the SAO found that the payer B purchased the machine from a German company that had established an organizational unit in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not declare the acquisition of goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
The response from the German tax authority to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not make an intra-Community delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000, but delivered the goods within the Czech Republic.
BRH’s follow-up found that, following a tax audit, the intra-Community supply of the machine had been reclassified as a domestic supply of the machine and the VAT exemption had been abolished.
6)
The German taxpayer was to deliver goods worth EUR 11 600 to the Czech taxpayer in the third quarter of 2004.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator assessed the submitted additional VAT return, which wrongly indicated the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods in the specified value.
BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax authority corrected the German taxpayer's VAT return and made an additional VAT assessment of EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to a tax audit.
The recapitulative statement of the German payer has not yet been corrected because only the payer who submitted the recapitulative statement can make corrections to recapitulative statements in Germany.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as to whether the Czech taxpayer purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech taxpayer for the amount of CZK 0 after the tax procedure for the tax period of February 2005 and informed the German tax administrator that he could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
A subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for non-compliance with obligations and the Czech tax administrator sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
Subsequent inspection by BRH found that the German payer had changed his registered office and the new locally competent tax authority had revoked his VAT exemption on the supply of the car in question to the Czech payer on the basis of the inspection carried out.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the data in the recapitulative statement and has lodged an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to the VIES data, the German taxpayer supplied goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the Czech taxpayer between the third quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
A subsequent audit of the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator tried to find out the causes of the differences created by the Czech tax payer when acquiring goods in the period from the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech taxpayer has repeatedly submitted a supplementary VAT return for the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not explain the difference in the value of the purchased goods amounting to CZK 134 273 for the period from the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005, because according to the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture the commercial transactions for each quarter and therefore the tax administrator accepted the submitted additional tax returns.
9)
The German taxpayer delivered goods worth EUR 46 854 to the Czech taxpayer in the third quarter of 2004.
For the same period, the Czech payer granted an intra-Community acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of deliveries made as part of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the supply of goods of EUR 31 998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data listed in the VIES system.
Subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that the Czech payer filed a supplementary VAT return for the tax period July 2004 up to January 2007 after many urges from the tax administrator.
In that tax return, the taxpayer at the same time exercised the right to deduct VAT, thus leaving the tax liability for that tax period unchanged.
The follow-up check verified that in selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most of the tax procedures had been completed and that the tax authorities in both the Czech Republic and Germany had taken adequate measures (i.e. additionally assessed VAT or prevented the refund of input tax).
4.3 Checking selected risk intra-community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the audit in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for the detection of risk takers within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with the data on the acquirers.
Since the first quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic has been sending data to EUROCANET on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers.
Within the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for the audit.
They acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
EUROCANET captured relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States.
As the German tax administration did not participate in the EUROCANET data exchange, it was not possible to obtain any information that would help to establish whether suppliers with a German VAT ID were classified by the German tax administration as being at risk.
The audit operation revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Where applicable, tax administrations have used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• The tax authorities did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions when verifying the signal information.
The tax authorities continuously monitor such tax entities for their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT in the accounts submitted, even though they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed business relations with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• The verification of commercial transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with the tax authorities and could not be contacted.
For the most part, the locally competent tax authorities scrutinised the risky tax entities and the risky transactions listed in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax authorities have limited possibilities when examining risky transactions, in particular in relation to missing traders, and it is difficult to prove fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer simply by physically examining the documents.
Stricter VAT registration requirements and more flexible cancellation of registrations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered for the purpose of reporting fictitious deliveries of goods within the EU or for the purpose of issuing formally correct tax documents to taxpayers who unduly deduct input VAT on the basis of these documents.
In cases where there is suspicion of the involvement of tax entities in carousel transactions and other fraud and where goods are imported and exported from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help in identifying goods and irregularities in transport documents, as well as in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the final consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of EUROCANET which should be remedied by the establishment of a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Inspection results in Germany
BRH analysed the information available from the Federal Central Tax Office, which included EUROCANET data.
That information was the criterion for selecting the six files of German taxpayers for inspection.
Like some other countries, Germany has refused to participate actively in EUROCANET.
As a result, Germany has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but only receives data from EUROCANET.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement: ...in the Government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis for violating the applicable rules on tax secrecy.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such data are used in EUROCANET by other Member States. “17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has been carrying out analyses of EUROCANET data and forwarding them to the Länder tax authorities in accordance with the agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive audit information on the direct business relations of the payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relations with traders from other Member States who also have business dealings with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, the inspection in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to set up a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The Council of the EU reached a political agreement on the draft regulation, the main contribution of which lies in the establishment of EUROFISC.
Experience gained from the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the envisaged VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, the cases brought before the courts at national and European level show that a discussion between the Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions appears to be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
4.4.1 International recovery assistance in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following Directives provide for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No 252/2000 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims.
After the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal order and at the same time to amend the aforementioned Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims, was adopted.
Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28.11.2008 is a new regulation in the system for regulating international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU.
The annex to the Regulation sets out new models of requests, which are to be used from 1 January 2009, newly establishes the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the requesting authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guiding principles for the provision of international debt recovery cooperation:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always provided only on the basis of an application containing the prescribed particulars;
3. the assistance does not cover financial claims which are in the nature of a criminal sanction in the requested State;
4. the provision of international recovery assistance shall be governed by the national law of the State in which the assistance is requested;
5. foreign claims do not have priority for recovery;
6. assistance shall be provided only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has, without success, made use of all available possibilities to recover a claim under its legal system).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines three forms by which assistance takes place, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
The locally competent tax office electronically sends the request for information, the request for service or the request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance through the financial directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will provide a translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it including the annexes and send it via the CCN/CSI network to the competent tax authority of the designated state.
There are two basic requirements for recovery: the claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and not more than 5 years old.
If the above requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
On receipt of an application from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must acknowledge receipt of the application as soon as possible and within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the rejection of the request, indicating the specific provisions of the Directive on which it relies.
This notification shall be sent no later than three months after the date of the acknowledgement of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance verifies whether the application has all the elements required by law and should immediately forward the application through the Financial Directorate to the local tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator, among other things, identifies the debtor's assets, e.g. by obtaining extracts from the real estate register, checking bank accounts, verifying the registration of vehicles at the DMV, etc.
After a period of six months from the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance should communicate to the requesting authority the result of the enquiry carried out in order to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contacting tax subjects, where it is not possible to recover the claim, the applicant authority should also be informed thereof.
Any sum recovered by the tax authority shall be transferred to the applicant authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not inconceivable that the Czech tax administrator recovering foreign claims will allow it to be deferred or paid in instalments, provided that the State which requested the recovery agrees.
During the recovery period, the debtor is prescribed interest or penalty payments in accordance with Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the State which requested the recovery.
In the case of received requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not send requests to the local tax authorities to be processed in time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the context of international recovery assistance in the case of requests received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not comply with Act No. 191/2004 Coll. because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months of the date on which receipt of the application was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistics
The Czech Ministry of Finance, in accordance with the provisions of Section 13(4) of Act No. 191/2004 Coll., processes every year until 15 March statistical data for the European Commission indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or recovery sent or received in the past year and indicating the amount of the claims to which the requests relate.
On the basis of the documentation provided by all EU Member States, the European Commission prepares a report on the state of recovery for submission to the Council of the EU and the European Parliament.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data due to an error in the item of recovered receivables in 2008 by EUR 5 250 000 by indicating the incorrect value of the recovered receivable for VAT (this was a shift of the decimal point after the conversion of the receivable from Czech crowns into the value in euros).
This error was subsequently reflected in the European Commission's statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including the amounts recovered, is given in the table below.
4.4.2 International recovery assistance in Germany
The legal mandate for international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from European Community law, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Recovery Directive) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In order to make its wording more accessible and easier to understand, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76/308/EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the State Tax Collection (EC) Act of 3 May 2003.
The recovery procedure in Germany is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities in force in national jurisdiction and on the basis of the EC Act on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) lays down statutory provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
The administrative operations of the tax authorities are governed in particular by the instructions for execution and the instructions for enforcement.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with the representatives of the Länder (Supreme Tax Offices) on the principles of administrative assistance for the assessment of taxes and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general conditions for lodging claims for recovery are as follows:
• Legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of enforcement have already been exhausted.
• Claims which are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be definitive.
• No more than 5 years may elapse between the issuing of the enforcement order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. it is no longer subject to appeal) and the date on which the application is submitted.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the relevant foreign office, such as the Czech Customs Office, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The detailed procedure follows the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Receivables) of 19 January 2004.25 Currently, a working group of the federal and provincial governments is reviewing this methodological guideline in order to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
The application, including annexes, shall be submitted electronically by the tax office to the intermediate office.
That authority shall check the correctness of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it is returned to the relevant tax office.
If it meets all the requirements, it is transferred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
Subsequently, the Federal Central Tax Office will ensure the necessary communication with the competent foreign office and provide a translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and a receipt shall be sent within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check whether the formal requirements have been fulfilled.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these requests to the Intermediate Office, which forwards them to the competent tax authorities and monitors their execution.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the application takes more than 6 months to be processed, the intermediate office shall request a preliminary report to be submitted in accordance with Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94/EC.
Once the formal and factual elements of the application have been checked, the implementing services shall notify the means of recovery.
Any sums recovered shall be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of their receipt.
Statistics
