4.4.3 Recovery check, case studies
Within the framework of international cooperation, 21 applications for international assistance in the recovery of claims between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for examination.
Examination of ten selected cases revealed, among others:
1.
On 20 October 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany a request for recovery of a VAT claim for the years 2004 and 2005 for a total amount of EUR 3 883, i.e. CZK 109 820, from a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax authority until 26 February 2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire enforced debt by mortgage, a payment plan with instalments of at least CZK 2,000 per month was agreed with the Czech tax entity.
On 31 August 2009, information was sent to the German tax administration on the state of recovery of the claim, with the claim being partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49 600 as of 25 August 2009.
This sum was sent to Germany and a further instalment of CZK 3 000 was sent to Germany on 28 August 2009.
2.
On 7 January 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech taxpayer who owed EUR 180 869, i.e. CZK 4 434 915, in Germany in respect of VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the tax administrator until 27 November 2008.
By examining the ownership of bank accounts, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movable property, the tax administrator found that the debtor does not own any executable property.
Furthermore, the on-the-spot investigation revealed that the debtor had not stayed at his permanent address for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 April 2009 and on 16 April 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
On 21 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany a request for recovery concerning tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3 139, i.e. CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim to the tax administrator on 6 August 2008, although on 18 February 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax authorities that the request for recovery had been processed by the payment of the claim by a Czech taxpayer in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also recovered in the course of recovery in the Czech Republic and transferred to Germany on 27 October 2008.
Due to the long time-limits within which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorised tax administrators, the claim was paid twice in this case - by the entity itself in Germany and by the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been set off against the claim of a further request for recovery of EUR 6 649 to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance registers only a request for recovery of the claim in the amount of EUR 3 139 with this company, the request for recovery of the claim in the amount of EUR 6 649 does not appear in the register of the Czech Ministry of Finance with this company.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech taxpayer who owed EUR 39 957, i.e. CZK 956 654, in respect of income tax and VAT and accessories in Germany.
On 19 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
On 1 June 2009, a procedure for the recovery of the claim was initiated, execution was ordered on the attachment of the claim to accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and on the deduction from wages (the deduction amounted to CZK 7 000).
During negotiations with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax authority found that the taxpayer had in the past been willing to repay EUR 250 per month, which was not accepted by the German tax authority.
The taxpayer promised to discuss the application with the German tax authorities in order to obtain a change in the amount of its claim.
Enforcement of the claim continued during the audit operation of the SAO.
5.
On 19 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning a Czech taxpayer who owed a total of EUR 113 444, i.e. CZK 3 116 304, in income tax for 2005 and in turnover tax for 2003-2007 and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the Tax Office for Prague 1, which is in charge of tax administration for non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14 November 2008, because it was not possible to determine the tax administrator locally on the basis of the address given to the tax entity.
During the investigation, the FÚ was informed that the debtor had an income of EUR 4 704 on 19 September 2008; however, the FÚ could no longer issue an execution order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance did not transmit the request for recovery until after that date.
On 26 January 2009, the Czech tax administrator initiated the enforcement of the claim and issued an execution order to establish the claim against the debtor's funds in accounts opened with banks and savings and credit cooperatives.
Enforcement of the claim continued during the audit operation of the SAO.
6.
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in the recovery of the VAT claim and the costs of the proceedings totalling CZK 146 223 742 on 3 October 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax administration until 13.5.2008.
On 8 September 2008, the German tax authority transferred to the Czech authorities via the Bundesbank the amount obtained from the seizure of funds in the debtor's account in the amount of EUR 17 700, i.e. CZK 439 226.
An error in the recalculation of the amount recovered was detected during the verification of the volume of recoveries.
The amount of CZK 146 223 742 recovered was converted at EUR 1 = CZK 25,065, erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct conversion of the amount recovered amounts to EUR 5 833 781,83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover a tax arrears from a Czech taxpayer who owed CZK 1 970 632, or EUR 79 847, in respect of VAT and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax administration until 10.11.2008.
On 4 February 2009, the German tax authority requested the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant decrease in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and in particular in the first half of 2009 and the related liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to cover the arrears: EUR 4 600 on 8.4.2009, EUR 3 000 on 6.5.2009 and EUR 2 500 on 16.6.2009.
These payments were sent to the account of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax authorities agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500 by 30 June 2009.
8.
The request for recovery totalling EUR 398 653, i.e. CZK 9 832 779, including the real estate transfer tax claim, was received from the Czech tax administrator at the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 May 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2 October 2008.
On 3 April 2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a communication from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax authorities justified the refund on the grounds that the tax on the transfer of immovable property was not a tax within the meaning of Article 2(e), (f), (g) or (h) of Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
The German tax authorities also stated that Article 2(g) concerns claims relating to income tax and wealth tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55/EC applies to taxes on income and capital listed in Article 1(3) in conjunction with Article 4 of Council Directive 77/799/EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed to draw up and submit a new request for recovery, excluding arrears of real estate transfer tax amounting to CZK 61 759 and including arrears of VAT, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be sent again to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has received a new request from the Czech tax administrator for the recovery of tax arrears concerning the same taxpayer who owes CZK 7,079,735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6 February 2006, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech taxpayer who owed CZK 3 445 782, i.e. EUR 123 328, in personal income tax and VAT.
Of this amount, VAT accounted for CZK 1 133 967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the German tax administration until 18 April 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax administrator the reply of the German tax administration dated 9 July 2007 until 11 November 2008.
The reply stated that the German tax authorities had issued an execution order on 11 June 2007 against a bank account, but that the bank had stated that it had no business relations with the taxpayer.
As a result, the German tax authorities considered the application to be completed.
10.
On 26 September 2005, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1 296 845, or EUR 43 591.
The request from the Czech tax administrator was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10 October 2005.
On 15 December 2005, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the German tax administration.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax administrator executed execution on the debtor's funds in bank accounts and withholding from wages and established a mortgage on the immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authorities on 16 March 2005.
The reply to the request for information received by the Czech tax authority on 16 September 2005 showed that the Czech taxpayer was resident in Germany and had an income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activities.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20.4.2006, but forwarded it to the Czech tax authority only on 12.2.2008.
The reply stated that no recovery proceedings could be initiated in Germany because of the debtor's insolvency - no assets had been identified and his non-business income was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
The German tax authorities therefore considered the request for recovery to be completed.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which requests for international recovery assistance are handled is the same in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and the SAO compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay particular attention to the management of their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of statistical discrepancies had decreased, although the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important to renegotiate statistical issues at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent discrepancies, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics should show the annual number of claims as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amounts recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by Member States, as this can assist Member States in assessing their own effectiveness in fighting VAT fraud.
The fact that recovery rates can be calculated on a Member State-by-Member basis is considered useful by both SAIs for Member States with lower recovery rates to step up their efforts and try to improve recovery rates to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery on time to the local tax authorities.
A similar situation was found for requests for international assistance received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not comply with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Claims, because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months from the date of the acknowledgement of receipt of the application.
4.5 Scrutiny of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons that were established or established for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax period stated in the personal/corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The classification of the taxpayer as a VDS took place after the submission of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time for 2003.
A taxpayer ceases to be classified as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax years from the end of the period in which he submitted the tax return on the basis of which he was classified as a VDS, his net turnover for the tax year falls below that threshold.
A taxpayer may not be removed from the VDS register without a tax inspection of at least one tax per tax year.
All VDS were checked at a minimum five-year frequency until the end of 2009.
From 2010 onwards, a written assessment of the taxpayer must be carried out at least every 2 years and the subsequent procedure chosen must eliminate the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The audit of the FC is focused on at least one type of tax; The tax administrator usually chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS were audited by the specialised inspection departments, which are set up in 13 FUs in total, or by the staff of the inspection departments of the locally competent FUs.
The Specialised Controls Unit shall carry out tax audits within the remit set by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific business lines;
• entities where it is technically and time-consuming to carry out a tax audit;
• entities with a diversified territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• Entities linked in chains and networks suspected of large-scale tax evasion and unjustified lure of excess deductions.
The number of tax inspections carried out by the specialised control units of the FC and the results of these inspections are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., on Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists in the establishment of a specialised Tax Office with nationwide competence for selected tax entities (i.a. for legal entities established for business purposes that have achieved a turnover of more than CZK 2 billion).
4.5.2 Scrutiny of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls for large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • German Fiscal Code (AO), • Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on control are laid down in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax Inspection on the Spot. In particular, those articles lay down the rules governing the admissibility of an on-the-spot tax inspection (i.e. at the premises of the undertaking), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules governing the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the inspection notice, the principles of the inspection, the obligation for the taxpayer to cooperate and the prerequisites for carrying out the final consultation and communication of the inspection report.
Tax inspections on the spot are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Governance Act Under Article 5.1(1) in conjunction with Article 19 of the Law, participation in tax on-the-spot checks by the tax authorities is compulsory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the nature and extent of the involvement of the Federal Central Tax Office in tax inspections on the spot.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it collects be inspected within a period to be determined by it.
In such a case, it may publish rules on the conduct and content of the inspection at the premises of those companies.
Rules on fiscal controls Pursuant to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the regulations on tax inspections (German abbreviation BpO 2000) were approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper house of the German Parliament in which the governments of the Länder are represented).
These administrative rules apply to on-the-spot checks carried out by the Land tax authorities and the Federal Central Tax Office.
Enterprises are classified by size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BPO 2000.
Large undertakings are subject to ex post control (Article 4.2 of the BPO).
Under Article 33.1 of the BpO 2000, any informed tax authority must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BpO 2000.
Methodological guidance
In addition to the above, the additional methodology for the tax administration is set out in the following guidelines:
• Uniform manual for special VAT controls in Germany;
• a USLO manual setting out the methodology for the use of data on intra-community business relationships maintained in the VIES system;
• a ZAUBER manual setting out the methodology for the use of the ZAUBER database;
• working aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits depending on the type of business.
Data are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the following three years.
The number of companies to be inspected - not just large companies - must be determined at regular inspection intervals.
As a general rule, inspections of large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Controls are usually announced, including VAT controls.
This means that, in the course of the inspection, checks are carried out definitively, in particular on income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT inspections may be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisation of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by the controls usually varies between three and five years.
The BpO 2000 foresees a control period of three years.
All taxes of the company are subject to verification.
4.5.3 Control management of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of performed VDS checks, but focused on management issues in order to gain an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VDS VAT controls.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax authorities on the areas they considered essential for managing this issue.
• What statistical records and analyses concerning the VAT control of VDS are available to the tax administration management?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or records of the extent to which the fight against VAT fraud is distinguished from VAT control in general?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such resolution with the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between a control designed to combat VAT fraud and a general VAT control.
• Are there any statistics or records of the timeliness of VAT controls (linked to the time period of the audited transactions)?
Czech Republic: The records of the timeliness of the questioning with relevance for intra-Community acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information recorded in the ADIS also includes data such as how long the questioning took.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at Federal level for tax inspectors only contain information on the average time of the last inspection (year information).
This figure does not provide an overview of selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; They also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, the statistics produced at federal level for the special VAT control units do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
• Are there any statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenue generated, disaggregated e.g. according to the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the taxpayer has unduly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
iii. additional collection of the tax revenue (payment of the additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech Tax Administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the volumes of tax additionally assessed broken down by type of tax, by the number of tax entities audited and by the number of tax periods audited.
Other tax procedures (local investigations, complaints procedures) are followed in the same way.
Time data and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded as a separate task.
Statistics on general debts broken down by type of tax are also kept, but not by declared tax or tax established by the tax authorities.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not distinguish between these criteria.
Moreover, most of the tax administrations visited do not distinguish these differences.
• Are there control areas that generate high additional revenue?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to collect tax payers for verification based on criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of the ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach between the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must record the increased tax (VAT) they have imposed if it exceeds a certain amount.
In such a case, it must specify, for example, the nature of the increase in tax liability assessed.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDSs claim an undue right to deduct input tax in respect of supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to Section 72(1) of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to Section 75(3) of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73(1) of the VAT Act;
- The VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Section 21(1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It has been noted that there are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at Federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
Findings concerning VAT are not separately registered by the Länder if they result from the VDS tax inspections.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder have to enter the increased tax (VAT) liability they have imposed if it exceeds a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration carry out analyses of the areas of control that generate a high ‘return’ and draw the consequences for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching nationwide audits focused on risky commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
The uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide data on audit areas that generate high ‘returns’.
There are different views on the process of analysis as well as on the management of cases in terms of materiality.
Some regional tax offices provide special information, but its use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
The differences in the replies of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a lot of data from the tax inspections carried out, as well as data from the financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the establishment of a specialised financial office for the management of VDS is planned in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows that it is more difficult to carry out those tasks in a similar manner.
However, Germany's philosophy places more emphasis on the selection of individual cases on the basis of the data from the submitted tax returns.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
Expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT on the basis of adequate reference notes.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help to reduce VAT revenue shortfalls.
As a result, the revenue from VAT collection will increase and the risk detection rate for unreliable entrepreneurs will improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of both SAIs on parallel controls of the VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
The two SAIs have become better acquainted with each other's systems in the following areas: • intra-community transactions; • VAT risk management, in particular as regards the selection of risk-prone transactions; • VAT recovery assistance; and • VAT control of large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud detection strategies as well as differences in the above mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany have been revealed.
The audit findings were compared and used to identify best practices.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to launch a debate on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation between the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6. Communiqué
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Closing date: June 2010.
